# kiso-run/core — v0.9 Development Plan

## Problem Statement

Kiso now has broad test coverage across unit, bash, integration, Docker,
live, functional, and plugin suites, but the remaining risk is no longer
"untested modules". The risk is that several runtime guarantees explicitly
promised by the docs are still verified only indirectly, only at unit level,
or only through weak smoke oracles — and that the suite itself has grown
large enough to slow contributors down without delivering proportional
confidence.

v0.9 should therefore focus on **confidence alignment**: the highest-risk
contracts in startup recovery, worker concurrency, connector protocol,
workspace file handoff, plugin lifecycle, and secret containment need
tests at the level where they can actually fail in production. In parallel,
the suite needs a one-time investment in performance and a deliberate
audit/prune so future tests build on a fast, lean baseline.

## Current Test Topology

Kiso already has a strong suite pyramid:

- **Unit**: dominant layer; strong coverage for planner/worker helpers, CLI,
  storage, security, webhook logic, tool manifests, and many regressions.
- **Bash**: good coverage for `install.sh` and `kiso-host.sh`.
- **Integration**: currently thin but valuable; mocked LLM + real ASGI app,
  ideal for API/runtime protocol guarantees.
- **Docker**: focused isolation/sandbox checks.
- **Live**: verifies role compliance and selected runtime semantics with real
  LLMs, but should stay targeted because it is slow and provider-fragile.
- **Functional**: real end-to-end user scenarios; strongest for observable
  file/tool/runtime behavior, but must avoid weak wording-only assertions.
- **Plugin / interactive / destructive**: useful as smoke and acceptance,
  but not substitutes for deterministic runtime tests.

The suite today: **104 test files, ~66k lines, no parallelization**, all
integration fixtures function-scoped. The default suite is fast enough but
adding 17+ new milestones on top of the current baseline would compound an
already significant cost.

## Problems

### P1 — Runtime guarantees are documented more strongly than they are tested

Docs in `flow.md`, `connectors.md`, and `tools.md` promise behavior such as
startup message recovery, atomic worker spawn, polling fallback, `uploads/`
handoff, and scoped ephemeral secrets. Some of these are covered only by
unit tests on helpers or store functions, not by tests that exercise the
actual runtime seams where they could break.

### P2 — Integration tests underuse their best role

The integration layer is the correct place to validate ASGI routes,
worker spawning, queueing, webhook behavior, and connector protocol with
mocked LLMs and deterministic assertions. Today it covers basic request/flow
cases, but not several of the concurrency and recovery contracts that most
need a host-level, non-LLM oracle.

### P3 — Plugin and connector lifecycle confidence is split across weak layers

Tools/connectors have good unit coverage for manifest validation and CLI
behavior, and plugin smoke tests validate clone/build/test. But update,
refresh, daemon lifecycle, restart/backoff behavior, and connector
protocol recovery are not yet covered as end-to-end operational flows.

### P4 — File and secret boundaries need stronger end-to-end evidence

Kiso's value proposition depends on correct movement of files and secrets
across plans and tools: `uploads/`, `pub/`, `plan_outputs`, scoped
`session_secrets`, and published URLs. Many helper-level tests exist, but
the highest-risk boundary failures are "everything looked valid in unit
tests, but the real runtime handed the wrong path, leaked a secret, or
forced a re-download".

### P5 — Some suites still use weaker oracles than the runtime now supports

The structured-runtime redesign introduced stronger state surfaces:
normalized plan/task contracts, canonical task results, plan/task DB rows,
published artifact URLs, worker/process state, and classified replan
behavior. New tests in v0.9 should prefer these oracles over wording-based
assertions whenever possible.

### P6 — Long-tail surfaces are covered unevenly or only as TODOs

Negative install paths for nonexistent plugins are explicitly TODO in
`docs/testing-live.md`, and the registry matrix beyond the default preset
trio (browser/ocr/aider) is partial. These are less urgent than runtime
recovery, but they should still be captured in the plan so they do not
remain perpetual TODOs.

### P7 — Cross-layer adversarial paths rely on layered defenses, not isolated filters

Kiso's docs and architecture explicitly rely on layered defenses
(paraphraser, reviewer, replan classification, sanitization). Those layers
are valuable only if the important cross-layer handoffs are tested as a
system, not only as isolated helper behavior. Today the handoffs themselves
have no end-to-end tests.

### P8 — The suite is large, function-scoped, and unparallelized

104 files, 66k lines, no `pytest-xdist`, all integration fixtures
function-scoped. Adding 17+ milestones on top of the current baseline would
make local TDD painful and CI slower. The single highest-leverage change
v0.9 can make is paying the perf debt once, so the new tests inherit the
speedup instead of compounding the slowness.

### P9 — Accumulated test redundancy in the largest unit modules

`tests/test_worker.py` has 613 tests in 13.5k lines and `tests/test_brain.py`
825 tests in 10.5k lines — sizes that almost certainly contain duplicate
scenarios accumulated over many milestones. v0.9 should end with a
deliberate audit pass — not a blind delete, but a structured review that
proposes specific cuts/merges for human approval.

## Test Design Principles For v0.9

1. **Test the guarantee at the seam where it can fail.**
   Startup recovery belongs in integration/runtime startup tests, not only
   store tests. Connector polling fallback belongs in integration protocol
   tests, not only in connector docs.
2. **Prefer deterministic host-level assertions over live LLM assertions.**
   Use integration for worker/process/protocol guarantees. Use live or
   functional only when the property depends on actual model behavior.
3. **Use observable runtime state as the oracle.**
   Prefer queue state, worker count, task rows, webhook deliveries, file
   existence, published URLs, and tool stdin payloads over output prose.
4. **Audit before adding.**
   Existing suites already cover meaningful pieces (see "Items intentionally
   NOT in v0.9" at the end). Each milestone that touches their territory
   was checked against the actual code before being added to this plan.
5. **Build durable harnesses once, reuse them everywhere.**
   M1268 exists specifically so subsequent milestones do not each
   reinvent fake tools, fake connectors, webhook collectors, or
   spawn-race fixtures.
6. **Pay perf debt before adding cost.**
   M1267 must land before any new test milestone, so the additions
   inherit xdist parallelism and tmpfs storage.
7. **Keep smoke tests smoke-sized.**
   Plugin clone/build tests and external-service checks are useful, but do
   not upgrade them into blocking semantic coverage unless the oracle is
   robust against external drift.

## Phase 0 — Foundations: performance and harness (M1267-M1268)

### M1267 — Test suite performance baseline, xdist, and tmpfs ✅

**Problem:** P8.

**Files:** `pyproject.toml`, `tests/conftest.py`,
`tests/integration/conftest.py`, `tests/functional/conftest.py`,
`utils/run_tests.sh`, `tests/README.md`.

**Verified facts that shape this milestone:**
- `kiso/store/setup.py::init_db(db_path: Path)` opens an aiosqlite
  connection in WAL journal mode and runs ALTER TABLE migrations.
  In-memory SQLite (`:memory:`) is **not** a drop-in: WAL is degenerate
  for in-memory databases, and the test suite uses `tmp_path` heavily.
  The realistic fast-storage path is **tmpfs**, which is a real
  filesystem and supports WAL and ALTER TABLE without changes.
- `kiso/main.py` has module-level mutable state: `_workers` (dict at
  line 302), `_worker_phases` (dict at line 305), `_rate_limiter`
  (singleton at line 113). xdist isolates per-subprocess so cross-worker
  state is fine, but tests within the same xdist worker share these
  dicts. The cleanup pattern from `tests/test_inflight.py::_cleanup_worker`
  (pop `_workers[session]` and `_worker_phases[session]`, cancel the
  task) is the correct shape — promote it into a shared fixture.
- All fixtures in `tests/integration/conftest.py:175-272` are
  function-scoped. Promoting app/runtime init to session/module scope
  is the largest single fixture-level win.

**Change:**

1. **Baseline first.** Run the unit suite with `pytest --durations=20`
   and record the top-20 slowest tests and total wall time. Same for
   integration. Commit the baseline numbers in `tests/README.md` so
   subsequent gains are measurable.
2. **Add `pytest-xdist`** as a dev dependency and wire `-n auto` into
   `utils/run_tests.sh` for the unit and integration tiers. Add a
   shared autouse fixture (in `tests/conftest.py`) that pops any
   leftover entries from `kiso.main._workers` / `_worker_phases` after
   each test, modeled on `tests/test_inflight.py::_cleanup_worker`.
   Where shared state cannot be cleaned, use `--dist=loadfile` so
   tests in the same file run on the same worker.
3. **tmpfs for the temp tree.** Wire
   `pytest --basetemp=/dev/shm/pytest-kiso` into `utils/run_tests.sh`
   for the unit and integration tiers (with a Linux-only guard and a
   filesystem fallback for macOS contributors). This gives WAL-friendly
   storage at RAM speed without touching `init_db` or any test code.
4. **Promote function-scoped fixtures to session/module scope where
   safe.** Inspection target: `tests/integration/conftest.py:175-272`.
   Candidates for promotion: app/runtime initialization, role prompt
   loading (`kiso/roles/*.md`), planner module assembly cache. Reset
   per-test data via small helpers, not by re-initializing the whole
   stack.
5. **Cache role prompt loading.** `kiso/roles/*.md` are read from disk;
   the planner module assembler (`kiso/brain/planner.py`) reassembles
   modules with a budget cap. Add a session-scoped fixture or
   `functools.lru_cache` so each test does not re-pay this cost.
6. **Tighten the default tier.** No test in the default suite (no
   flags) should take >1s. Mark anything slower with the appropriate
   opt-in marker (`functional`, `integration`, `extended`) and verify
   `pytest_collection_modifyitems` in `tests/conftest.py` handles them.
7. Re-run baselines, record before/after numbers in `tests/README.md`,
   and document the chosen parallelization strategy so future tests
   stay compatible.

**Why:** Adding 17 more milestones on top of an unparallelized 66k-line
suite makes local TDD painful. Doing this first means every Phase 1-7
addition inherits the speedup.

**Test:** Self-evident — measure wall time before and after, on the
same machine, with the same flags. Document the delta.

**Outcome (2026-04-08):**
- Unit tier: **137s → 42s (3.2x)** with `pytest-xdist -n auto` +
  `--basetemp=/dev/shm/...`. 4045 tests still passing, zero state
  isolation issues.
- Integration tier: **10s → 6s (1.8x)** with the same flags.
- Wired into `utils/run_tests.sh` for tier 1 (unit) and tier 3
  (integration), with a Linux-only guard on tmpfs and a graceful
  fallback to default basetemp on macOS.
- Baseline + delta documented in `tests/README.md`.

**Deferred (intentional, with reasons):**
- *Promote integration fixtures to session/module scope* — xdist
  already delivered 3.2x. Promoting `kiso_client` and friends is
  risky because they all initialize the global `app` state via
  `_init_app_state(app, config, db)`; the gain would be marginal and
  the regression risk is real. Defer to a future perf cycle if the
  base time drifts back up.
- *Cache role prompt loading* — verified already cached at module
  level via `kiso/brain/prompts.py:11` `_prompt_cache` dict. No work
  needed.
- *Tighten default tier so no test takes >1s* — the slowest tests
  (`TestInitKisoDirs` 5-6s each, 7 tests) do real filesystem ops with
  PRAGMA WAL. Forcing them under 1s requires substantial test
  refactor and is out of scope for a perf-only milestone. The xdist
  parallelism already addresses the wall-clock pain.
- *Autouse cleanup for `_workers`/`_worker_phases`* — not needed
  because xdist subprocess isolation handles cross-worker, and
  same-worker test ordering already works (no xdist failures
  observed). M1268 may add this as a defensive net for the new
  spawn-race tests.

### M1268 — Test harness foundations and existing-coverage audit ✅

**Problem:** P1, P2, P3, P4, P5.

**Files:** `tests/integration/conftest.py`, new
`tests/integration/_harness/` package (or equivalent helpers module),
`tests/README.md` for the audit map.

**Change:**

1. Build the reusable fixtures every Phase 1-2 milestone needs:
   - **Fake tool package** that prints, in a structured way, the stdin
     payload it received, the env vars it can see, and any
     `session_secrets` keys passed in. Must be installable as a real
     Kiso tool from a temporary directory.
   - **Fake connector directory** with controllable lifecycle: a launcher
     that can be told to exit cleanly, crash, hang, or run stably so the
     supervisor lifecycle tests have a deterministic counterpart.
   - **Webhook collector/dropper** with attempt counting, configurable
     failure modes (drop N then succeed, always 500, partial body), and
     a simple replay buffer for assertions.
   - **Spawn-race barrier**: an `asyncio.Event` based fixture that can be
     monkeypatched into `kiso.main._ensure_worker` so concurrency tests
     can widen the race window deterministically. Reuse the
     `_make_busy_worker` pattern from `tests/test_inflight.py` for the
     "worker already exists" half of the harness.
   - **Drain helper** that waits for worker idle + plan/task settle.
2. Produce a short audit table in `tests/README.md` mapping the surfaces
   v0.9 is going to touch to the test files that already cover them:
   webhook delivery → `test_webhook.py:209-341`; supervisor lifecycle →
   `test_supervisor.py` (251 lines); startup recovery helpers →
   `test_startup_recovery.py` (7 tests); in-flight message routing →
   `test_inflight.py` (8 tests); cancel route and drain →
   `test_cancel.py` (10 tests); LLM stall/fallback → `test_brain.py`
   (8+ tests including `test_stall_uses_fallback_model`,
   `test_timeout_uses_fallback_model`,
   `test_retry_llm_with_validation_fallback`); schema migrations →
   `test_store.py:2069+`; cron CRUD/scheduler → `test_cron.py` and
   `test_cron_api.py`; admin/runtime API → `test_admin.py` (11 tests
   for /admin/reload-env), `test_health.py` (5 tests),
   `test_published.py` (~15 tests for /pub/{token}/{filename}),
   `test_stats.py`. Subsequent milestones must read this table before
   writing new tests.
3. Document the harness in a top-of-file docstring inside
   `tests/integration/conftest.py`.

**Why:** Without this, every Phase 1 and Phase 2 milestone re-invents
the same fixtures and the audit step gets skipped. With this, "write
the new test" becomes a 1-function exercise and the rest of v0.9 stops
duplicating work that already exists in older suites.

**Test:** Self-test by porting at least one existing integration test
to the new harness to prove the fixtures actually work as intended.

**Outcome (2026-04-08):**
- Extended `WebhookCollector` with configurable `failure_mode`
  (`ok` / `drop_n` / `always_500` / `always_drop`) and `attempts_log`
  for exact attempt-count assertions. `mock_deliver_webhook` rewired
  to consult collector failure mode. Existing 25 integration tests
  still pass (default mode preserves behavior).
- New `fake_tool` fixture creates a Kiso tool package whose `tool.py`
  echoes stdin keys, declared session_secrets, and visible env vars.
  Ready for M1273 secret containment tests.
- New `fake_connector_dir` fixture creates a connector directory with
  a launcher that supports `clean_exit` / `crash` / `hang` / `stable` /
  `crash_after` modes via `FAKE_CONNECTOR_MODE` env var. Ready for
  M1276 supervisor lifecycle tests.
- `wait_for_worker_idle` drain helper already existed; documented in
  the harness docstring section.
- Audit table added to `tests/README.md` mapping every runtime surface
  v0.9 touches to its existing coverage (webhook, supervisor, startup
  recovery, inflight, cancel, LLM fallback, migrations, cron, all
  admin/runtime API routes).

**Deferred (intentional, with reasons):**
- *Spawn-race barrier fixture* — verified that
  `kiso.main._ensure_worker` (kiso/main.py:325-350) is **synchronous**
  with the explicit guarantee "Atomic: no await between checking and
  creating". The atomicity is structural (single-threaded asyncio
  semantics), not lock-based, so there is no race window to widen.
  M1270 will test concurrent `/msg` POSTs at the HTTP layer and
  assert exactly-one-worker without needing this fixture.

## Phase 1 — Runtime recovery and concurrency seams (M1269-M1271)

### M1269 — Startup recovery end-to-end ✅

**Problem:** P1, P2.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_runtime_recovery.py` — new module;
`tests/integration/conftest.py` for any additional bootstrap helpers;
keep `tests/test_startup_recovery.py` as the store-level layer.

**Change:**

1. Add integration tests that exercise `_startup_recovery()` from
   `kiso/main.py:504` against a real app/runtime, not just the store
   helpers (which `tests/test_startup_recovery.py` already covers with
   7 tests).
2. Seed trusted `processed=0` messages across one and multiple sessions
   (including messages with `source="cron"` so cron-recovery is
   covered alongside user messages — both go through the same DB row),
   initialize the app, run startup recovery, and assert:
   - stale running plans/tasks are marked failed
   - trusted unprocessed messages are re-enqueued
   - workers actually process them through to completion
   - final webhook deliveries (collected via M1268 collector) appear
   - messages are not processed twice on repeated startup recovery calls
3. Add one queue-pressure case: queue full during startup recovery
   should leave the message unprocessed in DB for the next restart.

**Why:** The docs explicitly promise crash recovery on startup. Today
the store helpers are covered, but the actual recovery pipeline is not
proven at the runtime level where worker creation and queueing occur.

**Test:** New integration module with deterministic DB + webhook
assertions, all powered by M1268 fixtures.

### M1270 — Same-session worker spawn atomicity (covers /msg and cron) ✅

**Problem:** P1, P2.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_runtime_concurrency.py` — new
module; uses the M1268 spawn-race barrier.

**Verified facts that shape this milestone:**
- `kiso/main.py:472` shows the cron scheduler calls
  `queue = _ensure_worker(session, db, config)` — the **same** function
  that the `/msg` route uses to spawn workers. So cron-fired jobs and
  user `/msg` requests share the spawn check, and racing them on the
  same session is one race surface, not two.
- `tests/test_inflight.py` covers the **opposite** case: a `/msg`
  arriving when a worker is **already busy** (in-flight classification:
  stop / independent / update / conflict). It uses `_make_busy_worker`
  to pre-create the worker. The boundary with this milestone must be
  stated in the new module's top docstring so future contributors do
  not duplicate either side.
- One subtle gap: cron pushes via `queue.put(msg_payload)` directly
  (`kiso/main.py:473`), so a cron job firing while a worker is busy
  **bypasses** inflight classification entirely. Whether that is a bug
  or by-design is a design question, not a test gap — the milestone
  documents the current behavior with one regression test and flags
  the question for product review, it does not change behavior.

**Change:**

1. Fire multiple `POST /msg` requests concurrently against the same
   session.
2. Use the M1268 spawn-race barrier (an `asyncio.Event` monkeypatched
   into `_ensure_worker`) to widen the race window deterministically.
3. Assert:
   - exactly one worker is created for that session
   - every message is processed exactly once
   - no duplicate tasks or duplicate webhook deliveries are emitted
   - session queue order stays coherent
4. Add a cross-session control test showing concurrent posts to
   different sessions create independent workers as expected.
5. **Cron + /msg interleave test**: drive a cron-fired enqueue and a
   concurrent `/msg` against the same session, and assert the spawn
   check still emits exactly one worker.
6. **Cron + busy worker regression**: with a busy worker already
   present, cron-enqueue a message and assert it lands in the queue
   without invoking inflight classification (current behavior). Add a
   `# DESIGN NOTE:` comment explaining this is the bypass surface and
   that any future change to it must update this test.

**Why:** `flow.md` treats atomic check-and-spawn as a hard runtime
guarantee. This is exactly the kind of race that can pass unit tests
and still fail in production if the runtime seam drifts.

**Test:** Integration-only, mocked LLM, strong counts/oracles.

### M1271 — Webhook integration retry and connector polling fallback ✅

**Problem:** P1, P2, P3.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_connector_protocol.py` — extend the
existing 5-test module; reuse webhook collector/dropper from M1268.

**Change:**

1. **One** end-to-end retry test: a `/msg` flow where the first
   delivery attempts fail (configured via the M1268 dropper) and a
   later retry succeeds. Assert attempt count and a single final
   delivered payload. Note that `tests/test_webhook.py:209-341` already
   covers `deliver_webhook` retry/backoff at unit level — this
   milestone only adds the route-level proof, not duplicate retry
   coverage.
2. Polling fallback test:
   - session has a webhook configured to drop delivery
   - fake connector posts `/msg`
   - no callback arrives
   - fake connector polls `GET /status/{session}?after={last_task_id}`
   - missed response is recovered through the `after=` cursor
   - the `after=` cursor is implemented in `kiso/api/sessions.py`
3. `after=` cursor correctness test: only new tasks past the cursor
   are returned, not the full historical status payload.

**Why:** The connector docs call polling fallback a protocol
requirement. Today the suite proves `/status` works, but not the
recovery behavior that connector authors are required to depend on.

**Test:** Integration tests with deterministic webhook collector/dropper.

## Phase 2 — File, artifact, and secret boundaries (M1272-M1274)

### M1272 — `uploads/` attachment handoff end-to-end ✅

**Problem:** P1, P4.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_workspace_handoff.py` — new module.

**Change:**

1. Write a file into `sessions/{session}/uploads/`, then process a
   message whose task/plan reads that file from the workspace.
2. Drive a deterministic mocked-plan path first: pre-shape an exec or
   tool task that consumes `uploads/foo.txt`.
3. Add one acceptance-level scenario that proves the planner/runtime
   can use an uploaded local file without inventing
   download/curl/wget steps when the file is already present locally.
4. Assert the final task uses local workspace paths and the resulting
   output comes from the uploaded file content.

**Why:** `uploads/` is a declared platform contract for connectors.
The helper-level behavior is tested, but the real handoff is not.

**Test:** Integration first; one acceptance scenario only if the
oracle is file/path behavior rather than model wording.

### M1273 — Scoped `session_secrets` containment end-to-end ✅

**Problem:** P1, P4.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_secret_boundaries.py` — new module;
fake tool fixture comes from M1268.

**Change:**

1. Use the M1268 fake tool that prints stdin payload keys, declared
   `session_secrets`, and visible env vars.
2. Drive the runtime with a mix of declared and undeclared secrets and
   assert:
   - the tool receives only declared `session_secrets`
   - undeclared secrets are absent from stdin
   - secrets are not promoted into env vars
   - task output, webhook payloads, and audit-facing strings are
     sanitized
3. Failure-path case: a tool that echoes a secret value back. Confirm
   the stored/delivered output is redacted.

**Why:** Kiso's secret model is security-sensitive. Helper coverage
exists, but the full runtime path from planner/worker memory to tool
subprocess and back to user-visible output is not yet pinned down.

**Test:** Deterministic integration tests using the M1268 fake tool.

### M1274 — Published file provenance and local-file routing ✅

**Problem:** P4, P5.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_cross_plan_files.py` (extend), and
one deterministic test in `tests/integration/test_workspace_handoff.py`
if helpful.

**Change:**

1. Strengthen existing cross-plan file tests so the oracle is not only
   "a file exists", but also:
   - planner/runtime use `pub/...` local paths when appropriate
   - no redundant network fetch is introduced
   - published URL corresponds to the file actually produced in-session
2. Add one deterministic test where an already-published file is
   reused in a later plan and the runtime does not duplicate or
   re-download it.
3. Keep assertions on file identity, plan/task rows, and produced URL
   shape — not on natural-language explanation text.

**Why:** This is where artifact identity can silently regress. The
runtime now has better state surfaces, so the tests should use them.

**Test:** Mostly functional plus one deterministic integration case.

## Phase 3 — Plan validation determinism (M1275)

### M1275 — Circular replan deterministic stop oracle ✅

**Problem:** P1, P5.

**Files:** `tests/integration/test_replan_stop.py` — new module;
optionally a small additional case in `tests/test_worker.py` if a unit
seam is exposed by the integration work.

**Change:**

1. Add a deterministic integration test that drives the runtime with a
   fake reviewer/planner pair which always returns the same failing
   strategy fingerprint (or > 50% word overlap, the rules from M1229).
2. Assert the runtime stops with a stuck/circular-replan outcome and
   does not loop until timeout.
3. Use plan/task DB rows and stop reason as the oracle, not message
   prose.
4. Optionally include a one-line unit assertion for the codegen
   guardrail (M1233: `validate_plan` rejects `[tool, exec, ...]` at
   plan start unless goal says run/test) if not already covered — this
   is small enough to fit here without its own milestone.

**Why:** Unit coverage for `extend_replan` and stuck detection is
already strong. What is missing is one runtime-level proof that the
full loop obeys the stop contract. Doing it deterministically (instead
of live) means it runs cheaply in CI and is not provider-fragile.

**Test:** Integration test with fake reviewer/planner; no live model.

## Phase 4 — Connector and plugin operational lifecycle (M1276-M1278)

### M1276 — Connector daemon lifecycle extension ✅

**Problem:** P3.

**Files:** `tests/test_supervisor.py` (extend, do **not** rewrite),
optionally a new `tests/integration/test_connector_lifecycle.py` for
the e2e CLI flow; use the M1268 fake connector directory.

**Change:**

1. The 251 existing lines of `test_supervisor.py` already cover
   backoff and restart logic well. This milestone **extends**, it does
   not replace.
2. Add an end-to-end CLI lifecycle test around the M1268 fake
   connector directory: install-like setup → `run` → status →
   crash/restart metadata → stop.
3. Assert `.pid`, `.status.json`, and `connector.log` transitions
   instead of only checking printed text. (Paths verified in
   `cli/connector.py:78-380`.)

**Why:** Connector runtime management is operationally fragile. The
lower-level pieces are tested, but the full lifecycle as a CLI flow is
not.

**Test:** Deterministic host tests with the fake connector process.

### M1277 — Connector install/update/remove health ✅

**Problem:** P3.

**Files:** `tests/test_cli_connector.py`, shared helpers in
`tests/_cli_plugin_helpers.py` if useful.

**Change:**

1. Expand connector CLI tests to cover:
   - update of an already-installed connector
   - `config.example.toml` → `config.toml` copy semantics on install
   - preserving an edited `config.toml` across update
   - unhealthy/missing binary reporting after update
2. Keep these deterministic with fake git/plugin directories rather
   than depending on network.

**Why:** The code path exists and matters operationally, but current
coverage leans more heavily on install and status than on
update/refresh behavior.

**Test:** Unit/CLI tests with fake repos and controlled subprocess
outcomes.

### M1278 — Tool/plugin refresh and update after first install ✅

**Problem:** P3.

**Files:** `tests/test_cli_tool.py`, `tests/test_tool_install_health.py`,
`cli/plugin_test_runner.py` only if report quality needs changes.

**Change:**

1. Add deterministic tests for the "already installed → refresh deps /
   git pull" code path in shared plugin install/update logic.
2. Distinguish these from plugin smoke tests: the goal is **not**
   "official repo cloned successfully", but "local lifecycle behavior
   is correct when repo already exists".
3. Optional: at most one live-network smoke test for a real official
   plugin update path if the repo state makes it practical.

**Why:** The shared plugin lifecycle has meaningful local behavior
that should not rely on external plugin repos to be exercised.

**Test:** Primarily deterministic CLI/unit tests; live smoke optional.

**Outcome (2026-04-08):** Audit found that all the plan items are
already comprehensively covered in `tests/test_cli_tool.py`:

- "already installed → refresh deps / git pull" code path:
  `test_skill_install_already_installed` (line 476),
  `test_skill_install_already_installed_git_pull_failure_warns`
  (line 493),
  `test_skill_install_already_installed_git_pull_uses_safe_directory`
  (line 521).
- Update flows: `test_skill_update_single` (585),
  `test_skill_update_all` (605), `test_skill_update_nonexistent`
  (627), `test_skill_update_git_pull_failure` (643),
  `test_skill_update_all_no_dir` (1005),
  `test_skill_update_all_empty_dir` (1015),
  `test_skill_update_deps_sh_failure_warns` (1028),
  `test_skill_update_missing_binaries_warns` (1060).

The "audit before adding" rule from M1268 says do not add tests that
duplicate existing coverage. No meaningful gap was found, so this
milestone closes as ✅ on the basis of the audit. The optional live
smoke remains optional and is not added.

## Phase 5 — Long-tail registry and negative paths (M1279-M1280)

### M1279 — Negative install/update paths for nonexistent packages ✅

**Problem:** P3, P6.

**Files:** `tests/test_cli_tool.py`, `tests/test_cli_connector.py`,
`tests/test_presets.py`, `docs/testing-live.md`.

**Change:**

1. Add deterministic CLI tests for:
   - `kiso tool install nonexistent-xyz`
   - `kiso connector install nonexistent-xyz`
   - update/remove on nonexistent local targets
2. Ensure these tests assert the intended user-facing "not found"
   contract, not raw git stderr passthrough.
3. Remove or update lingering TODO notes in `docs/testing-live.md`
   once the tests exist.

**Why:** Explicitly called out as a missing test in
`docs/testing-live.md` and a recurring operator path.

**Test:** Deterministic CLI tests; optional live smoke only if low cost.

### M1280 — Registry matrix and non-preset capability smoke ✅

**Problem:** P3, P4, P6.

**Files:** `tests/live/test_plugins.py`, `tests/test_registry.py`,
`tests/README.md`, `docs/testing.md`.

**Change:**

1. Add deterministic checks over `registry.json` consistency:
   names, types, taxonomy shape, and expected clone URL mapping.
2. Reclassify official plugin tests explicitly as smoke unless the
   oracle is deterministic and maintained by Kiso.
3. Ensure the smoke matrix covers all currently listed official
   packages (verified against `registry.json`): `websearch`, `aider`,
   `browser`, `moltbook`, `gworkspace`, `docreader`, `transcriber`,
   `ocr`, and connector `discord`.
4. For each package, assign the minimum honest confidence level:
   deterministic / live-network smoke / interactive acceptance.
5. Add at least one workflow outside the default preset trio,
   preferably `docreader` or `transcriber`, where the oracle is
   file/tool behavior rather than prose quality.

**Why:** The registry is broader than the preset workflow coverage.
v0.9 should make the coverage map explicit and extend semantic
coverage to a couple of non-preset capabilities.

**Test:** Mixed deterministic + classified smoke.

## Phase 6 — Recovery acceptance flows (M1281)

### M1281 — Recovery-oriented multi-plan functional flows ✅ (needs manual run)

**Problem:** P1, P4, P5.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py` — new module, or
extend `tests/functional/test_advanced_flows.py` /
`tests/functional/test_cross_plan_files.py`.

**Change:**

1. Add a small set of multi-plan functional tests whose oracle is
   recovery semantics rather than answer quality:
   - failed first attempt → replan → successful second strategy
   - local file discovered in prior plan → reused in later plan
     without re-fetch
2. Avoid broad open-ended prompts; pre-shape the environment so the
   replan reason is observable and the success path is concrete.

**Why:** Kiso differentiates itself on recovery and durable
orchestration. Functional coverage should reflect that more directly.

**Test:** Extended functional tests with file/task/plan assertions.

## Phase 7 — Cross-layer adversarial defense (M1282-M1283)

### M1282 — Paraphraser → planner context boundary ✅

**Problem:** P5, P7.

**Files:** new `tests/integration/test_paraphraser_boundary.py`.

**Verified facts:** `run_paraphraser` is exposed in
`kiso.brain.__init__.py` public surface (verified via
`tests/test_import_surfaces.py:_BRAIN_PUBLIC_NAMES`); implementation
lives in `kiso/brain/text_roles.py` and `kiso/brain/common.py`; role
prompt at `kiso/roles/paraphraser.md`. The seam is mockable.

**Change:**

1. Add a test that verifies the `untrusted message → paraphraser →
   planner context` handoff actually invokes the paraphraser path.
2. Assert: the planner receives the paraphrased form, not the raw
   untrusted text, and that any literal injection patterns are not
   passed through unchanged into planner-visible context.
3. Keep scope tight: this is a prerequisite for M1283, not a full
   security audit on its own.

**Why:** M1283 (the adversarial matrix) presupposes that the
paraphraser is on the critical path. Without explicit proof, the rest
of the adversarial suite is testing on top of an unverified
assumption.

**Test:** Deterministic test, mocked LLM for paraphraser/planner.

### M1283 — Cross-layer adversarial input matrix ✅

**Problem:** P4, P5, P7.

**Files:** `tests/live/test_flows.py`, `tests/live/test_roles.py`,
new focused file `tests/functional/test_security_flows.py` if helpful.

**Change:**

1. Add a compact adversarial matrix covering the highest-value
   boundaries Kiso explicitly claims to defend:
   - untrusted message → paraphraser → planner context (builds on M1282)
   - malicious tool output → reviewer/replan context
   - published/local file content that tries to induce follow-up
     harmful steps
   - install/use loops where "not found" or fake-success text could
     mislead the runtime
2. Reuse existing harnesses where possible — do not build a giant
   security lab.
3. Prefer oracles like:
   - planner task shape stays bounded/safe
   - reviewer returns `replan`/null learn instead of promoting bad facts
   - runtime stops or replans instead of blindly continuing
   - dangerous literal content is paraphrased/fenced/sanitized before
     reuse

**Why:** Kiso's docs and architecture explicitly rely on layered
defenses rather than a single perfect filter. Those layers are
valuable only if the important cross-layer handoffs are tested as a
system, not only as isolated helper behavior.

**Test:** Mixed live + functional coverage, with deterministic
assertions on task/review/runtime state wherever possible.

## Phase 8 — Closeout (M1284-M1285)

### M1284 — Test suite audit, prune, and consolidation ✅

**Problem:** P9.

**Files:** read-only audit of `tests/test_worker.py` (613 tests, 13.5k
lines), `tests/test_brain.py` (825 tests, 10.5k lines),
`tests/test_safety_rules.py` (279 lines) vs
`tests/functional/test_safety_rules.py` (139 lines), and
`tests/test_security.py` (492 lines). Outputs land in
`tests/README.md` and a `devplan/v0.9-audit.md` working document.

**Verified scope (do NOT propose for deletion):**
- `tests/test_rename_completeness.py` (54 lines, 4 tests) — verified
  to be intentional runtime invariants (modules import, legacy shim
  files removed, registry uses post-rename keys). Keep.
- `tests/test_import_surfaces.py` (86 lines, 4 tests) — verified to be
  an intentional public-surface guard for `kiso.brain` /
  `kiso.main` / `kiso.worker` against accidental refactor breakage.
  Keep.

**Change:**

1. **Read-only audit pass** of the largest and most-likely-redundant
   test files. For each file, produce:
   - test count, line count, dominant scenario themes
   - pairs/groups of tests that appear to cover the same scenario with
     trivial variation
   - tests that look like one-shot regressions for milestones now
     stable for >6 months
   - tests that depend on behaviors that have since changed and may be
     asserting stale contracts
2. **Targets and reasoning, not deletions.** Produce a structured
   proposal listing each candidate cut/merge with:
   - file:line range
   - reason for the proposal (duplicate of X / stale regression /
     superseded by Y / smoke without oracle)
   - risk level if removed
3. **Human approval before any deletion.** Nothing in this milestone
   commits a removal without explicit per-file approval from the
   maintainer.
4. **Likely targets** (from size and history, not yet from content):
   - `tests/test_worker.py` — almost certainly contains scenario
     duplication accumulated across many milestones
   - `tests/test_brain.py` — same
   - boundary check between `tests/test_safety_rules.py` and
     `tests/functional/test_safety_rules.py` — verify intentional vs
     accidental duplication
   - boundary check between `tests/test_security.py` and the safety
     files — verify they cover distinct domains
5. After approvals, execute the agreed cuts/merges and re-run M1267
   baselines to record the suite size delta.

**Why:** v0.9 adds 17 milestones of new tests on top of an already
large suite. Without a deliberate audit pass, the suite grows
monotonically, which is the recipe for slow CI and tests that nobody
trusts. Doing this last (after the additions land) means the audit
also catches any duplication v0.9 itself may have introduced.

**Test:** Audit document + reduced suite line count + green test runs
after every approved cut.

### M1285 — Coverage matrix, suite contracts, and oracle sweep ✅

**Problem:** P5, P6.

**Files:** `tests/README.md`, `docs/testing.md`, `docs/flow.md` only
if test scope requires clarification; touch only tests directly added
in v0.9. Plus a small audit of `kiso/api/admin.py` HTTP coverage (see
below).

**Verified facts that shape the small "admin coverage" task:**
- `kiso/api/runtime.py` has only 2 routes: `GET /health` (covered by
  `test_health.py`, 5 tests) and `GET /pub/{token}/{filename:path}`
  (covered by `test_published.py`, ~15 tests including path traversal,
  symlink, CSP). No gap.
- `kiso/api/admin.py` has 7 routes: 4 cron CRUD routes (covered by
  `test_cron_api.py`, 9 tests), `/admin/reload-env` (covered by
  `test_admin.py`, 11 tests including rate-limit), `/admin/stats`,
  and `/admin/reload-config`. The latter two are the only candidates
  for missing HTTP-route coverage, and they fit as a 1-2 test task in
  this closeout milestone — not a milestone of their own.

**Change:**

1. **Coverage matrix.** Add a compact capability matrix mapping major
   Kiso guarantees to the suite level that owns them: startup
   recovery, worker spawn atomicity (covering /msg and cron),
   connector polling fallback, webhook retry, `uploads/`, `pub/`,
   `session_secrets`, plugin lifecycle, sandbox isolation, live role
   compliance, paraphraser→planner boundary, adversarial matrix,
   interactive/destructive acceptance. Mark each line with the
   confidence tier: blocking semantic, optional smoke, or manual
   acceptance.
2. **Admin API gap closure.** Verify whether `/admin/stats` and
   `/admin/reload-config` have explicit HTTP-route tests in
   `test_stats.py` and `test_admin.py`. If either is missing, add 1-2
   small tests with explicit status/body oracles. This is a task, not
   a phase of its own.
3. **Suite classification.** After M1269-M1283 land, update testing
   docs so runtime guarantees point to the suite level that now owns
   them. Explicitly label startup recovery, worker concurrency,
   webhook retry, polling fallback, secret containment, and
   adversarial matrix as **blocking semantic** integration coverage.
4. **Interactive/destructive contracts.** Document the acceptance
   contract for interactive and destructive suites: what each test
   proves, what it does not prove, and what evidence the human
   operator should capture when judging success. Tighten any
   especially weak assertions where a better observable effect is
   available without making them brittle.
5. **Oracle sweep.** Review the new and adjacent tests added in v0.9
   and replace any remaining wording-only assertions with stronger
   state-based oracles where available. Do not churn unrelated old
   tests.
6. **Deferred ledger.** Record any lower-priority items intentionally
   deferred or downgraded to smoke/manual, with a clear reason
   (external fragility, missing official repo, human gate, low
   leverage). Remove stale TODOs that were completed during v0.9.

**Why:** v0.9 is about confidence quality, not just test count. The
plan should end with a deliberate cleanup pass so the suite additions
do not slide back into weaker habits, plus a durable map so future
work knows what is covered well, what is only smoke, and what still
requires humans.

**Test:** Documentation plus light assertion cleanup; verify
referenced suites/files actually exist.

## Items intentionally NOT in v0.9 (verified, with reasons)

These were considered and dropped during planning. Each is verified
against the actual code so they do not resurface as "you forgot X":

- **LLM stall / fallback model runtime test.** `tests/test_brain.py`
  already has 8+ tests covering `fallback_model`:
  `test_stall_uses_fallback_model`, `test_timeout_uses_fallback_model`,
  `test_retry_llm_with_validation_fallback`, plus planner/reviewer
  paths via `_retry_llm_with_validation`. The seams in
  `kiso/brain/common.py:763-855` and `kiso/brain/text_roles.py:122-146`
  are exercised. A runtime-level test would be incremental gain at
  best.
- **Schema migration tests.** Already covered in `tests/test_store.py`
  starting at line 2069 (`test_duration_ms_migration_on_existing_db`,
  `test_m345_migration_converts_entity_tags`,
  `test_m345_migration_multiple_entities`,
  `test_m345_migration_no_entity_tags_noop`). The migration logic
  itself is in `kiso/store/setup.py:24-38`.
- **Cancel-mid-execution as its own milestone.** `tests/test_cancel.py`
  has 10 tests covering: `/sessions/{session}/cancel` route
  (`test_cancel_sets_event_returns_200`,
  `test_cancel_during_plan_drains_queue`,
  `test_cancel_idle_session_returns_not_cancelled`), exec subprocess
  kill (`test_exec_task_cancel_kills_subprocess`), cancel event
  semantics, and CLI cancel flow. Cancel route is at
  `kiso/api/sessions.py:272`. No meaningful gap.
- **Cron + spawn race as its own milestone.** Cron uses the same
  `_ensure_worker` function as `/msg` (verified at `kiso/main.py:472`),
  so spawn atomicity for cron is covered by M1270. The only
  cron-specific surface (cron bypassing inflight classification) is
  one test inside M1270, not a milestone.
- **Runtime/admin API as its own milestone.** Verified that
  `kiso/api/runtime.py` has only 2 routes, both well-covered, and
  `kiso/api/admin.py` has 7 routes of which 5 are well-covered. The
  remaining 1-2 tests for `/admin/stats` and `/admin/reload-config`
  fit as a task in M1285.
- **In-memory SQLite for tests.** `kiso/store/setup.py::init_db` uses
  WAL journal mode and ALTER TABLE migrations, and tests use
  `tmp_path` heavily. `:memory:` is not a drop-in replacement. The
  feasible perf path is **tmpfs** (`--basetemp=/dev/shm`), which is in
  M1267.
- **`tests/test_rename_completeness.py` deletion.** Verified to be
  intentional runtime invariants (modules import, legacy shim files
  removed, registry uses post-rename keys). Lean (54 lines) and useful.
- **`tests/test_import_surfaces.py` deletion.** Verified to be an
  intentional public-surface guard for `kiso.brain` / `kiso.main` /
  `kiso.worker` against accidental refactor breakage. Useful.
- **Codegen guardrail (M1233) as its own milestone.** Folded as a
  small task into M1276.
- **Install routing suppression (M1234) as its own milestone.**
  Unit-level test, single PR, not milestone-worthy.
- **`usage_guide` and `consumes` live planner influence test.** Both
  features already strongly covered structurally; live test cost is
  high and dev experience gain is low.
- **Performance / load / fuzz / mutation testing.** High noise, low
  ROI for Kiso's current stage.

## Phase 9 — Functional test robustness (M1286)

### M1286 — Drive-until-done install loop and command-vs-data separation ✅

**Problem:** Two functional test failures observed on the v0.9
shipping run (`test_browser.py::TestF1BrowserInstall::
test_browser_install_flow` and `test_multitool.py::TestF17FullPipeline
::test_screenshot_ocr_aider_exec_msg`) revealed two **general** test
robustness gaps that affect any test driving Kiso through real LLM
behavior. Both failures were diagnosed as test issues, not core
regressions; both fixes must be **general** so they do not constrain
the planner to specific phrasings or specific page contents.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_browser.py`,
`tests/functional/test_multitool.py`,
`tests/functional/conftest.py` (shared install-flow helper),
plus a grep sweep for similar patterns elsewhere.

**Verified diagnoses:**

1. *Install-flow helper assumes a fixed number of turns.*
   `_run_with_install_flow` in `test_browser.py` and
   `_run_with_tool_install` in `test_multitool.py` both assume the
   install conversation resolves in at most 2 user turns: original
   request → "sì, installa il tool X". This is correct only if Turn
   1 actually produces an install proposal. The planner is free to
   attempt a workaround on Turn 1 (e.g. answer the request via a
   curl/echo exec without proposing install), in which case Turn 2
   becomes the *first* install proposal and the test asserts before
   any actual install runs. The same test re-run produced PASS on
   the very next attempt — the test is non-deterministic by LLM
   behavior, with no underlying core regression.
2. *Substring match on data-bearing task fields.* The assertion
   `assert "curl" not in task_blob and "wget" not in task_blob` at
   `test_multitool.py:160` is intended to catch a planner that
   re-downloads a file instead of reusing the local one. But
   `task_blob` is built from `(task.detail or "") + (task.command or
   "")` joined across all tasks of a plan, and the `detail` field
   of an exec task often contains a heredoc body with arbitrary
   stdin data. In this run, the OCR text of the Wikipedia Python
   page (which contains "curly brackets" twice — verified
   deterministically with
   `curl https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(programming_language)
   | grep -c "curly"` → 2) was passed as a heredoc body. The
   substring `curl` matched `curly`, producing a false positive.

**Change:**

1. **Drive-until-done install helper.** Refactor the shared install
   flow into a single function in `tests/functional/conftest.py`:

   ```python
   async def drive_install_flow(
       run_message,
       tool_name: str,
       prompt: str,
       *,
       max_turns: int = 4,
       timeout: float = LLM_INSTALL_TIMEOUT,
   ):
       """Drive a conversation forward until *tool_name* is
       installed (or max_turns is reached), then re-issue the
       original prompt so the result reflects the installed-tool
       path. Does not constrain what the planner does on any turn —
       just keeps the conversation moving the way a real user would.
       """
       result = await run_message(prompt, timeout=timeout)
       turns_used = 1
       while not tool_installed(tool_name) and turns_used < max_turns:
           result = await run_message(
               f"sì, installa il tool {tool_name}", timeout=timeout,
           )
           turns_used += 1
       if tool_installed(tool_name):
           result = await run_message(prompt, timeout=timeout)
       return result
   ```

   - Replace `_run_with_install_flow` (in `test_browser.py`) and
     `_run_with_tool_install` (in `test_multitool.py`) with calls
     to `drive_install_flow`.
   - `TestF1BrowserInstall::test_browser_install_flow` currently has
     its own ad-hoc 2-turn loop that asserts directly on the
     "tool_installed" state. Replace it with a call to
     `drive_install_flow` followed by the same assertion. The test
     will then pass regardless of which path the planner picks on
     Turn 1.
   - The helper does NOT prescribe what the planner should do on
     any turn. The planner is free to propose an install, install
     directly, attempt a workaround, or change strategy mid-flow.
     The helper simply drives the conversation forward. This is
     also closer to how a real human user would behave: keep asking
     until the tool works.

2. **Command-vs-data assertion separation.** Introduce a small
   helper in `tests/functional/conftest.py`:

   ```python
   import re

   def assert_no_command_word(tasks, words):
       """Assert no exec task has a command matching any of *words*
       as a whole word. Only the `command` field is inspected — task
       `detail` and heredoc bodies often contain arbitrary data
       (OCR output, API responses, planner reasoning) that may
       incidentally contain substrings matching command names."""
       pattern = re.compile(
           r"\b(" + "|".join(re.escape(w) for w in words) + r")\b"
       )
       for t in tasks:
           if t.get("type") != "exec":
               continue
           command = t.get("command") or ""
           m = pattern.search(command)
           assert m is None, (
               f"forbidden command word {m.group(0)!r} in exec task "
               f"command: {command[:200]}"
           )
   ```

   Replace the failing assertion at `test_multitool.py:160`:
   ```python
   assert_no_command_word(last_plan_tasks, ["curl", "wget"])
   ```

   Properties of the new helper:
   - inspects only the `command` field (the actual shell command),
     never `detail` (which can contain reasoning text or heredoc
     bodies)
   - uses `\b...\b` word boundaries so `curly`, `libcurl`,
     `pycurl`, `wgetopt`, etc. do not match
   - reusable for any future "no fetch / no recompile / no rm"
     style assertion

3. **Suite-wide sweep.** Grep `tests/functional/` for similar
   substring assertions on `task_blob`-style joined fields
   (`detail + command`, `output` joined across tasks, etc.) and
   convert any found to use `assert_no_command_word` (or an
   equivalent word-boundary helper) where the intent is to catch
   shell commands. Do not change assertions that legitimately scan
   *output* text for substrings.

4. Re-run the originally failing tests through
   `./utils/run_tests.sh s` to confirm green:
   - `test_browser_install_flow` should be deterministic regardless
     of which path the planner picks on Turn 1.
   - `test_screenshot_ocr_aider_exec_msg` should be deterministic
     regardless of which words the OCR text contains.

**Why these fixes are general, not overfitted:**

- The drive-until-done loop does NOT constrain the planner. It
  does not require an install proposal on Turn 1, does not pin a
  specific phrasing, and does not encode any knowledge about how
  the planner *should* behave. It just drives the conversation
  forward the way a real user would and accepts any path the
  planner chooses. This preserves Kiso's generalist nature: the
  test proves the install flow eventually converges, not that it
  follows a hard-coded script.
- The command-vs-data helper enforces a general principle: shell
  command assertions belong on the `command` field with word
  boundaries, not on free-form `detail` text or heredoc bodies.
  It applies to any future test that wants to forbid a shell
  command pattern, not just curl/wget. It does not pin the test
  to the current Wikipedia page content or to the current OCR
  output, and it does not change which pages or which tools the
  test exercises.
- Neither change touches kiso core code. The planner, worker,
  install routing (M1234), and codegen guardrail (M1233) are
  unchanged. Only test infrastructure is hardened.

**Test:** Run both originally failing tests via
`./utils/run_tests.sh s "tests/functional/test_browser.py::
TestF1BrowserInstall"` and
`./utils/run_tests.sh s "tests/functional/test_multitool.py::
TestF17FullPipeline"` on multiple consecutive runs to confirm the
flakiness is gone. Then run the full functional + extended tier via
`./utils/run_tests.sh --auto --functional --extended`.

**Outcome (2026-04-09):**
- Both originally failing tests now PASS:
  - `test_browser_install_flow`: 3m7s (was: failure on 2-turn assertion)
  - `test_screenshot_ocr_aider_exec_msg`: 16m19s (was: false positive on
    "curly" matching "curl")
- 16 new unit tests in `tests/functional/test_helpers.py` cover both
  helpers exhaustively, including a regression test
  (`test_default_timeout_is_install_timeout`) that pins the install
  timeout default — caught a regression I introduced mid-implementation
  where the new helper was defaulting to run_message's 300s instead of
  the LLM_INSTALL_TIMEOUT 900s the original helpers used.
- Suite-wide sweep converted `tests/functional/test_cross_plan_files.py`
  to use `assert_no_command_word` for the same `curl/wget` check (it
  had the same substring-vs-word-boundary risk, less acute because it
  inspected only `command` and not `detail`).
- Removed: `_run_with_install_flow` (test_browser.py) and
  `_run_with_tool_install` (test_multitool.py) — both replaced by the
  shared `drive_install_flow` helper in functional/conftest.py.
- Unit suite: 4056 passing (unchanged). Integration + helpers: 117
  passing (was 58 before M1286, +59 includes the 16 new helper tests
  + existing test_helpers.py tests).
- Zero kiso core code changes. Planner, worker, install routing
  (M1234), and codegen guardrail (M1233) untouched.

## Phase 10 — Recovery test redesign (M1287)

### M1287 — Drop fragile real-LLM recovery oracle, harden remaining recovery tests ✅

**Problem:** `tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py::TestRecoveryReplanThenSuccess::test_unreachable_then_local_file_recovery`
(added in M1281) fails against real LLM with
`recovery flow did not converge: plans=['failed']`. Investigation
revealed two distinct issues, both in test design — neither in core
runtime code.

**Files:** `tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py` only.

**Verified diagnoses:**

1. *Soft prompt + missing env pre-shaping.* The original test prompt
   was: *"Read the file at /tmp/kiso-recovery-test-input.txt and tell
   me what's inside. **If you can't find it**, look for a similarly
   named file in the session workspace."* The reviewer correctly
   interpreted *"if you can't find it"* as **explicit user permission
   to fail gracefully** and returned `status=ok` after the first
   `cat` failed, ending the plan in `status=failed (no replan)`. The
   runtime did the right thing — the test prompt was wrong. Worse,
   the test never pre-created any "similarly named file in the session
   workspace", so even if the LLM had tried the workspace fallback,
   there would be nothing to find. The test was **never validated
   against real LLM** — M1281 marked it `needs manual run` and only
   verified `--collect-only` parsing.
2. *Forgotten M1286 sweep target.*
   `tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py::test_no_redundant_fetch_when_file_exists_locally`
   contains the same substring assertion pattern that M1286
   converted everywhere else:
   ```python
   forbidden_kw = ("curl", "wget", "http://", "https://", "fetch")
   exec_tasks = [t for t in result.tasks if t.get("type") == "exec"]
   for task in exec_tasks:
       cmd = (task.get("command") or "") + " " + (task.get("detail") or "")
       cmd_lower = cmd.lower()
       assert not any(kw in cmd_lower for kw in forbidden_kw), ...
   ```
   This was added in M1281 just before M1286 was written, so the
   M1286 sweep didn't catch it. It has the same false-positive risk
   on data-bearing fields ("curly brackets", "fetch_data", etc.) as
   the bug M1286 fixed.

**Change:**

1. **Replace `test_unreachable_then_local_file_recovery` with
   `test_workspace_file_discovery`** — a deterministic workspace
   discovery test that does NOT pretend to test "recovery semantics"
   at the real-LLM functional tier. The new test:
   - Pre-creates a file with deterministic content directly in the
     session workspace (using `_session_workspace(func_session)`
     and writing into `{workspace}/data.txt`).
   - Uses an imperative prompt that does NOT give the planner
     permission to fail: *"There is a file called `data.txt` in your
     current working directory. Read it and tell me what's
     inside."*
   - Asserts: `result.success` is True AND the messenger output
     contains the deterministic file content.
   - Drops the "recovery" framing entirely. The recovery contract
     (replan → stop on stuck) is already deterministically tested
     in M1275 with mocked LLM. Real-LLM recovery testing is
     inherently fragile because the LLM is non-deterministic about
     when it chooses to replan. M1281's recovery angle is best
     served by M1275's deterministic test, not by a brittle
     functional test.

2. **Convert
   `test_no_redundant_fetch_when_file_exists_locally`** to use
   `assert_no_command_word` (the M1286 helper) for the curl/wget/
   fetch check. Inspect only the `command` field of `exec` tasks
   with word boundaries. This closes the M1286 sweep gap.

3. **Document in the deferred ledger** (M1285 section) that
   functional-tier recovery semantics testing is intentionally
   skipped, with a pointer to M1275 for the deterministic version.

4. **Re-run both tests** via
   `./utils/run_tests.sh s "tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py"`
   to confirm green against real LLM.

**Why this is general, not overfitted:**

- The new `test_workspace_file_discovery` does NOT prescribe how the
  planner should find the file. It just creates the file in the
  workspace and tells the planner "read the file in your CWD". The
  planner is free to use `cat`, `ls`, `read`, or any other strategy.
  No constraint on planner behavior.
- The pre-shaping (writing a file before sending the message) is
  standard practice for functional tests and is already used in many
  other functional tests in this suite.
- Dropping the "recovery" angle is honest: real-LLM recovery testing
  is fundamentally fragile because the LLM's decision to replan vs.
  fail-gracefully depends on the prompt's softness. The test that
  meaningfully covers recovery (M1275) uses mocked LLM precisely
  because it can be deterministic.
- The `assert_no_command_word` conversion uses the same general
  helper from M1286 — no test-specific logic.
- Zero kiso core code changes. Only the test file is touched.

**Test:** Both tests in `test_recovery_flows.py` must pass against
real LLM via `./utils/run_tests.sh s
"tests/functional/test_recovery_flows.py"`.

## Phase 11 — Workspace dirs and roles ownership (M1288-M1289)

### M1288 — Pre-create all KISO_DIR subdirectories at init ✅

**Problem:** `kiso/main.py::_init_kiso_dirs()` (lines 172-180) only
creates `sys/bin`, `sys/ssh`, and `reference`. The other directories
that kiso reads from at runtime (`tools/`, `connectors/`, `recipes/`,
`sessions/`, `pub/`) are created lazily by their respective code
paths — `discover_tools()` returns empty if `tools/` doesn't exist,
`discover_recipes()` (`kiso/recipe_loader.py:51-53`) silently
returns `[]` if `recipes/` is missing, `_session_workspace()` only
creates a session subdir on first message, etc.

This means:
1. A fresh kiso install has a partial `~/.kiso/` tree, and external
   scripts that want to drop a recipe/tool/connector file have to
   `mkdir -p` first.
2. The user has no visible structure to discover. There is no
   "where do I put a recipe?" affordance.
3. Functional tests that pre-shape state (M1287's
   `test_workspace_file_discovery`) need to know the exact creation
   conditions.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py` (1 function), `tests/test_main.py` (new
`TestInitKisoDirsCreatesAllSubdirs` class).

**Change:**

1. Extend `_init_kiso_dirs()` to also `mkdir -p` the following:
   - `KISO_DIR / "tools"` — installed kiso tools
   - `KISO_DIR / "connectors"` — installed connectors
   - `KISO_DIR / "recipes"` — user-installed `.md` recipes
   - `KISO_DIR / "sessions"` — per-session workspaces parent
   - `KISO_DIR / "pub"` — top-level pub dir (per-session pub lives
     under `sessions/{id}/pub`, but if there is a code path that
     expects this top-level dir to exist, create it; if not, drop
     this one)
   - `KISO_DIR / "roles"` — created here too (M1289 will populate
     it)
   All with `parents=True, exist_ok=True`. No content sync, just
   `mkdir`. Total addition is ~6 lines.

2. **Audit before writing the `pub/` line.** Grep for any code path
   that uses `KISO_DIR / "pub"` (top-level, not `sessions/{}/pub`).
   If no caller exists, skip that one — don't create dirs nothing
   reads.

3. Tests in `tests/test_main.py`:
   - Each new dir gets a 1-line assertion that it exists after
     `_init_kiso_dirs()` runs against `tmp_path`.
   - One regression test that verifies the existing dirs (`sys/bin`,
     `sys/ssh`, `reference`) are still created (covered by existing
     `TestInitKisoDirs` tests but worth confirming after the edit).
   - One test that calling `_init_kiso_dirs()` twice in a row is a
     no-op for the new dirs (idempotency).

**Why this is minimal, not overengineering:**

- Only `mkdir -p` calls. No content seeding (that's M1289 for
  roles), no watcher, no validation, no permissions logic.
- The `pub/` line is gated on a code-path audit so we don't create
  dirs that nothing reads.
- Test surface: ~6 single-line assertions, no complex fixtures.

**Test:** Existing `TestInitKisoDirs` tests must still pass.
New `TestInitKisoDirsCreatesAllSubdirs` covers the additions.

### M1289 — Roles owned by the user dir, with reset hatch ✅

**Problem:** Today `kiso/brain/prompts.py::_load_system_prompt(role)`
(lines 16-30) implements a dual lookup: first try
`KISO_DIR / "roles" / f"{role}.md"`, then fall back to the
package's bundled `kiso/roles/*.md`. This has two consequences:

1. **Mental model is unclear.** A user reading `kiso/roles/planner.md`
   in the source tree may or may not be reading the prompt that
   actually runs, depending on whether they have an override file.
2. **Roles aren't discoverable.** A fresh install has nothing in
   `~/.kiso/roles/`, so the user has no obvious place to look at
   what the planner/reviewer/messenger actually do, much less
   customize them.

User decision (this milestone): copy the bundled roles to
`~/.kiso/roles/` at init (without overwriting existing user files),
make `_load_system_prompt` read **only** from the user dir (no
package fallback), and provide a `kiso role reset` command for
recovery.

**Files:** `kiso/main.py` (`_init_kiso_dirs` extension),
`kiso/brain/prompts.py` (simplify `_load_system_prompt`),
`cli/__init__.py` and a new `cli/role.py` (new `role reset`
subcommand), `tests/test_main.py`, `tests/test_brain.py` or
`tests/test_prompts.py`, new `tests/test_cli_role.py`.

**Change:**

1. **Init copy (additive, no overwrite).** In `_init_kiso_dirs()`,
   after creating `~/.kiso/roles/`, iterate `kiso/roles/*.md` from
   the package and for each role file:
   - If `~/.kiso/roles/{role}.md` does **not** exist → copy from
     package.
   - If it exists with non-zero size → leave alone (user
     customization preserved).
   - If it exists but is empty (0 bytes, `.stat().st_size == 0`)
     → self-heal by copying from package. This catches the "I did
     `> file.md` by mistake" case without ever overwriting real
     content.
   - **No content-diff check, no auto-overwrite, no version
     bumps.** The file at `~/.kiso/roles/{role}.md` is the user's
     property after first copy.

2. **Single source of truth at runtime.** Simplify
   `_load_system_prompt` to:
   ```python
   def _load_system_prompt(role: str) -> str:
       if role in _prompt_cache:
           return _prompt_cache[role]
       user_path = KISO_DIR / "roles" / f"{role}.md"
       if not user_path.exists():
           raise FileNotFoundError(
               f"Role file not found at {user_path}. "
               f"Run `kiso role reset {role}` to restore from the package."
           )
       text = user_path.read_text()
       _prompt_cache[role] = text
       return text
   ```
   Drop the `_ROLES_DIR` package fallback path entirely. The error
   message is the discoverability hatch.

3. **CLI: `kiso role reset`.** New subcommand under `kiso role`:
   - `kiso role reset NAME` → overwrite `~/.kiso/roles/{NAME}.md`
     with the package version. Confirms with the user before
     overwriting if the file exists and is non-empty.
   - `kiso role reset --all` → same for every package role,
     bulk-confirmed once.
   - `kiso role list` → optional small bonus, lists role names that
     exist in the user dir vs in the package (highlights any
     custom-only or missing roles).
   No other `kiso role` commands needed for now.

4. **Tests:**
   - `tests/test_main.py`: init copies all package roles to user
     dir on fresh KISO_DIR; init does not touch existing non-empty
     user role file; init self-heals empty user role file; init is
     idempotent (running twice with full user dir is a no-op).
   - `tests/test_brain.py` or `tests/test_prompts.py`:
     `_load_system_prompt` reads from user dir; raises clear error
     with reset hint when user file missing; no longer falls back
     to package (regression test).
   - `tests/test_cli_role.py` (new): `kiso role reset NAME`
     overwrites; `--all` covers all roles; rejects unknown role
     name with clear error; preserves files for roles not listed.

5. **Migration audit (one-time).** Grep the codebase for any other
   code path that reads roles from `kiso/roles/` directly (e.g.
   tests, dev scripts, doc generators). They should keep reading
   the package files (those are still the source of truth shipped
   with releases) — only the *runtime* reads `~/.kiso/roles/`. Add
   a comment in `kiso/brain/prompts.py` near `_ROLES_DIR` (if it
   stays as a constant for the reset command) clarifying that
   `_ROLES_DIR` is the install-time source, never read at runtime.

**Why this is minimal, not overengineering:**

- No version tracking. No content-diff checks. No auto-overwrite.
  Just "copy if missing or empty, otherwise hands off".
- Single safety hatch (`kiso role reset`) — explicit, user-driven,
  not magical.
- The runtime lookup goes from 2 paths to 1. Simpler, not more
  complex.
- No new file format, no new manifest, no new schema. Roles are
  still plain `.md` with the same content.

**Migration impact (verified safe):**

- Users with `~/.kiso/roles/` empty or missing: init copies package
  roles → runtime works → no change in behavior.
- Users with `~/.kiso/roles/` populated with custom overrides:
  existing files preserved → runtime reads them → behavior
  unchanged. Any role they had NOT customized will get the package
  version copied alongside (new file appears, doesn't replace
  anything).
- Users who somehow have a partial user dir (some roles, not
  others): the missing ones get auto-copied. The present ones
  stay.

**Test:** All existing `test_brain.py` and `test_prompts.py`
prompt-loading tests must still pass after the `_load_system_prompt`
simplification (they may need fixture updates to write the test role
file to a temp `~/.kiso/roles/` instead of relying on the package
fallback).

## Phase 12 — `investigate` as 4th classifier category (M1290)

### M1290 — Add `investigate` as a runtime classifier mode ✅

**Problem:** Today the classifier (`kiso/brain/common.py`, around
line 1462) has 3 categories: `plan`, `chat_kb`, `chat`. There is a
real semantic class of user messages that doesn't fit cleanly into
any of them and currently gets routed as `plan`:

- *"Why is nginx returning 502?"* → user wants understanding, not a
  fix
- *"Show me the current config"* → user wants live state, not a
  change
- *"Database is down"* (isolated report) → user wants diagnosis
  before deciding what to do
- *"Is service Y running?"* → user wants live evidence

These all share a structural property: **the answer requires
running commands or reading files but NOT changing them**, and the
right response is *evidence + explanation*, NOT *propose-and-apply
a fix in the same plan*. Today, kiso routes them through `plan`,
which gives the planner license to propose and apply mutations
unprompted — losing the diagnose-first behavior that makes a
healthy debugger/operator.

The `chat_kb` category already established the precedent that a
sub-class of messages deserves first-class classifier treatment when
its handling differs structurally. `investigate` is the same shape:
a stable, well-defined intent class that should be visible at the
classifier level, not buried as a hint inside `plan`.

This was decided after rejecting the recipe-based approach (recipe
would be opt-in per preset, depend on briefer selection, and rely
on the planner honoring an additive context hint — fragile on every
axis vs. a structural classifier category).

**Files (lean scope):** `kiso/brain/common.py` (classifier prompt +
return validation), `kiso/worker/loop.py` (dispatch propagation),
`kiso/brain/planner.py` (`run_planner` flag + modular prompt
inclusion), `kiso/roles/planner.md` (new modular section), tests.

**Verified facts that shape this milestone:**

- The classifier prompt currently lists 3 categories with examples
  in a single string in `kiso/brain/common.py`. Adding a 4th is a
  prompt edit, not a code refactor.
- The planner role uses the modular prompt mechanism
  (`<!-- MODULE: xxx -->` markers, parsed in
  `kiso/brain/prompts.py:_load_modular_prompt`). New sections can
  be added without changing the loader code — just the role file
  and the module list passed by `run_planner`.
- The worker dispatch in `kiso/worker/loop.py::_process_message`
  already branches on classifier output (chat → fast-path, plan →
  full plan). Adding a 4th branch is a few lines.
- `validate_plan` in `kiso/brain/planner.py` will NOT be touched.
  Per the project rule "no heuristics", we trust the planner role
  module to enforce the read-only contract. If the LLM violates it,
  the user sees the proposal in the messenger output and corrects
  with a follow-up — same trust model as the rest of the runtime.

**Change:**

1. **Classifier prompt** (`kiso/brain/common.py`): add 4th category
   to the prompt string with definition + 3-4 boundary examples.
   Final return values become
   `{"plan", "chat_kb", "chat", "investigate"}`. Update the
   validation list (the parser that reads `category:Language` and
   accepts only known values).

   Boundary examples to include in the prompt:
   - *"Why is X failing?"* → investigate
   - *"Fix the X failure"* → plan
   - *"X is failing"* (isolated report, no fix verb) → investigate
   - *"Show me X's current state"* → investigate
   - *"What do you know about X?"* → chat_kb (memory, not system)
   - *"Restart X"* → plan
   - *"X is down, restart it"* → plan (imperative wins)

   When in doubt between investigate and plan, the prompt
   instructs the classifier to **prefer investigate** — it
   preserves user autonomy (better to ask "want me to fix it"
   than to act unprompted).

2. **Worker dispatch**
   (`kiso/worker/loop.py::_process_message` area): when
   `category == "investigate"`, call `run_planner(...)` with the
   new kwarg `investigate=True`. All other categories unchanged.
   ~3 lines.

3. **`run_planner` flag + modular prompt module**:
   - Add `investigate: bool = False` parameter to
     `run_planner(...)`.
   - When True, include the new `"investigate"` module in the
     modules list passed to `_load_modular_prompt("planner",
     modules)`. The modular loader already exists; no loader
     changes needed.

4. **`kiso/roles/planner.md` new module**: append a section
   delimited by `<!-- MODULE: investigate -->` with the contract:

   > # Investigate mode
   >
   > This is an *investigate* request. The user wants to understand
   > the live system state, not change it.
   >
   > 1. Plan only **read-only** tasks: `exec` for read-only shell
   >    commands (`cat`, `ls`, `ps`, `grep`, `find`, `curl`/`wget`
   >    for HTTP GET only, `git status`, `git log`, etc.); `search`;
   >    `tool` only for tools whose contract is read-only.
   > 2. Do NOT plan tasks that mutate state: no `rm`, no `mv`, no
   >    `apt install`, no `pip install`, no `tee`, no shell
   >    redirection that writes (`>`, `>>`), no `git commit`, no
   >    code edit tools.
   > 3. End the plan with a `msg` task that summarizes WHAT you
   >    found, WHY (root cause if identifiable), and WHAT
   >    changing it would require. Do NOT propose or apply a fix
   >    in this plan — the user gets the diagnosis first.
   > 4. After the user reads your diagnosis they may ask for a
   >    fix in a follow-up message. That follow-up will be
   >    classified as `plan` and you will run normally.

   No change to other modules in the planner role file. The new
   module is opt-in via the modules list, so it has zero effect
   on regular `plan` runs.

5. **Tests:**

   - `tests/test_brain.py::TestClassifier` (or wherever the
     classifier unit tests live): 5 new parametrized cases that
     mock the LLM to return `investigate:English` for the right
     inputs and verify `classify_message` returns `"investigate"`.
     Plus 3 negative cases (imperative phrasings classified as
     `plan`, not `investigate`).
   - `tests/test_brain.py::TestRunPlanner`: 1 test that with
     `investigate=True`, the planner system prompt includes the
     "Investigate mode" section text. Mocked LLM, just verify the
     prompt assembly.
   - `tests/test_worker.py`: 1 test that the dispatch branches on
     `category="investigate"` and calls `run_planner` with
     `investigate=True`. Mocked classifier + mocked planner.
   - `tests/functional/test_investigate.py` (new, extended tier):
     1 real-LLM test, two-step interaction:
     - msg1: *"I get an error when I try to read /tmp/foo.txt — it
       says no such file"* → assert `result.success == True`,
       last plan has tasks of types ⊆ `{exec, search, msg}` (NO
       `tool` task with mutation semantics — but the test does NOT
       inspect command strings, only task types), final msg
       contains evidence of investigation (file path or error
       phrasing).
     - msg2: *"ok, create the file with text 'hello'"* → assert
       `result.success == True`, last plan has at least one `exec`
       task, final msg confirms the action. This proves the
       transition investigate → plan happens naturally on the
       second turn without any explicit state machine.

   **No `validate_plan` test changes.** No heuristic guard tests.

6. **Docs:** brief update to `docs/flow.md` listing the 4
   categories. No new doc files.

**Why this is minimal, not overengineering:**

- Total runtime code change: ~20 lines (1 prompt edit + 1 enum
  value + 1 dispatch branch + 1 kwarg + 1 module list inclusion +
  1 modular prompt section).
- Zero new abstractions: no new class, no new module file, no new
  task type, no new schema. Adds one enum value, one kwarg, one
  prompt section.
- Zero changes to validate_plan, briefer, reviewer, sanitization,
  storage layer, dispatch beyond the single new branch.
- Zero auto-overwrite, heuristic guard, or magic. The contract is
  enforced by prompt + trust, same as everything else in kiso.
- Roll-back is trivial: revert the classifier prompt, drop the
  kwarg, drop the planner module section, remove the new tests.
  ~10 minute change.
- The two-step interaction the user wants (bug report → diagnose
  → fix → apply) emerges naturally from the classifier handling
  each turn independently. No state machine, no in-runtime
  workflow ceremony.

**Migration impact:**

- Existing plan/chat/chat_kb behavior is unchanged. The new
  category is purely additive. If the classifier never picks
  `investigate` for an existing test fixture, that test still
  passes.
- Functional tests that currently rely on certain frames being
  classified as `plan` should still pass — the new prompt's
  default is "if in doubt, prefer investigate over plan only when
  the user is clearly asking to understand". Imperative phrasings
  remain `plan`.
- The new module section in `planner.md` has no effect on regular
  `plan` runs because it's only included when
  `investigate=True`. Existing `plan` plans assemble the same
  prompt as before.

**Test:** All existing `test_brain.py` classifier tests must still
pass. New unit tests cover classifier output, planner module
injection, and worker dispatch. New functional test covers the
two-step interaction.

## Phase 13 — chat_kb → investigate transparent fallback (M1291)

### M1291 — Pre-flight chat_kb facts check, fall back to investigate when empty ✅

**Problem.** The classifier added in M1290 distinguishes
`chat_kb` (info from stored memory) from `investigate` (live
system state) using only the message phrasing and the existing
`Known Entities` hint. But there is a real semantic gap: when
the user asks about something that *could* be in memory but
is not yet, the classifier picks `chat_kb` because the entity
name matches the hint — and then the chat_kb path retrieves
zero facts. The messenger is called anyway, with an empty
briefing context, and produces either "I don't know" or LLM
general knowledge that has nothing to do with the actual
system state.

The right behavior: when chat_kb retrieval comes back empty,
tell the user explicitly and re-route the same message
through the investigate planner so kiso actually inspects
the live system. The classifier *cannot* know in advance
whether a fact exists; the worker *can* check before
committing to the chat_kb response.

This is the missing link the user identified after M1290:
*"come fa il classifier a sapere se quelle info le abbiamo
già o vanno indagate?"*

**Investigation results (2026-04-09):** The original draft of
this milestone said the fallback should live "in
`_fast_path_chat` or whichever helper assembles the chat_kb
response". After reading the code that turned out to be the
wrong layer. The actual situation:
