- The classifier dispatch lives in `handle_message()` in
  `kiso/worker/loop.py` around lines 2540-2571. The branch
  `if msg_class in ("chat", "chat_kb"):` calls
  `_fast_path_chat(...)` which immediately commits a plan
  row + msg task row to the DB
  (`kiso/worker/loop.py:323-446`, plan creation around
  lines 349-354).
- The actual facts retrieval does NOT happen in
  `_fast_path_chat`. It happens downstream in
  `_msg_task_impl()` in `kiso/worker/message_flow.py:206-214`,
  via `search_facts_scored(...)`, *after* the briefer has
  already run and produced `entity_id` and `relevant_tags`.
- That means by the time the "is the result empty" signal
  exists, the plan and msg task are already persisted, the
  briefer has already burned an LLM call, and rolling back
  to take the investigate path requires either committing
  garbage rows or deleting them after the fact.

**Design decision: pre-flight check at the dispatcher.**
Instead of trying to short-circuit the chat_kb path mid-flight,
do a cheap deterministic facts query at the dispatcher *before*
calling `_fast_path_chat`. If `msg_class == "chat_kb"` and the
pre-flight returns zero facts, persist the transition message,
reassign `msg_class = "investigate"`, and fall through to the
existing investigate branch at `loop.py:2617`. No rollback, no
refactor of `_msg_task_impl`, no new sentinels.

**Trade-off — explicit and accepted.** The pre-flight uses raw
keywords from the user message (`content.lower().split()[:10]`,
the same pattern `_msg_task_impl` already uses on
`message_flow.py:211`). The normal chat_kb path uses
`entity_id` + `relevant_tags` derived from the briefer, which
is strictly more precise. So the pre-flight can produce false
negatives: the briefer would have found something, the
keyword search does not, and the user gets an investigate plan
instead of a fast chat_kb response. The failure mode is
*"slightly more verbose than ideal"*, not *"wrong answer"* —
the investigate plan still answers the user's question, just
with read-only shell commands instead of a memory lookup. This
is an acceptable cost for avoiding all the rollback complexity
of the alternative.

The reverse failure mode (pre-flight finds something the
briefer would have rejected) is harmless: the chat_kb path
runs as today.

**Files touched.**

- `kiso/worker/loop.py` — `handle_message()` dispatch site
  around lines 2540-2571: add the pre-flight check between
  the classifier call and the existing
  `if msg_class in ("chat", "chat_kb"):` branch.
- `kiso/store/sessions.py` — used as-is via `save_message()`
  at line 63 for the transition message. No changes.
- `kiso/brain/planner.py` — used as-is. `run_planner(...)`
  already accepts `investigate=True` (M1290). No changes.
- `kiso/store/facts.py` (or wherever `search_facts_scored`
  lives) — used as-is. No changes.
- `tests/test_chat_kb.py` — add new test cases next to the
  existing `TestChatKBEntityFlow` class (line 36).
- `tests/test_brain.py` — leave the existing investigate
  tests around lines 1915 and 1934 untouched; they continue
  to assert the planner-side behavior.

**Boundary — when the fallback does NOT fire.**

- `msg_class == "chat"` (small talk) — no KB lookup, no
  fallback. Pre-flight is skipped entirely.
- `msg_class == "plan"` or `"investigate"` — already
  routed through the planner. Pre-flight is skipped.
- `msg_class == "chat_kb"` AND pre-flight returns ≥1 fact —
  the existing chat_kb path runs unchanged, briefer included.
- Pre-flight DB error (search_facts_scored raises) — log
  the error and proceed with the existing chat_kb path
  unchanged. Do NOT silently fall back; the fallback is
  reserved for *empty result*, not *failed query*.

**Transition message — fixed strings, deterministic.** Per
detected `user_lang` (already returned by `classify_message`
as a string like "Italian" or "English" — see
`kiso/brain/common.py:1468-1471`). The dispatcher already
binds it to a local `user_lang` at `loop.py:2544`. The
transition message is persisted via `save_message(db,
session, None, "assistant", text, trusted=True)` following
the pattern already used in `_fast_path_chat` around line
406.

Default English fallback when `user_lang` is empty or not
in the table:

- English: *"I don't have this in my knowledge base — let
  me check the live system."*
- Italian: *"Non ho questa info nella mia knowledge base —
  vado a controllare il sistema dal vivo."*

The table lives inline in the dispatcher as a small dict.
Two languages at first; adding more is a one-line change.
This is intentionally not a role/prompt because the message
is fixed, deterministic, and must not vary across runs.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Read `handle_message()` in `kiso/worker/loop.py`
  around lines 2540-2620 in full and confirm that
  `user_lang`, `content`, `session`, and the planner kwargs
  are all in scope at the point where the pre-flight check
  will be inserted.
- [x] Confirm the import path for `search_facts_scored`
  from the dispatcher (it is currently imported in
  `kiso/worker/message_flow.py:206`); add the import to
  `loop.py` if missing.
- [x] Add a helper `_chat_kb_preflight_fallback(db,
  config, session, plan_id, content, user_lang, slog)`
  in `loop.py` that runs `search_facts_scored` with raw
  keywords from `content.lower().split()[:10]`, no
  `entity_id`, no `tags`, persists the transition msg
  task on `plan_id`, and returns `True` when the caller
  should re-route to investigate.
- [x] In `handle_message()`, immediately after the
  classifier returns and before the
  `if msg_class in ("chat", "chat_kb"):` branch, add: if
  `msg_class == "chat_kb"` and the pre-flight returns
  True, reassign `msg_class = "investigate"` and fall
  through.
- [x] Add a 2-key dict `_CHAT_KB_FALLBACK_MSGS` mapping
  `user_lang` → transition string for English and
  Italian, with English as the default for any other or
  empty value.
- [x] Wrap the pre-flight `search_facts_scored` call in
  a try/except: on exception, log via the existing
  session logger and proceed with the original `chat_kb`
  path unchanged (do NOT fall back on error, only on
  empty result).
- [x] Confirm that the existing branch
  `if msg_class == "investigate":` at `loop.py` picks up
  the reassigned `msg_class` correctly with no other
  state needed (the planner only requires `db`, `config`,
  `session`, `user_role`, `new_message`, plus
  `investigate=True`, all already in scope).
- [x] Unit test in `tests/test_chat_kb.py`: chat_kb with
  pre-flight returning ≥1 fact → fallback NOT triggered,
  no transition task persisted.
- [x] Unit test in `tests/test_chat_kb.py`: chat_kb with
  pre-flight returning 0 facts → transition msg task
  persisted, helper returns True (caller re-routes).
- [x] Unit test: empty content (no extractable
  keywords) → fallback NOT triggered.
- [x] Unit test: pre-flight `search_facts_scored`
  raises → fallback NOT triggered, no transition task,
  exception logged.
- [x] Unit test: transition message uses the Italian
  string when `user_lang == "Italian"`, the English
  string when `user_lang == ""` or unknown.
- [ ] (Optional, extended tier) functional test in
  `tests/functional/`: user asks *"What's the current
  uptime?"* against an empty KB → DB ends with one
  transition message + one investigate plan whose tasks
  include a read-only `exec` running `uptime`. Skipped:
  unit tests above already cover the contract.
- [x] Run `tests/test_chat_kb.py` and the existing
  investigate tests in `tests/test_brain.py` to confirm
  zero regression (969 tests passed).

**Why this is minimal, not overengineering.**

- ~15 lines added at one site in `loop.py`. Zero new
  modules, zero new task types, zero new schemas, zero
  changes to the planner or to `_msg_task_impl`.
- Re-uses M1290's `investigate=True` planner flag
  completely. The investigate branch at `loop.py:2617`
  is unchanged.
- The trigger is a deterministic structural check
  (`len(...) == 0`), not a heuristic. The transition
  string is a fixed dict lookup, not LLM-generated.
- The fallback is observable: every transition lands in
  the DB via `save_message` and is delivered through the
  existing webhook path. Easy to debug, easy to test.
- Roll-back is reverting one diff in `loop.py` plus the
  new tests. No data migration, no schema change.

**Out of scope.**

- Refactoring `_msg_task_impl` to expose retrieval results
  to the dispatcher. The pre-flight approach makes this
  unnecessary; if a future milestone wants briefer-quality
  precision in the pre-flight, that is a separate
  decision.
- Adding more languages to the transition string table
  beyond English and Italian. Trivial follow-up if needed.
- Changing the classifier prompt to predict KB hits.
  Already explicitly rejected; the classifier cannot
  know.
- Suppressing the transition message when the investigate
  plan would be very fast. The transition is the user's
  signal that kiso is switching mode; hiding it defeats
  the purpose.

## Phase 14 — Roles UX, naming, and discoverability (M1292-M1294)

**Context.** After M1289 the role prompt files live under
`~/.kiso/roles/` and are owned by the user, and after M1290 there
are 12 distinct roles in active use (`planner`, `messenger`,
`worker`, `reviewer`, `briefer`, `curator`, `consolidator`,
`classifier`, `inflight-classifier`, `paraphraser`,
`summarizer-session`, `searcher`). An audit of role usage on
2026-04-09 confirmed that **all 12 roles are alive** — every
`.md` file is loaded by exactly one Python entry point and
called from the worker loop, message flow, planner, or
review flow. There are no dead roles to delete.

The audit did surface three real UX/clarity problems that are
worth a dedicated phase:

1. **Discoverability is zero.** There is no `kiso roles`
   command. The user only learns that roles exist by opening
   `~/.kiso/config.toml` `[models]`, by triggering an error
   that mentions `kiso role reset {role}`, or by listing
   `~/.kiso/roles/`. After M1289 made roles user-owned, the
   absence of a discovery surface is a visible gap.

2. **Naming inconsistencies between role filenames and
   Python entry points.** The most jarring case is
   `worker.md` → `run_exec_translator()`, which collides with
   the unrelated `kiso/worker/` *module* (the actual task
   executor). Other smaller gaps: `classifier.md` →
   `classify_message()`, `inflight-classifier.md` →
   `classify_inflight()`, and `summarizer-session.md` whose
   `-session` suffix is not reflected in `run_summarizer()`
   (and no other summarizer variant exists). None of these
   break anything, but together they make jumping between
   the prompt and the call site noisier than it should be.

3. **`classifier` and `inflight-classifier` may overlap.**
   Two roles, two prompts, two functions, same default
   model (`gemini-2.5-flash`), classifying messages at two
   different points in the lifecycle. They might genuinely
   need to be separate, or they might be a candidate for
   consolidation behind a `phase` parameter. The audit did
   not compare the prompts; that comparison is the milestone.

This phase addresses all three, in dependency order: ship the
discovery surface first (it has standalone value), then the
internal renames (which benefit from the registry built in
M1292), then the investigation-only milestone for the
classifier overlap.

**What is explicitly out of scope for v0.9:**

- No new roles. No removal of any existing role.
- No change to model defaults in `_MODEL_METADATA`.
- No REST endpoint for role management. Roles stay internal
  infrastructure; only the CLI surface is added.
- No change to the planner prompt budget or modular markers.
- No touching `~/.kiso/roles/` content as part of M1292
  beyond what the user already gets after M1289.

### M1292 — `kiso roles` CLI surface and roles registry ✅

**Problem.** Users have no way to ask kiso "what roles do
you have, what model does each one use, and where is the
prompt file for each one". Today this information is split
across `kiso/config.py` (`_MODEL_METADATA`), `kiso/roles/*.md`
filenames, `~/.kiso/config.toml` `[models]`, and the Python
call sites. The error message added in M1289 already
references a `kiso role reset {role}` form that does not
exist as a discoverable top-level command surface.

**Goal.** Add a single `kiso roles` command group that is
the canonical user-facing entry point for inspecting roles,
and back it with an in-code **roles registry** that becomes
the single source of truth for role metadata (name,
description, default model, Python entry point, prompt
file path).

**Approach.**

- Create `kiso/brain/roles_registry.py`. This module exposes
  a `ROLES` dict (or list of dataclasses), one entry per
  role currently in `_MODEL_METADATA`, each with:
  - `name` (matches the `.md` filename stem)
  - `description` (one human-readable sentence)
  - `default_model` (cross-referenced from
    `_MODEL_METADATA`, not duplicated — the registry imports
    it; drift is impossible by construction)
  - `prompt_filename` (just the filename, not a full path —
    the path is resolved at read time against the user dir)
  - `python_entry` (string like `"text_roles.run_messenger"`,
    used only for documentation/`kiso roles show`)
- Add CLI command group in `cli/roles.py` (new file) wired
  into `cli/__init__.py`:
  - `kiso roles list` — table with columns: name, model,
    description, `user override` flag (✓ if the file in
    `~/.kiso/roles/<name>.md` differs from the bundled
    default, otherwise empty).
  - `kiso roles show <name>` — print the resolved prompt
    text (user override if present, otherwise bundled
    default), preceded by a 2-line header (model, entry
    point).
  - `kiso roles diff <name>` — unified diff of user
    override vs bundled default. If no override, prints
    "no user override".
  - `kiso roles reset <name>` — same behavior as the
    existing `kiso role reset` (M1289), now exposed under
    the plural group. Keep the singular form working as a
    deprecated alias for one cycle (no warning yet, just
    keep it).
- Help text for `kiso roles` mentions that role files are
  user-owned in `~/.kiso/roles/` and that editing them is
  supported.
- The registry **does not** introduce a new model for any
  role and **does not** change role loading semantics. The
  Python brain code keeps loading prompts via the existing
  `_load_system_prompt()` / `_load_modular_prompt()` paths
  in `kiso/brain/prompts.py`. The registry is purely a
  metadata layer for the CLI and for future docs.

**Why a registry, not just a CLI.** Without a registry, the
CLI would have to hardcode the list of roles in two places
(`_MODEL_METADATA` and the new CLI), which would drift the
moment someone adds a role. With a registry, adding a new
role means: (1) add to `_MODEL_METADATA`, (2) add to
registry with description. Both live in code, not in the
CLI, and the CLI just iterates.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Create `kiso/brain/roles_registry.py` exposing one
  entry per role with `name`, `description`, `model_key`
  (looked up against `MODEL_DEFAULTS` at access time, not
  duplicated), `prompt_filename`, and `python_entry`.
- [x] Create `cli/roles.py` and wire it into
  `cli/__init__.py` as the `kiso roles` command group.
- [x] Implement `kiso roles list` (columns: name, model,
  override flag, description).
- [x] Implement `kiso roles show <name>` (resolved prompt
  + 2-line header with model, source, entry point).
- [x] Implement `kiso roles diff <name>` (unified diff
  user vs bundled, or "no user override").
- [x] Implement `kiso roles reset <name>` delegating to
  the existing `cli.role.role_reset` path.
- [x] Keep the singular `kiso role reset` form working as
  a deprecated alias for one cycle, no warning yet.
- [x] Add help text mentioning that the singular form is
  deprecated (via inline comment in build_parser).
- [x] Unit test: every `_MODEL_METADATA` model_key has a
  registry entry; every registry entry has a non-empty
  description and a `prompt_filename` matching an actual
  file under `kiso/roles/`.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles list` lists every registry
  role with the expected default model each.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles list` marks `user override`
  when the user-dir file differs from bundle, empty when
  it matches.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles show <name>` prefers user
  override when present, falls back to bundled.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles diff <name>` returns "no user
  override" with no override, unified diff with one.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles reset <name>` overwrites the
  override with the bundled default.
- [x] CLI test: `kiso roles show nonexistent` exits
  non-zero with stderr error.
- [x] CLI test: singular `kiso role reset` still parses
  (deprecated alias preserved).

### M1293 — Roles naming alignment (Python ↔ files) ✅

**Problem.** The audit on 2026-04-09 found that role
filenames and Python entry points have drifted in ways
that add cognitive overhead when navigating the brain
package:

- `worker.md` → `run_exec_translator()` in
  `kiso/brain/text_roles.py`. The function name is the
  *implementation* (it translates a task description into
  a shell command), but the role name on the user side is
  `worker`. Worse, `kiso/worker/` is also a *module* in
  the codebase (the actual task executor / event loop
  owner), so "worker" means two different things depending
  on which directory you're in.
- `classifier.md` → `classify_message()` in `common.py`,
  not `run_classifier()`.
- `inflight-classifier.md` → `classify_inflight()`, not
  `run_inflight_classifier()`.
- `summarizer-session.md` is the only summarizer in
  existence; the `-session` suffix is dead context that
  never got the sibling it implied.

**Goal.** Bring Python function names in line with role
filenames, and rename `summarizer-session.md` to
`summarizer.md`, with automatic migration for any user
who already has a custom override.

**Approach.**

- **User-facing rename: `summarizer-session.md` →
  `summarizer.md`.** Update the bundled file under
  `kiso/brain/roles/`. Update the registry entry from
  M1292. Add a one-shot migration in the role-loading
  code path: at first access, if `~/.kiso/roles/` contains
  a `summarizer-session.md` and no `summarizer.md`,
  rename the file in place; if both exist, leave both,
  log a warning, and prefer `summarizer.md`. The
  migration is idempotent and runs at most once per file.
- **Python rename: `run_exec_translator` → `run_worker`**
  in `kiso/brain/text_roles.py`. Update all call sites
  (search the worker loop, exec handler, and any test
  imports). Note: this does **not** rename the
  `kiso/worker/` module — that one keeps its name. The
  goal is not to remove the word "worker" from the code,
  it's to make the role-name → function-name mapping
  obvious. The remaining ambiguity ("which worker?") is
  resolved by package path.
- **Python rename: `classify_message` → `run_classifier`,
  `classify_inflight` → `run_inflight_classifier`** in
  `kiso/brain/common.py`. Update all call sites.
- **Do NOT rename:** `build_planner_messages()` keeps its
  name. It does not call the LLM; it assembles the
  modular planner prompt for downstream consumers. The
  `run_*` convention is reserved for functions that
  actually invoke the role.
- **Do NOT introduce shims or aliases** for the Python
  renames. They are internal symbols. A clean rename + a
  green test suite is the migration.
- **Do NOT rename `worker.md` itself.** The user-facing
  filename already matches the role name as the user
  thinks of it. The drift was on the Python side.

**Migration risk and mitigation.**

- The summarizer file rename touches user state. The
  in-place migration covers existing installations;
  M1292's `kiso roles list` will reflect the new name
  the first time it runs after the upgrade.
- The Python renames are internal-only and have zero
  user-visible effect, but break in-tree imports until
  every call site is updated. Done as a single coherent
  change set, not split across commits.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Rename bundled file
  `kiso/roles/summarizer-session.md` → `summarizer.md`.
- [x] Update the M1292 registry entry for the summarizer
  role to use the new filename and `name="summarizer"`.
- [x] Add an idempotent in-place migration
  (`_migrate_summarizer_session_role`) in `kiso/main.py`,
  invoked from `_init_kiso_dirs` before the additive
  bundled-roles copy.
- [x] Rename `run_exec_translator` → `run_worker` in
  `kiso/brain/text_roles.py`. In `kiso/worker/loop.py`,
  import via `from kiso.brain import run_worker as
  run_worker_role` to avoid clashing with the long-lived
  `kiso.worker.loop.run_worker` session loop.
- [x] Rename `classify_message` → `run_classifier` in
  `kiso/brain/common.py` and update every call site.
- [x] Rename `classify_inflight` →
  `run_inflight_classifier` in `kiso/brain/common.py`
  and update every call site
  (`kiso/main.py`, `kiso/api/sessions.py`, all consumer
  tests).
- [x] Confirmed `build_planner_messages` left untouched
  (does not call the LLM directly).
- [x] Confirmed `kiso/worker/loop.py:run_worker` (the
  session loop) and `kiso.worker` package are untouched;
  the brain function lives at `kiso.brain.run_worker`.
- [x] Unit test for the summarizer migration happy path
  (only old file → renamed in place).
- [x] Unit test for the conflict case (both files → both
  kept, `summarizer.md` wins, warning logged).
- [x] Unit test for noop on `summarizer.md` only and on
  empty dir; idempotency test.
- [x] Grep-guard tests: no `run_exec_translator`,
  `classify_message`, `classify_inflight`, or
  `summarizer-session` references in `kiso/` source
  outside the migration helper itself.
- [x] Updated M1292's registry tests to assert the
  summarizer role is named `summarizer`.
- [x] Updated `tests/test_import_surfaces.py` expected
  `kiso.brain` exports.
- [x] Updated `tests/test_prompts.py` core-terms table.
- [x] Updated `tests/test_worker.py` patch targets
  (`kiso.worker.loop.run_worker_role`,
  `kiso.worker.loop.run_classifier`).
- [x] Updated live test imports
  (`tests/live/test_flows.py`,
  `tests/live/test_roles.py`); verified collection.
- [x] Full unit suite regression: 4134 tests passed.

### M1294 — `classifier` vs `inflight-classifier` consolidation review ✅

**Status: investigation only.** No code changes are part
of this milestone — the deliverable is a written decision
appended to this milestone, plus a follow-up milestone
*if and only if* the investigation concludes that
consolidation is the right move. If the conclusion is
"keep them separate", that decision is recorded here and
the milestone closes without code.

**Problem.** Two roles classify user messages:
`classifier.md` (initial routing into `plan`,
`investigate`, `chat_kb`, `chat`) and
`inflight-classifier.md` (in-flight routing for messages
that arrive while a task is already running:
`stop`/`update`/`independent`/`conflict`). Both default
to `gemini-2.5-flash`. They live in different files, are
loaded by different functions, and are documented in two
places. It is not obvious whether the duplication is
load-bearing or accidental.

**What to investigate.**

- Read both prompts in full. Quantify how much text is
  shared (intro framing, output schema framing, examples
  framing) vs. how much is genuinely phase-specific
  (initial categories vs. inflight categories).
- Check whether the two functions share any helper code
  in `common.py` that could become the shared substrate
  if the prompts are merged.
- Consider whether merging behind a `phase=initial|inflight`
  parameter would: (a) reduce maintenance cost, (b) risk
  cross-contamination of categories, (c) make the prompt
  too long to stay in the same model's optimal range.
- Check whether the inflight categories are stable enough
  that they belong in the same prompt, or whether they
  are likely to diverge further (e.g., new
  `pause`/`resume` categories on the inflight side that
  would have no analogue on the initial side).

**Decision criteria.**

- **Merge** if: shared framing >60% of total prompt, no
  cross-contamination risk visible in the existing
  categories, and the merged prompt fits comfortably in
  the existing budget.
- **Keep separate** if: phase-specific text dominates,
  there is plausible drift between the two category sets
  in the next cycle, or the merged prompt would push the
  classifier into a slower or more expensive model.
- **Default to "keep separate"** if the investigation is
  inconclusive. The current setup works; consolidation
  is a quality-of-life refactor, not a bug fix.

**Deliverable.** A written conclusion appended to this
milestone in the devplan, with the percentages and the
decision. If the decision is "merge", a follow-up
milestone (e.g. `M1295`) is added to v0.9-wip.md or to
the next cycle, depending on remaining v0.9 budget. The
follow-up is **not** auto-created; it is proposed to the
user first.

**Tasks.**

- [ ] Read `classifier.md` and `inflight-classifier.md`
  in full and quantify the percentage of shared framing
  vs phase-specific text.
- [ ] Review `classify_message` and `classify_inflight`
  in `kiso/brain/common.py` for shared helper code that
  could become a common substrate.
- [ ] Evaluate merge feasibility behind a
  `phase=initial|inflight` parameter against the three
  risk dimensions (maintenance, cross-contamination,
  prompt size/model fit).
- [ ] Assess drift likelihood for inflight-only
  categories (e.g. potential `pause`/`resume`) over the
  next cycle.
- [ ] Apply the decision criteria (merge if shared >60%
  and no contamination risk and prompt fits; default to
  keep separate if inconclusive).
- [ ] Append the written decision to this milestone with
  the measured percentages.
- [ ] If the decision is "merge", propose a follow-up
  milestone (e.g. `M1295`) to the user before adding it
  to the devplan.

**Test.** None. This milestone closes when the written
decision is in the devplan.

**Investigation conclusion (2026-04-09).**

Read both prompts in full and quantified the structural
overlap:

| Metric | `classifier.md` | `inflight-classifier.md` |
|---|---|---|
| Bytes | 3959 | 585 |
| Lines | 34 | 10 |
| Categories | 4 (plan / investigate / chat_kb / chat) | 4 (stop / update / independent / conflict) |
| Output format | `cat:Language` | bare `cat` |
| Language detection | yes | no |
| Entity / Known-Entities disambiguation | yes | no |
| Recent-conversation disambiguation rules | yes (5+ rules) | no (just templated injection) |
| Boundary rules (plan↔investigate, etc.) | yes (10+ rules) | no |
| Templated `{...}` substitutions | no — built in Python | yes (`{plan_goal}`, `{new_message}`, `{recent_conversation}`) |

**Word-for-word shared text: well below 5%.** The two
prompts have zero category overlap and only generic
phrases like "Classify" / "Respond with ONLY..." in
common. The shared framing budget required to consider a
merge per the milestone criteria was 60%; we are roughly
an order of magnitude below that.

**Code-level sharing.** Both functions
(`run_classifier`, `run_inflight_classifier`) call
`call_llm(config, "classifier", ...)` with the same
model key, so they already share the model assignment
via `_MODEL_METADATA` (one source of truth, set during
the M1213 upgrade). The message-construction helpers
(`build_classifier_messages` vs
`build_inflight_classifier_messages`) are separate.
There is no helper code that could become a shared
substrate beyond what is already shared at the
`call_llm` layer.

**Drift likelihood.** The initial classifier already
evolved this cycle: M1290 added the 4th category
`investigate`, M1291 added the empty-KB pre-flight
fallback. The inflight classifier categories have not
changed since they were introduced. There is plausible
future drift on both sides (e.g. inflight could grow a
`pause` / `resume` category once long-running jobs land)
but **independently** — there is no scenario where one
side's evolution constrains the other.

**Decision: KEEP SEPARATE.**

Reasons, in order of weight:

1. **Cross-contamination risk dominates.** Merging
   would mean a single prompt that the LLM has to
   route into 8 categories (4 initial + 4 inflight)
   based on a `phase` parameter. That is strictly
   worse for classifier accuracy than the current 4+4
   split, where each prompt has exactly the choices
   that apply to its phase. Fewer categories per
   call = fewer plausible mistakes.
2. **Output format divergence.** Initial returns
   `cat:Language`, inflight returns bare `cat`.
   Merging requires either a more complex output
   schema or branching post-processing — both add
   failure modes for zero benefit.
3. **Templated vs message-constructed.** Inflight
   uses string substitution (`{plan_goal}` etc.);
   initial uses Python-side message assembly. Merging
   requires picking one mechanism and rewriting the
   other.
4. **Shared framing far below the 60% threshold** that
   the milestone criteria established as the bar for
   merge.
5. **The default decision when inconclusive was "keep
   separate"**, and this analysis is not even
   inconclusive — it actively favors keeping them
   separate.

**No follow-up milestone proposed.** The two roles
deserve to stay separate. They already share the
expensive thing (the model assignment) and nothing
else needs to be shared. The duplication in
`__brain_exports__` and the slight maintenance cost of
two `.md` files is negligible compared to the cost of
merging.

**Optional polish (not part of this milestone, will
flag separately if user wants it):** add a one-line
note at the top of each `.md` cross-referencing the
sibling role and explaining the deliberate separation,
so future maintainers do not re-investigate this from
scratch.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Read `classifier.md` and `inflight-classifier.md`
  in full and quantify the percentage of shared framing
  vs phase-specific text (table above; <5% shared).
- [x] Review `run_classifier` and `run_inflight_classifier`
  in `kiso/brain/common.py` for shared helper code that
  could become a common substrate (none beyond
  `call_llm` model-key sharing already in place).
- [x] Evaluate merge feasibility behind a
  `phase=initial|inflight` parameter against the three
  risk dimensions (maintenance — neutral;
  cross-contamination — negative; prompt size/model
  fit — would push the merged prompt to ~4.5KB which
  still fits, but offers no real benefit).
- [x] Assess drift likelihood for inflight-only
  categories (independent drift on both sides; no
  shared evolution pressure).
- [x] Apply the decision criteria: shared <60% AND
  cross-contamination risk → keep separate.
- [x] Append the written decision to this milestone
  with the measured percentages (above).
- [x] No follow-up milestone proposed; investigation
  closes here.

## Phase 15 — Subprocess cancellation cleanup hygiene (M1295)

### M1295 — Reap subprocess on `wait_for(communicate(), timeout)` cleanup at 4 call sites ✅

> **Diagnosis correction (2026-04-09).** The original M1295 body
> hypothesised the bug was in `_run_subprocess`'s cancel branch
> (the `for t in pending: t.cancel()` race in
> `kiso/worker/utils.py`). When TDD red-phase tests were written
> against that hypothesis, **both the FD-leak test and the
> whitebox spy test on the cancelled `pending` set passed without
> any code change.** That falsified the original diagnosis. The
> real bug is described below; the original analysis is preserved
> verbatim further down for the audit trail.

**Problem.** Running the full unit suite under `xdist` produces a
recurring noisy traceback near the 100% mark:

```
Loop <_UnixSelectorEventLoop running=False closed=True ...> that handles pid 68407 is closed
Exception ignored in: <function BaseSubprocessTransport.__del__ ...>
  ...
  File ".../base_events.py", line 545, in _check_closed
    raise RuntimeError('Event loop is closed')
RuntimeError: Event loop is closed
```

The tests **all pass**. The traceback fires at GC time after the
event loop has been closed, so it does not break a single test, but:

- it pollutes test output and can mask real warnings;
- it indicates the asyncio child-watcher is holding stale PID
  references between tests;
- it gets worse over time as the suite grows.

**Real root cause (verified 2026-04-09 after the original
hypothesis was falsified by red tests).** The bug is **not** in
`_run_subprocess`. That function correctly calls `_kill_proc(proc)`
in the cancel branch, which does `proc.terminate()` followed by
`await proc.wait()` — the OS process is reaped and the child
watcher slot is released. Whitebox spy tests on the `pending` set
confirm the cancelled `comm_task` ends up in `done()` state by
the time `_run_subprocess` returns (the `await _kill_proc(proc)`
yields to the loop, which then drives the cancellation to
completion).

The actual bug is in **four other call sites** that wrap
`proc.communicate()` in `asyncio.wait_for(...)` and silently
swallow `TimeoutError` without killing or reaping the
subprocess:

1. `kiso/hooks.py:48-67` — `run_pre_exec_hooks`:

   ```python
   try:
       proc = await asyncio.create_subprocess_shell(...)
       stdout, stderr = await asyncio.wait_for(
           proc.communicate(context.encode()),
           timeout=_HOOK_TIMEOUT,
       )
       ...
   except asyncio.TimeoutError:
       log.warning("Pre-exec hook timed out after %ds, "
                   "allowing execution", _HOOK_TIMEOUT)
   # ← proc is NOT terminated, NOT awaited.
   #   The child process keeps running. The
   #   _UnixSubprocessTransport stays alive holding the pipes.
   #   The child watcher still has a callback registered for
   #   the PID. All three leak until process exit.
   ```

2. `kiso/hooks.py:95-107` — `run_post_exec_hooks`: same pattern,
   same swallow.

3. `kiso/tool_repair.py:61-80` — `repair_unhealthy_tools`: same
   `wait_for(proc.communicate(), timeout=...)` followed by
   `except asyncio.TimeoutError: log.warning(...)` with no
   cleanup.

4. `kiso/tool_repair.py:145-164` — `rerun_all_deps`: same pattern.

When any of these timeouts fires, `wait_for` cancels the inner
`proc.communicate()` coroutine, the StreamReaders abort their
reads, the transport survives in memory holding pipe FDs and
a registered child callback. Later, when the test (or the
process) exits and the event loop closes, the orphan transport
is GC'd; its `__del__` calls `self.close()` →
`proto.pipe.close()` → `_loop.call_soon(...)` → `_check_closed()`
→ `RuntimeError: Event loop is closed`. Same chain for the
`Loop ... that handles pid X is closed` warning emitted by
`SafeChildWatcher` for the un-released callback.

**Verified by direct code inspection** of all
`asyncio.create_subprocess_*` call sites in `kiso/`:

| Site | Pattern | Leaks? |
|---|---|---|
| `kiso/worker/utils.py:_run_subprocess` (cancel branch) | `wait` + `_kill_proc` | No — proc is killed and awaited |
| `kiso/worker/utils.py:_run_subprocess` (no-cancel branch) | direct `await proc.communicate(...)` | No — communicate awaits wait |
| `kiso/hooks.py:run_pre_exec_hooks` | `wait_for(communicate(), timeout)` + bare `except` | **Yes** |
| `kiso/hooks.py:run_post_exec_hooks` | same | **Yes** |
| `kiso/tool_repair.py:repair_unhealthy_tools` | same | **Yes** |
| `kiso/tool_repair.py:rerun_all_deps` | same | **Yes** |
| `kiso/brain/text_roles.py:run_worker` (bash -n syntax check) | direct `await proc.communicate(...)` (no wait_for) | No |

**Fix.** Introduce a small private helper in a new
`kiso/_subprocess_utils.py` module:

```python
async def communicate_with_timeout(
    proc: asyncio.subprocess.Process,
    input_bytes: bytes | None,
    timeout: float,
) -> tuple[bytes, bytes]:
    """Like ``await asyncio.wait_for(proc.communicate(input), timeout)``
    but kills + reaps the subprocess on timeout so the
    ``_UnixSubprocessTransport`` and the child watcher slot are
    released before the function returns.

    Re-raises ``asyncio.TimeoutError`` after cleanup so callers
    can handle it normally.
    """
    try:
        return await asyncio.wait_for(
            proc.communicate(input_bytes), timeout=timeout,
        )
    except asyncio.TimeoutError:
        try:
            proc.kill()
        except ProcessLookupError:
            pass
        try:
            await proc.wait()
        except BaseException:
            pass
        raise
```

A new top-level module is the cleanest home: `kiso/hooks.py` and
`kiso/tool_repair.py` cannot import from `kiso/worker/utils.py`
without risking dependency cycles, and inlining the same 8 lines
4 times is worse for maintenance.

Then update each call site:

- `kiso/hooks.py:run_pre_exec_hooks` — replace
  `await asyncio.wait_for(proc.communicate(...), timeout=...)`
  with `await communicate_with_timeout(proc, ..., _HOOK_TIMEOUT)`.
- `kiso/hooks.py:run_post_exec_hooks` — same.
- `kiso/tool_repair.py:repair_unhealthy_tools` — same.
- `kiso/tool_repair.py:rerun_all_deps` — same.

Each call site keeps its existing `except asyncio.TimeoutError:`
block — the `TimeoutError` is still raised by the helper, just
after cleanup. Behavior on the success path is identical.

**Why kill + wait, not terminate + wait_for grace + kill:** the
hook / repair scripts that timed out are already past their
budget. There is no "give it 5 more seconds to clean up
gracefully" — the budget was the budget. SIGKILL guarantees the
process exits and `proc.wait()` returns promptly without a
second timeout layer. `_run_subprocess`'s `_kill_proc` uses the
SIGTERM → grace → SIGKILL escalation because exec tasks may have
side effects worth flushing; hook/repair processes are
short-lived utilities that do not.

**Why `_run_subprocess` is NOT touched:** verified by two failed
red-phase tests (`test_cancel_does_not_leak_file_descriptors`
and `test_cancel_drains_pending_communicate_task`). The
`_kill_proc` call inside the cancel branch already drains the
cancelled `comm_task` by virtue of yielding to the loop during
`await proc.wait()`. The `_run_subprocess` cancel path is clean.

**Boundary — what this milestone does NOT do.**

- Does NOT change `_run_subprocess` or `_kill_proc`. They are
  correct as written.
- Does NOT change the public contract of `run_pre_exec_hooks`,
  `run_post_exec_hooks`, `repair_unhealthy_tools`, or
  `rerun_all_deps`. Each function still raises (and catches)
  `asyncio.TimeoutError` exactly as today; the only change is
  that the underlying subprocess is reaped before the
  `TimeoutError` reaches the `except` block.
- Does NOT add a new public API. `communicate_with_timeout` is
  module-private (no `__all__`, name not exported).
- Does NOT touch `kiso/brain/text_roles.py` — its `bash -n`
  syntax check uses direct `await proc.communicate(...)` with
  no `wait_for`, so no leak.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Create `kiso/_subprocess_utils.py` with the
  `communicate_with_timeout(proc, input_bytes, timeout)`
  helper. Module-private; no public API.
- [x] Helper uses a manual `asyncio.wait` race
  (communicate vs sleep) instead of `wait_for`. On
  timeout it killpgs the entire process group, **drains
  the comm_task naturally** (rather than cancelling it),
  then awaits proc.wait() — this avoids the
  half-suspended StreamReader pattern that made the
  earlier `wait_for + cancel + kill` approach hang for
  the full natural sleep duration.
- [x] Add private `_kill_process_group(proc)` helper that
  uses `os.killpg(os.getpgid(proc.pid), SIGKILL)` with a
  safety check that we never killpg our own process
  group.
- [x] Update `kiso/hooks.py:run_pre_exec_hooks` to use
  the helper AND pass `start_new_session=True` so the
  spawned shell is its own process-group leader.
- [x] Update `kiso/hooks.py:run_post_exec_hooks` to use
  the helper AND pass `start_new_session=True`.
- [x] Update `kiso/tool_repair.py:repair_unhealthy_tools`
  to use the helper AND pass `start_new_session=True`.
- [x] Update `kiso/tool_repair.py:rerun_all_deps` to use
  the helper AND pass `start_new_session=True`. (Same
  `replace_all` covered both tool_repair sites since
  they share the same exec invocation pattern.)
- [x] Add unit tests in `tests/test_subprocess_utils.py`
  (new, 6 tests): happy-path with stdin, happy-path with
  DEVNULL stdin, happy-path with input_bytes, timeout
  reaps proc, timeout reaps when input_bytes pending,
  already-dead proc no-op.
- [x] Add `tests/test_hooks.py::TestPreExecHooks::test_pre_hook_timeout_reaps_subprocess`
  — OS-level proof via `os.kill(pid, 0)` that the spawned
  hook PID is gone after `run_pre_exec_hooks` returns.
- [x] Add `tests/test_hooks.py::TestPostExecHooks::test_post_hook_timeout_reaps_subprocess`
  — same for the post-exec path.
- [x] Verify existing hooks tests still pass: 18/18 in
  `tests/test_hooks.py`.
- [x] Add `tests/test_worker.py::TestRunSubprocessCancel::test_cancel_branch_leaves_pending_task_done`
  as a regression-keeper for `_run_subprocess` (proves
  that the existing `_kill_proc` flow already drains
  the cancelled comm_task; documents that
  `_run_subprocess` is NOT a leak source).
- [x] Run full unit suite under xdist: 4147 passing
  (was 4138 + 9 new tests). The
  `Exception ignored in: BaseSubprocessTransport.__del__`
  / `Loop ... is closed` traces from the previous
  baseline are GONE.
- [x] Run integration suite: 58/58 passing.
- [x] Document the M1295 invariant in
  `docs/architecture.md` (subprocess timeouts are
  self-cleaning via `communicate_with_timeout` + must
  use `start_new_session=True`).

**Out of scope for v0.9** (flag separately if it ever becomes a
real problem):

- Switching from `SafeChildWatcher` to `PidfdChildWatcher`
  globally. That would also eliminate the watcher-related
  warnings on Linux ≥5.3, but it is a runtime-config change with
  broader implications and is independent of this fix.
- Auditing every `asyncio.wait_for` usage in the codebase for
  the same class of cancel-without-drain bug. If M1295 fixes
  the symptom, that audit can wait for a future cycle; if it
  doesn't, we revisit then.

## Phase 16 — M1289 loader resilience (M1296)

### M1296 — Self-heal `_load_system_prompt` + refactor `_init_kiso_dirs`

**Problem.** Running the full test matrix on HEAD reports:

```
✓ Unit tests        4134 passed
✓ Bash tests          89 passed
✓ Integration         58 passed
✓ Docker              10 passed
✓ Plugin               9 passed
✗ Live tests          17 failed, 45 passed
✗ Functional tests    36 failed, 3 skipped
✗ Extended tests       9 failed, 2 skipped
```

Every failure has the same signature:

```
FileNotFoundError: Role file not found at <KISO_DIR>/roles/<role>.md.
Run `kiso role reset <role>` to restore from the package.
```

The error message is the one introduced by **M1289**
(`kiso/brain/prompts.py:_load_system_prompt`). v0.8 closed
green at M1266 because the loader had a package fallback;
M1289 deliberately removed that fallback to enforce
"user dir = single source of truth at runtime", and the
test infrastructure was only partially updated.

**Verified root cause (2026-04-09).** Compared
`kiso/brain/prompts.py` at commit `6131e0c` (M1266 / v0.8
close) vs HEAD:

- v0.8:

  ```python
  user_path = KISO_DIR / "roles" / f"{role}.md"
  if user_path.exists():
      return user_path.read_text()
  pkg_path = _ROLES_DIR / f"{role}.md"   # ← package fallback
  if pkg_path.exists():
      return pkg_path.read_text()
  raise FileNotFoundError(...)
  ```

- HEAD (post-M1289):

  ```python
  user_path = KISO_DIR / "roles" / f"{role}.md"
  if not user_path.exists():
      raise FileNotFoundError(
          f"Role file not found at {user_path}. "
          f"Run `kiso role reset {role}` to restore from the package."
      )
  return user_path.read_text()
  ```

M1289 added the session-scoped fixture
`tests/conftest.py::_populated_user_roles_dir` to keep the
4134-test unit suite green. M1289 did **not** update:

1. **`tests/functional/conftest.py:_func_kiso_dir`**
   (lines 426-462) — creates an isolated `kiso_dir` with
   `tools/` and `sys/ssh/` subdirs and patches `KISO_DIR` on
   13 modules including `kiso.brain`, but **never copies the
   bundled roles** into it. Every functional test that loads
   a role hits FileNotFoundError → 36 fails.
2. **18 per-test `with patch("kiso.brain.KISO_DIR", tmp_path):`
   sites** in
   `tests/live/test_e2e.py` (2),
   `tests/live/test_flows.py` (4),
   `tests/live/test_practical.py` (7),
   `tests/live/test_roles.py` (5).
   Each of these patches `KISO_DIR` to a fresh empty `tmp_path`
   without populating `roles/` → 17 live fails. Pre-M1289 these
   patches worked because the loader fell back to the package.
3. **9 per-test `patch("kiso.brain.KISO_DIR", tmp_path)` sites**
   in `tests/test_brain.py` (lines 880, 950, 954, 964, 975,
   979, 2355, 3410, 3429). These currently still pass — likely
   because the session fixture primes `_prompt_cache` early and
   the cache survives the per-test re-patches in the same
   xdist worker — but they are fragile and should be made
   explicit too.
4. **`tests/functional/conftest.py:TestF14CuratorEntityCreation`**
   (extended tier) is the only failure with a different surface
   message ("No entity matching 'python'"). Same root cause one
   layer down: the curator pipeline raises FileNotFoundError on
   role load, the helper at `kiso/worker/message_flow.py:372`
   swallows it via `try/except`, and the test fails on a
   downstream assertion ("no facts found"). Fixing #1 above
   resolves this too.

M1289's commit message reports "Full unit suite: 4079 passing"
and does not mention live/functional/extended. The breakage
landed on Apr 8 and went unnoticed until the full matrix was
run on 2026-04-09. M1290–M1294 did not touch any of the
affected files.

**Three options considered.**

- **A** — Fix only the test infrastructure: add a `populate_roles_in()`
  helper and call it from every conftest / per-test patch site that
  creates an isolated KISO_DIR. ~50 lines of test code. Preserves
  M1289 invariant exactly. Cons: every future test that creates a
  fresh KISO_DIR has to remember the helper or it fails the same
  way again. Long-term fragile.
- **B** — Restore the package fallback in `_load_system_prompt`
  (revert M1289 partially). One-file change. Tests just work. Cons:
  re-opens the "two sources of truth" trap M1289 was designed to
  close. A corrupted user file would be silently shadowed by the
  bundled default and the user would not notice. Unacceptable.
- **C — Self-heal in the loader (chosen).** When
  `_load_system_prompt` finds the user file missing or empty, copy
  the bundled default into the user dir atomically, log a WARNING,
  then read. The user dir remains the runtime source of truth — the
  bundle is the seed, not an alternate read path. Same mechanism
  `_init_kiso_dirs()` already implements at boot, just deferred to
  first access.

**Why C wins long-term.**

1. **Production resilience.** Today, if a role file is deleted or
   truncated AT RUNTIME (after the boot-time copy in
   `_init_kiso_dirs`), kiso dies on the next LLM call with a
   FileNotFoundError. The error message says "Run `kiso role reset
   NAME`" but that assumes a CLI is reachable — useless for hosted
   deployments, containers without exec access, read-only volumes,
   or sessions where a user simply cannot be at the terminal. With
   self-heal the server keeps working, the warning lands in the
   logs, and an operator can investigate at their leisure instead
   of being paged at 3 AM.
2. **Single source of truth preserved.** After self-heal, the user
   dir IS the only place the loader reads from. The bundle is the
   factory default that seeds the user dir on first access. This
   is exactly the M1289 contract — the only thing that changes is
   WHEN the seeding happens (lazy at first access vs eager at
   boot). Both paths converge on the same end state.
3. **Test infrastructure becomes trivial.** With self-heal in the
   loader, the 18 per-test patches in tests/live/* and the
   `_func_kiso_dir` functional fixture do not need to populate
   roles. The first time the loader is called during a test, it
   self-heals into whatever tmp dir is currently patched as
   `KISO_DIR`. Tests pass for the same reason production passes:
   the loader is defensive. **Zero ongoing maintenance burden** on
   future tests.
4. **Future-proof.** When a future milestone adds a new bundled
   role, the test infrastructure adapts automatically because
   self-heal copies whatever is in the bundle. Option A would
   require updating the helper every time the bundle changes.
5. **Coherence with the rest of the kiso resilience story.** The
   reset CLI, the boot-time copy, the audit trail, the
   user-dir-ownership story — all of them stay coherent. We just
   add one more layer: graceful degradation at the loader level.

**Trade-off accepted.** If a user customized a role and then
deletes the file (intentionally or by mistake), self-heal silently
restores the bundled default. The user loses their customization.
Mitigation: log a WARNING with the role name and the user dir
path. The warning is also clear about what was lost ("Any previous
customization is gone"). This is strictly better than M1289 (where
the same scenario kills the server) and strictly worse than a
hypothetical option that requires manual confirmation (which
defeats the resilience goal). Net: the warning is the right
balance.

**Implementation plan (Option C).**

Step 1 — refactor `kiso/main.py:_init_kiso_dirs`. Extract a
private helper `_populate_kiso_dir(target: Path)` that does:

- Create the standard subdirs (`tools`, `connectors`, `recipes`,
  `sessions`, `roles`, `sys/ssh`, `reference`).
- Run `_migrate_summarizer_session_role(target / "roles")` (M1293).
- Copy bundled roles (additive, never overwrites non-empty user
  files — same logic as today).
- Sync bundled reference docs (same logic as today).

`_init_kiso_dirs()` becomes `_populate_kiso_dir(KISO_DIR)` plus
the SSH key generation step that is production-only. Behavior
identical to today; the refactor only extracts a unit of work
that the loader and the test fixtures can both call.

Step 2 — add self-heal to `kiso/brain/prompts.py:_load_system_prompt`.
New behavior:

```python
def _load_system_prompt(role: str) -> str:
    if role in _prompt_cache:
        return _prompt_cache[role]
    user_path = KISO_DIR / "roles" / f"{role}.md"
    if not user_path.exists() or user_path.stat().st_size == 0:
        # Self-heal: seed the user dir from the bundled default
        # (the same way _init_kiso_dirs does at boot, but
        # deferred to first access). Logs a WARNING so operators
        # see when self-heal kicks in.
        pkg_path = _ROLES_DIR / f"{role}.md"
        if not pkg_path.exists():
            raise FileNotFoundError(
                f"Role file '{role}' missing from both user dir "
                f"({user_path}) and package bundle ({pkg_path}). "
                f"The kiso installation may be corrupted; reinstall."
            )
        _self_heal_role(user_path, pkg_path, role)
    text = user_path.read_text()
    _prompt_cache[role] = text
    return text


def _self_heal_role(user_path: Path, pkg_path: Path, role: str) -> None:
    """Atomically copy pkg_path → user_path and log a warning."""
    user_path.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    bundled_text = pkg_path.read_text(encoding="utf-8")
    tmp_path = user_path.with_suffix(user_path.suffix + ".tmp")
    tmp_path.write_text(bundled_text, encoding="utf-8")
    tmp_path.replace(user_path)  # atomic on POSIX
    log.warning(
        "Self-healed role '%s' from bundled default into %s. "
        "Any previous customization is lost; restore from backup if needed.",
        role, user_path,
    )
```

Notes:
- Atomic write via tmp + rename — concurrent self-heal from two
  workers cannot produce a partially written file.
- The empty-file case (`stat().st_size == 0`) is treated as
  "needs heal" because an empty system prompt is undefined LLM
  behavior. This matches the M1289 `_init_kiso_dirs` self-heal
  convention (`if not target.exists() or target.stat().st_size == 0`).
- Cache after self-heal contains the bundled content; subsequent
  calls hit the cache.
- The reset CLI hint in the FileNotFoundError now applies only
  to the truly catastrophic case where the package bundle itself
  is missing.

Step 3 — simplify the existing test infrastructure. The session
fixture `tests/conftest.py::_populated_user_roles_dir` no longer
needs to inline the copy loop because the loader self-heals on
first access. We KEEP the patch (so unit tests don't accidentally
write to the developer's real `~/.kiso/`), but drop the eager copy.
The patch alone is enough; the loader does the rest.

Step 4 — confirm zero changes needed to:

- `tests/functional/conftest.py:_func_kiso_dir` — patches KISO_DIR
  on 13 modules; the loader will self-heal on first access into
  the patched dir.
- `tests/live/test_e2e.py`, `test_flows.py`, `test_practical.py`,
  `test_roles.py` — 18 per-test `patch("kiso.brain.KISO_DIR",
  tmp_path)` sites. The loader self-heals into `tmp_path` on
  first access, no test changes required.
- `tests/test_brain.py` — 9 per-test patches. Same story.

Step 5 — new unit tests for self-heal. Add a class
`TestLoadSystemPromptSelfHeal` to `tests/test_brain.py` (or
wherever `TestLoadSystemPrompt` lives) covering:

- Happy path: empty user dir → first call self-heals → file
  exists in user dir afterward → content matches bundle.
- Existing user override is preferred: user file with custom
  content → loader returns custom content, does NOT touch the
  file.
- Empty user file is treated as missing: zero-byte file →
  loader self-heals → file is no longer empty.
- Cache hit after self-heal: second call does NOT re-read the
  file (verify via patching `read_text`).
- Warning is logged on self-heal (capture via `caplog`).
- Atomic write: simulate concurrent self-heal by patching
  `Path.write_text` to verify the tmp + rename pattern.
- Bundle missing → FileNotFoundError with the
  "kiso installation may be corrupted" message.

Step 6 — verification. Run the full test matrix and confirm:

- 4134 unit tests still pass + new self-heal tests pass.
- 89 bash + 58 integration + 10 docker + 9 plugin still pass.
- **62 live + functional + extended tests now pass.**
- No new warnings in any suite output OTHER than the
  intentional self-heal warnings during the very first test
  in each xdist worker (which is expected and acceptable —
  it shows self-heal is doing its job).

**Boundary — what this milestone does NOT do.**

- Does NOT change the production runtime contract. After self-heal,
  the user dir is still authoritative for every subsequent read.
- Does NOT touch `cli/role.py` or `cli/roles.py`. The reset CLI
  is unchanged.
- Does NOT touch `kiso/api/*`, the worker, the planner, the
  classifier, or any other consumer of `_load_system_prompt`. The
  function signature and successful-call behavior are identical
  to today; only the missing-file path changes.
- Does NOT introduce a new module or a new public API. The
  `_populate_kiso_dir` and `_self_heal_role` helpers are
  module-private.
- Does NOT add a CI gate that runs the live + functional matrix
  on every commit. That is a separate (much bigger) decision and
  should be tracked independently.

**Tasks.**

- [x] Refactor `kiso/main.py:_init_kiso_dirs` to extract a private
  `_populate_kiso_dir(target: Path)` helper that handles subdir
  creation, summarizer migration (M1293), bundled role copy, and
  reference doc sync. `_init_kiso_dirs()` becomes
  `_populate_kiso_dir(KISO_DIR)` plus `_init_ssh_keys()`.
- [x] Verify the existing M1289 + M1288 init tests
  (`tests/test_main.py::TestInitKisoDirs`) still pass after the
  refactor (4138 unit tests green).
- [x] Add `_self_heal_role(user_path, pkg_path, role)` private
  helper to `kiso/brain/prompts.py`. Atomic tmp + rename. Logs
  a WARNING with the role name, the user dir path, and the
  "customization is lost" notice.
- [x] Update `_load_system_prompt` to invoke `_self_heal_role`
  when the user file is missing or empty. Raise FileNotFoundError
  ONLY when the package bundle is also missing (real
  installation corruption).
- [x] Added a logger to `kiso/brain/prompts.py`
  (`log = logging.getLogger(__name__)`).
- [x] Simplify `tests/conftest.py::_populated_user_roles_dir`
  → renamed to `_isolated_kiso_dir`: drop the inline copy
  loop. Keep only the tmp dir creation and the
  `kiso.brain.KISO_DIR` patch.
- [x] Verify NO changes are needed to
  `tests/functional/conftest.py:_func_kiso_dir`,
  `tests/live/test_e2e.py`, `tests/live/test_flows.py`,
  `tests/live/test_practical.py`, `tests/live/test_roles.py`,
  or any per-test patch in `tests/test_brain.py`. Confirmed by
  the regression sims `test_functional_fixture_pattern_self_heals`
  and `test_live_fixture_pattern_self_heals`.
- [x] Add new unit tests in `tests/test_brain.py::TestLoadSystemPrompt`
  for the self-heal contract: happy path, existing override
  preference, empty file treatment, atomic write, bundle
  missing raises.
- [x] Add deterministic regression simulations
  `test_functional_fixture_pattern_self_heals` and
  `test_live_fixture_pattern_self_heals` that mirror the exact
  failure mode of the 62 fails reported in the M1296 problem
  statement (replicate the multi-module patch and per-test
  patch patterns, assert the loader self-heals).
- [x] Run the full unit suite under xdist and confirm 4138
  passing (was 4134 + 4 new regression and self-heal tests).
- [x] Run the integration suite (58 passing).
- [ ] User to run the full matrix
  (`./utils/run_tests.sh a` or equivalent with
  `--functional --extended --llm-live` and a real
  `KISO_LLM_API_KEY`) and confirm the 62 previously-failing
  live + functional + extended tests are now green. The
  unit-level regression sims above prove the loader contract
  is correct deterministically; the matrix run confirms the
  end-to-end LLM path with self-heal.
- [x] Add docstring notes in `_load_system_prompt`,
  `_self_heal_role`, `_populate_kiso_dir`, and
  `_init_kiso_dirs` explaining the lazy/eager seeding
  relationship.

**Out of scope.**

- Does NOT add a "freeze" mode where the loader refuses to
  self-heal (e.g., a `KISO_STRICT_ROLES=1` env var). Could
  be added later if a user wants the M1289 behavior back for
  paranoid deployments. Not needed for v0.9.
- Does NOT add a backup mechanism that preserves the previous
  customization before self-heal (writes the missing file to
  `*.lost` for forensic recovery). Could be a future
  enhancement; not needed for v0.9.
- Does NOT add an audit-trail entry for self-heal events. The
  log warning is enough for v0.9; promoting it to audit can
  happen later if operators want to track it.
- Does NOT change `kiso role reset` or `kiso roles reset`. The
  CLI commands remain the way to deliberately restore the
  bundled default.
- Does NOT add a CI workflow to run the live/functional/extended
  matrix on every push. Separate decision, separate milestone.

**Why this happened in the first place (post-mortem,
non-actionable).** M1289 changed a runtime contract and verified
only the unit suite. The live + functional + extended suites are
gated behind opt-in pytest flags (`--llm-live`, `--functional`,
`--extended`) because they are slow and expensive, so they were
not part of the M1289 validation path. The breakage landed on Apr
8 and was latent for one day until the full matrix was run on
2026-04-09. **Lesson for future contract changes:** when a
runtime contract change touches anything the test infrastructure
mocks or patches (KISO_DIR, config loading, DB layer, network),
the author must either run the full matrix manually before
commit, or update every conftest + fixture that interacts with
the changed contract — AND favor self-healing designs over
hard-fail designs whenever the failure mode is recoverable from
local state. M1296 corrects M1289 along the second axis: the
loader is now self-healing, so the same mistake cannot recur in
the same way.

## Phase 17 — Documentation backfill and polish (M1297-M1298, retroactive)

These two milestones were executed during the M1294 commits but
were bundled into M1294 instead of being captured as discrete
milestones. They are documented here retroactively (per user
request 2026-04-09) so the devplan history matches what
actually shipped. Both are already merged on `main` — the work
is **not** pending; this section is purely a backfill so the
audit trail is complete.

### M1297 — Documentation refresh: roles UX, classifier, flow, CLI ✅

**Problem (in retrospect).** M1291–M1294 added substantial
user-visible changes (chat_kb fallback, `kiso roles` CLI, 12-role
registry, naming alignment, inflight-classifier review) but the
docs were stale: `docs/llm-roles.md` still described the
classifier as a 2-category role (`plan`/`chat`), still referenced
`summarizer-session.md` and a non-existent `summarizer-facts.md`,
still called the worker role "Exec Translator", and the `kiso
roles` CLI surface was undocumented anywhere. `docs/cli.md` had
no Role Management section. `docs/architecture.md` did not
mention the registry. `docs/flow.md` had no description of the
classifier dispatch. `docs/safety.md` referenced
`classify_inflight()` (renamed in M1293). The docs would not
have helped anyone trying to understand the v0.9 changes.

**Approach.** Comprehensive sweep across 5 doc files in a single
pass, executed during the M1294 commit (`9b56afa`).

**Files touched.**

- `docs/llm-roles.md`:
  - New introduction "Why kiso splits work into roles" with the
    cost / accuracy / debuggability / extensibility framing.
  - New "Discovering roles" section pointing at the `kiso roles`
    CLI and the `roles_registry.py` single source of truth.
  - Classifier section rewritten end-to-end: 4 categories, full
    boundary rules table, M1291 chat_kb empty-retrieval pre-flight
    explanation including the trade-off rationale.
  - New Inflight Classifier section with the M1294 conclusion
    ("deliberately separate from classifier, see M1294").
  - "Exec Translator" section renamed to "Worker" with a
    naming note explaining the M1293 alignment and the
    `kiso.worker` vs `kiso.brain.run_worker` disambiguation.
  - "Worker (Messenger)" section renamed to "Messenger".
  - Summarizer section: removed the stale
    `summarizer-facts.md` reference, updated path to
    `kiso/roles/summarizer.md`, mentioned the M1293
    in-place migration helper.
  - New Consolidator section (was missing entirely).
  - Context-per-role table column headers updated to match
    the new role names.
- `docs/cli.md`:
  - New "Role Management" section documenting `kiso roles
    list / show / diff / reset`, the registry, and the
    deprecated singular `kiso role` alias.
- `docs/architecture.md`:
  - "Explicit phase boundaries" section expanded with the

**Ship state.** Merged in commit `9b56afa` (2026-04-09) bundled
with M1294. No tests required (documentation only). No
production code touched.

### M1298 — Cross-reference comments in classifier.md and inflight-classifier.md ✅

**Problem (in retrospect).** M1294 concluded that
`classifier.md` and `inflight-classifier.md` should stay
separate (zero category overlap, merging hurts accuracy). But
the bundled `.md` files themselves had no on-file marker
explaining the deliberate separation, so a future maintainer
investigating "should we consolidate these?" would have to
re-do the M1294 analysis from scratch.

**Approach.** Add a one-line HTML comment at the top of each
of the two role files cross-referencing the sibling and pointing
at M1294 in the devplan. HTML comments are read by the LLM as
part of the system prompt but framed as meta — at ~30 tokens
per call on `gemini-2.5-flash` the cost is negligible. The
comment fires before the actual instructions so it does not
shift the model's attention from the categorization task.

**Files touched.**

- `kiso/roles/classifier.md`: added the maintainer note at
  the top.
- `kiso/roles/inflight-classifier.md`: added the matching
  maintainer note at the top.

**Ship state.** Merged in commit `4ee2e4c` (2026-04-09).
Verified all 1046 unit tests in the relevant files
(test_prompts, test_brain, test_inflight, test_chat_kb,
test_cli_roles) still passed after the comment additions.
