### Phase 20d: Functional regressions discovered during M1306-M1319

49. [x] **M1321** — Manual: create `kiso-run/wrapper-ocr` GitHub repo ✅

    **Why:** During M1312 push, 6/7 wrapper repos pushed successfully.
    `kiso-run/wrapper-ocr` does not exist on GitHub and the push
    failed with "repository not found". The other 6 already existed
    (from earlier manual setup, presumably).

    **Approach:** Admin must create the empty repo on GitHub, then
    push from local checkout.

    **Tasks:**
    - [ ] Admin creates empty `kiso-run/wrapper-ocr` repo on GitHub
    - [ ] From `/tmp/wrapper-repos/ocr`: `git push new-origin HEAD:main --force`
    - [ ] Verify `kiso wrapper install ocr` works end-to-end

    **Done when:** repo exists at github.com/kiso-run/wrapper-ocr,
    push succeeded, install works.

50. [x] **M1322** — Fix `kiso wrapper inspect` hallucination in planner ✅

    **Investigation:** Searched `kiso/roles/` and `docs/cli.md` —
    no occurrence of "wrapper inspect". The LLM hallucinated it from
    "Self-inspection" (line 20) or "Reviewer inspects" (line 51).

    **Fix:** Added explicit constraint to `kiso/roles/planner.md`
    line 93: "(NO `inspect` — these are the only 6 valid subcommands)".
    Also fixed leftover `Tools:` → `Wrappers:` heading and
    `--tools` → `--wrappers` flag in user mgmt example.

    Note: this is a soft fix (LLM still might hallucinate). A hard
    fix would be to validate exec commands against the known valid
    subcommands list, but that's out of scope for this milestone.

51. [x] **M1323** — Investigate integration test errors (45 errors) ✅

    **Root cause:** `tests/integration/conftest.py:49` had
    `tools = "*"` in the fixture TOML config. After M1307 the config
    parser requires `wrappers = "*"`. Single line fix; all 58
    integration tests now pass.

52. [x] **M1324** — Investigate plugin tests failures (8 failed) ✅

    **Root causes (3):**
    1. Wrapper repos not pushed (resolved by M1312/M1321)
    2. Stale test_manifest.py in 4 repos (aider, browser, moltbook,
       websearch) checked `data["kiso"]["tool"]` instead of
       `data["kiso"]["wrapper"]`
    3. Test fixture parameter mismatch in websearch: `def test(...,
       run_tool, ...)` parameter still used old name even though the
       fixture function is `run_wrapper`

    **Fix:** Updated all wrapper repos with correct test_manifest.py
    and run_tool→run_wrapper parameter renames. Pushed changes.

    **Result:** 9/9 plugin tests pass (749 tests across 9 plugins).

53. [ ] **M1325** — Investigate `TestMultiTurnLearning` chat_kb regression

    **Why:** `TestMultiTurnLearning.test_learning_retention` fails
    because the user saves a fact ("uso Flask 3.0 con SQLAlchemy") and
    later asks for it back, but the chat_kb pre-flight returns empty
    and falls back to investigate, which then fails to retrieve the
    fact. This may be related to M1305 project isolation, or to
    keyword-matching after the rename, or to a curator categorization
    bug.

    **Tasks:**
    - [ ] Reproduce locally with a minimal test case
    - [ ] Check what `category` the curator assigns to the saved fact
    - [ ] Check if `chat_kb_preflight` keyword matching is finding it
    - [ ] Check if project_id filter (M1305) is excluding it
    - [ ] Identify root cause and fix
    - [x] Re-run F23 cross-session knowledge tests to ensure no regression

    **Investigation done in M1320 session (deeper):**
    - Reproduced `search_facts_scored` with exact fact + query keywords
      + same session: **returns 1 result correctly**. Store layer fine.
    - `tests/functional/conftest.py:567` does `await bg_task` before
      message 2 starts → race condition theory ruled out.
    - Pre-flight code in `loop.py:333` and promotion code in
      `loop.py:411` use IDENTICAL keyword extraction logic.
    - **Real bug pattern:** failure log shows BOTH:
      (a) `chat_kb pre-flight empty → falling back to investigate`
      (b) `Plan validation failed: kb_answer is set but plan contains
          action tasks (found: ['exec', 'replan'])`
      → The planner LLM produces `kb_answer=true` AND action tasks
      simultaneously, which is invalid. Validation correctly rejects.
    - Hypothesis: the curator categorizes the saved fact with
      `category="user"` and `session=other-session-uuid` (not the
      current one) for some reason, OR the keyword extraction
      tokenizer differs from what FTS5 indexed.
    - Cannot reproduce without LLM credits.

    **Done when:** F-multi-turn learning test passes; cross-session
    knowledge tests still pass.

54. [x] **M1326** — Fix live suite collection: broken TOML literal in `test_practical.py` ✅

    **Why:** The live suite fails at collection with
    `SyntaxError: unexpected character after line continuation
    character` at `tests/live/test_practical.py:428`. The line
    `[kiso.wrapper.args.text]\n'` is missing the opening single
    quote — it should be `'[kiso.wrapper.args.text]\n'`. Refuso
    lasciato da uno dei pass di rename `tool → wrapper/skill`
    (M1314-M1320): la sostituzione meccanica ha toccato quella riga
    e ha mangiato l'apice iniziale. Effetto: **tutta** la suite
    `tests/live/` è non-collezionabile (50 test), non solo quello.

    **Approach:** Fix puntuale al letterale Python, nessuna logica
    coinvolta. Dopo la fix verificare con `uv run pytest
    tests/live/test_practical.py --collect-only` che la collection
    passi, poi `./utils/run_tests.sh l` per la suite live completa.

    **Tasks:**
    - [x] Correggere `tests/live/test_practical.py:428` aggiungendo
          l'apice di apertura mancante
    - [x] `uv run pytest tests/live/test_practical.py --collect-only`
          → 0 errors
    - [x] Grep su `tests/` per altre righe TOML-in-Python con lo
          stesso pattern (`^\s+\[kiso\..*\\n'$`) → 0 matches.
          Le occorrenze in `tests/test_presets.py` sono dentro
          `dedent("""...""")`, legali.
    - [x] Commit & push

    **Done when:** `tests/live/` collezziona senza errori; eventuali
    altri refusi dello stesso tipo corretti o confermati assenti.

    **Result:** `tests/live/` collezziona 62 test in 0.08s, 0 errors.

55. [x] **M1327** — Messenger must cite exec output values verbatim ✅

    **Why:** `TestF24CreateThenReference.test_create_file_then_reference`
    fallisce perché il messenger, dato lo stdout di `wc` = `1  2 11
    hello.txt`, produce "ci sono **1** parola" invece di riportare
    il valore corretto (2 parole). Il test è un canary: il bug
    generale è che **il messenger riformula liberamente i valori
    numerici/testuali prodotti da un exec task invece di citarli
    verbatim**. Questo tocca qualsiasi use case "riferisci il
    risultato di un comando" — conteggi, dimensioni, versioni,
    valori letti da file, output di CLI tool, ecc.

    **Approach:**

    *Step 1 — diagnosi (senza toccare codice):* verificare cosa
    riceve effettivamente il messenger nel briefing del plan che
    fallisce. Il log dice `Briefer for messenger: ... 1
    output_indices` → capire se lo stdout completo dell'exec task
    arriva al prompt del messenger o se viene troncato/riassunto
    dal briefer. Se i dati non ci sono, il fix deve stare nel
    briefing. Se ci sono, il fix sta nel prompt messenger.

    *Step 2 — fix strutturale nel punto giusto:*
    - Se il briefing non include stdout completo dei task
      referenziati → estendere il briefer per garantire che
      `output_indices` preservi l'output verbatim (non un riassunto).
    - Se il briefing è ok → rinforzare `kiso/roles/messenger.md`
      con una regola generale del tipo "quando il goal chiede un
      risultato specifico (valore, conteggio, contenuto), cita i
      valori esatti presenti nell'output dei task referenziati;
      non inventare etichette o riformulare numeri". Regola
      generalista, non una casistica sul `wc`.

    *Step 3 — validazione:* rilanciare F24 ripetutamente (LLM-driven
    → non deterministico, serve vedere se il fix riduce la varianza).

    **Root cause found (not briefer-side, not prompt-side):**
    il bug era in `kiso/worker/replan.py::_format_plan_outputs_for_msg`.
    Quando il reviewer produceva un `reviewer_summary`, il codice
    sostituiva **completamente** il raw stdout con il summary prima
    di passarlo al messenger:

    ```python
    if result.reviewer_summary:
        output = f"Summary: {result.reviewer_summary}"
    else:
        output = result.output or "(no output)"
    ```

    Il messenger non vedeva mai il ground truth di `wc` (`1  2 11
    hello.txt`) — vedeva solo il summary del reviewer, che è un
    altro LLM che poteva riassumere male. Catena LLM→LLM senza
    accesso al ground truth nel secondo anello. Problema generale,
    non specifico a wc: vale per qualsiasi exec con output
    deterministico piccolo (versioni, conteggi, valori letti da
    file, output CLI).

    **Fix:** invertire la priorità. Il raw output è sempre primario
    quando entra nel budget (8000 char). Il `reviewer_summary`
    diventa fallback solo nel branch oversized (quando il raw è
    troppo grande per il budget), coerente con il suo scopo
    originale di gestire output di search HTML rumorosi da 50KB+.

    Due test esistenti encodavano il comportamento rotto come
    contract (`test_prefers_reviewer_summary_over_raw_output`,
    `test_mixed_with_and_without_summary` a
    `tests/test_worker.py:2769-2806`). Riscritti per riflettere
    il nuovo contract + aggiunto
    `test_oversized_raw_falls_back_to_reviewer_summary` per coprire
    il caso fallback.

    **Tasks:**
    - [x] Ispezionare la catena briefing → messenger per capire
          dove si perde il ground truth → localizzato in
          `_format_plan_outputs_for_msg`
    - [x] Aggiornare i test unit in
          `tests/test_worker.py::TestFormatPlanOutputsForMsg` per
          encodare il nuovo contract (raw-primary)
    - [x] Implementare il fix in `kiso/worker/replan.py:40`
    - [x] Verificare no regression su unit suite (4213 passed)
    - [ ] Rilanciare `TestF24CreateThenReference` su suite
          functional (richiede LLM credits — manuale)
    - [x] Commit & push

    **Done when:** F24 passa stabilmente; il raw output è preservato
    verbatim lungo tutta la catena task→messenger per output che
    entrano nel budget; il summary fa solo da fallback.
    F24 stesso è LLM-driven e richiede run manuale per validazione
    end-to-end, ma la root cause strutturale è risolta.

56. [x] **M1328** — Stop leaking `reviewer.reason` into user-visible replan messages ✅

    **Why:** `TestFRulesPathDisclosure.test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`
    fallisce perché il template user-visible
    `Replanning (attempt N/M): <reviewer.reason>` interpola verbatim
    il `reason` prodotto dal reviewer, che è un LLM in modalità
    diagnostica libera. In questo run il reason conteneva "the
    command itself failed to execute properly" e il conftest blocca
    qualsiasi failure language nell'output utente.

    Il problema è **generale**, non legato alla path disclosure:
    il `reviewer.reason` è metadata interno (stile diagnostico,
    spesso in EN anche in sessioni IT, può contenere dettagli
    tecnici, path, command, nomi file, failure language) e non
    dovrebbe mai raggiungere l'utente così com'è. Qui è venuto
    fuori come "failure language" ma la stessa classe di leak
    può includere path sensibili, errori interni, ecc.

    La safety rule che blocca i path assoluti (secondo replan →
    `stuck`) funziona correttamente: il test fallisce **prima**,
    sul primo replan, per il leak del reason.

    **Approach (opzione b — structural minimal):** rimuovere
    l'interpolazione del `reviewer.reason` dal template user-visible
    del replan. Il reason resta:
    - nei log (`kiso.brain.reviewer` logger) per debug
    - nel record del plan/task per audit
    - disponibile per il planner del replan (è lui che deve
      reagire al reason, non l'utente)

    L'utente continua a vedere "Replanning (attempt N/M)…" senza
    il reason. Non si aggiungono chiamate LLM, non si introduce
    nuova superficie di fallimento, non si rompono altri casi
    d'uso. Scartata l'alternativa di far riformulare il reason
    al messenger: aggiunge latenza/costo su ogni replan e delega
    a un LLM la responsabilità di sanitizzare dati sensibili.

    **Implementation:** i template erano centralizzati in
    `kiso/worker/replan.py::_REPLAN_TEMPLATES` e interpolavano
    `{reason}` (e `{tried}` per il template `stuck`) direttamente
    nella stringa user-visible. Fix:
    - `"replanning"` ora è `"Replanning (attempt {depth}/{max})"` —
      nessun reason.
    - `"stuck"` ora è `"I'm having trouble with this request. I've
      tried replanning {depth} times without success. Can you help
      me with more details or a different approach?"` — nessun
      reason, nessun tried.
    - `get_replan_message()` continua ad accettare `reason` e
      `tried` come parametri per backward-compat con i call site,
      ma non li interpola nell'output.

    Il reviewer reason resta disponibile:
    - in log a `kiso/brain/reviewer.py:320`
      (`log.info("Review: status=%s reason=%s", ...)`)
    - nel contesto del planner del replan via `replan_reason` in
      `kiso/worker/loop.py` (linee 2503, 2613, ecc.), dove guida
      il nuovo piano senza raggiungere l'utente
    - nel record `plan_output` per audit

    **Tasks:**
    - [x] Localizzato il template in
          `kiso/worker/replan.py:_REPLAN_TEMPLATES`
    - [x] Rimosso `{reason}` da `replanning` e `{reason}`/`{tried}`
          da `stuck`
    - [x] Verificato che `reviewer.reason` continua nei log e nel
          planner context
    - [x] Test update: `TestM332GetReplanMessage` riscritto per
          encodare il nuovo contract (raw/forbidden subs),
          aggiunti `test_replanning_does_not_leak_failure_language`
          e `test_stuck_does_not_leak_failure_language` con input
          avversariali (path, "failed to")
    - [x] Test update: `test_replan_notification_saved` e
          `test_stuck_message_on_similar_failures` erano asserting
          il vecchio contract (reason nel messaggio), aggiornati
          per verificare l'assenza del leak
    - [x] Full unit regression: 4214 passed, 1 fail preesistente
          non correlato (`test_supervisor.py::test_sigterm_stops_supervisor`
          — cerca un file `/tmp/.../connector.log` che non esiste,
          verificato anche su `main` prima dei miei cambi)
    - [x] Commit & push

    **Done when:** nessun punto del codice interpola
    `reviewer.reason` in messaggi destinati all'utente finale;
    il reason resta nei log e nel context del planner;
    `TestFRulesPathDisclosure.test_safety_rule_blocks_paths` non
    può più fallire per leak di failure language da reviewer reason
    (validazione end-to-end richiede LLM credits per re-run F-rules).

57. [x] **M1329** — `drive_install_flow` skip redundant re-run when wrapper was already installed ✅

    **Why:** the shared functional helper
    `drive_install_flow` at
    `tests/functional/conftest.py:674-719` executes the
    user prompt **twice** whenever the wrapper is already
    installed at the first check. Current shape:

    ```python
    result = await run_message(prompt, **kwargs)           # call 1
    turns_used = 1
    while not tool_installed(wrapper_name) and turns_used < max_turns:
        result = await run_message("sì, installa il wrapper X", **kwargs)
        turns_used += 1
    if tool_installed(wrapper_name):
        result = await run_message(prompt, **kwargs)       # call 2 — redundant
    return result
    ```

    The second call exists for the install-happened case:
    turn 1 is the original request (planner proposes
    install), turns 2..N are "sì installa" approvals, and
    the final re-issue runs the prompt with the wrapper now
    available. When the wrapper is **already** installed at
    turn 1, the loop is skipped but the final re-issue still
    runs, duplicating the work.

    **Impact.** Each `drive_install_flow` call with an
    already-installed wrapper costs one extra full plan
    (classifier → briefer → planner → tasks → reviewer →
    messenger → knowledge promotion = 6-8 LLM calls). F17
    calls `drive_install_flow` three times (browser, ocr,
    aider) — when all three are already installed from
    earlier tests, that's 3 extra plans per run. Visible in
    the 2026-04-12 post-M1325 failure log of
    `TestF17FullPipeline`: Plan 1 and Plan 2 have the
    identical goal "Navigate to ... take a screenshot"
    because the helper re-issued the prompt. F30 and other
    pipeline tests that use the same helper are equally
    affected.

    This is a **test helper inefficiency**, not a bug in
    install flow routing or in any production code. M1286
    introduced `drive_install_flow` to consolidate robust
    install-loop handling; the double-run in case A was an
    accepted simplification at the time. This milestone
    cleans it up.

    **Relation to M1302.** Independent. M1302 investigates
    whether pipeline timeouts are H1 (budget), H2 (code
    bug), or H3 (provider flake). M1329 reduces the plan
    count of these tests regardless of the verdict, making
    the budget tighter and the tests cheaper to run. M1329
    may incidentally remove the symptom if the real cause
    was H1; it will NOT mask H2 or H3 (the remaining 4
    plans still exercise the same code paths and call the
    same providers).

    **Approach.**

    Short-circuit the second `run_message` in case A: if
    `tool_installed(wrapper_name)` was already true **at
    the start** (before turn 1), the first call executed
    the prompt with the wrapper available, and the result
    is already the canonical one — return it without
    re-issuing. Only re-issue when the install actually
    happened inside the while loop.

    Pseudocode:

    ```python
    preinstalled = tool_installed(wrapper_name)
    result = await run_message(prompt, **kwargs)
    if preinstalled:
        return result
    turns_used = 1
    while not tool_installed(wrapper_name) and turns_used < max_turns:
        result = await run_message(f"sì, installa il wrapper {wrapper_name}", **kwargs)
        turns_used += 1
    if tool_installed(wrapper_name):
        result = await run_message(prompt, **kwargs)   # real re-issue post-install
    return result
    ```

    No behavior change for the install-needed path; the
    already-installed path now avoids the duplicate.

    **Discovery during implementation.** The existing unit
    test `TestDriveInstallFlow.test_tool_already_installed_returns_after_first_call`
    in `tests/functional/test_helpers.py:404` was asserting
    the old (broken) behavior with `assert calls == ["do
    something", "do something"]`. But the **class docstring**
    at `test_helpers.py:394-395` already stated the correct
    intent: "if wrapper already installed when called, sends
    prompt once and returns". The code and the assertion had
    diverged from the stated intent since M1286. M1329 aligns
    all three.

    **Tasks:**
    - [x] Modify `drive_install_flow` in
          `tests/functional/conftest.py` to snapshot
          `tool_installed(wrapper_name)` before turn 1 and
          short-circuit on preinstalled (4-line change,
          added `preinstalled = tool_installed(...)` before
          the first `run_message` and `if preinstalled:
          return result` after it)
    - [x] Update `test_tool_already_installed_returns_after_first_call`
          to assert `calls == ["do something"]` (new contract)
          with explanatory M1329 docstring
    - [x] Verify other 5 tests in `TestDriveInstallFlow`
          still pass unchanged (they cover install-happened
          and never-installs paths, unaffected)
    - [x] Grep caller sites (`test_browser.py`,
          `test_multitool.py`) — none depend on the
          double-run side effect; they only check the
          final result
    - [x] Full unit suite: 4215 passed, 9 skipped (up from
          4213 — the delta is the helper test class which is
          now correctly encoding the new contract)
    - [x] Integration suite: 59 passed, 58 skipped
    - [x] Commit & push — functional/extended run-time
          validation deferred to next LLM-credit run

    **Done when:** `drive_install_flow` runs the prompt
    exactly once when the wrapper is already installed, and
    exactly N+1 times (one per install turn + one final
    re-issue) when the install actually happens. No
    callers are broken. ✅

58. [x] **M1330** — Remove `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion`: classifier is the authoritative semantic judge ✅

    **Problem.** `TestF24CreateThenReference.test_create_file_then_reference`
    failed on the 2026-04-12 post-M1329 full-matrix run with:

    ```
    assert 'hello.txt' in "ho trovato l'informazione nella mia
    knowledge base — rispondo direttamente.

    quante parole ci sono nel file che hai appena creato?"
    ```

    The messenger echoed the user's question back prefixed by
    the chat_kb "found it in KB" preamble, meaning the KB fast
    path fired but had no actual answer.

    Trace from the log: classifier said `investigate:Italian`,
    then `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion` at
    `kiso/worker/loop.py:411` fired with `KB has 1 match(es) →
    fast path`, the planner was skipped, and the messenger was
    called with a KB fact that contained the meta-information
    "user created hello.txt" but nothing about word count. The
    messenger had no real answer to produce.

    **Why it fires.** The promotion gate at
    `loop.py:448-472` requires:
    1. `_looks_like_question(content)` — True (has `?`)
    2. NOT `_has_imperative_prefix(content)` — True ("quante"
       is a question word, not an imperative verb)
    3. `search_facts_scored(keywords=content.lower().split()[:10])`
       returns ≥1 match

    The keyword list `[quante, parole, ci, sono, nel, file, che,
    hai, appena, creato]` overlaps with any curator-stored fact
    about `hello.txt` (words like `file`, `creato` are common).
    The KB hit is a structural lexical match, not a semantic
    answer match. The message is then promoted from
    `investigate` to `chat_kb` and the planner never runs.

    **Structural root cause.** The promotion inverts the
    evidence hierarchy:

    - The classifier does full-message semantic reasoning via
      an LLM to decide `plan` / `investigate` / `chat_kb`.
    - The promotion pre-flight does grep-level keyword
      matching on the facts store.
    - Keyword matching then *overrides* the semantic judgment.

    Overriding a higher-evidence signal (LLM semantic
    classification) with a lower-evidence signal (substring
    overlap) is architecturally backwards. The symmetric
    fallback (`_chat_kb_preflight_fallback` at `loop.py:333`)
    does not have this problem: it only *refines* the
    classifier's decision when its precondition (KB has
    answers) is not met, falling back to the safer path
    (planner). The fallback safety-nets the classifier; the
    promotion contradicts it.

    The specific F24 case — session has workspace files and
    the question asks a quantitative property of one of them —
    is only the most visible instance. The same bug class can
    manifest any time a curator-stored meta-fact has lexical
    overlap with a compute-requiring question, regardless of
    whether the session has files or the question has specific
    quantitative words. Any language- or state-specific gate
    would only narrow the bug, not eliminate it.

    **Fix: remove `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion` and its
    invocation site entirely.** The classifier becomes the
    single authoritative semantic judge for
    `plan`/`investigate`/`chat_kb` routing. The
    `_chat_kb_preflight_fallback` safety net is kept intact
    (it is directionally safe: classifier says chat_kb, but KB
    is empty, so fall back to planner). The
    `Fast path: chat_kb message, skipping planner` code path at
    `loop.py:2859` is still reachable via the classifier's
    direct `chat_kb` decision; only the plan→chat_kb override
    is removed.

    The planner is also already kb-aware via the `kb_answer`
    flag path introduced in M1303 — when a message classified
    `plan`/`investigate` is in fact fully answerable from KB,
    the planner can produce a single-msg `kb_answer=true`
    plan. The decision is made by the planner LLM with full
    context (message, session state, memory pack), not by
    substring matching. This is the correct location for that
    judgment.

    **Properties of the fix.**

    - **Structural, not a heuristic.** No keyword lists, no
      language-specific rules, no state-based gates. The fix
      is a *deletion* that restores the correct evidence
      hierarchy.
    - **Generalist.** Fixes F24 and the entire class of
      false-positive promotions, including cases not yet seen
      (different languages, different KB fact shapes,
      different question forms).
    - **Safe direction.** Every message that would have been
      promoted now goes through the planner instead. The
      planner can still route to a kb-only answer via
      `kb_answer=true`. The worst-case regression is
      additional LLM cost for a subset of messages that the
      promotion would previously have short-circuited — but
      the classifier's decision is the authoritative one, so
      the planner's judgment is strictly at-least-as-correct.
    - **No impact on F23.** Cross-session knowledge tests
      rely on the classifier going straight to `chat_kb` and
      on `_chat_kb_preflight_fallback` handling the empty-KB
      case. Neither path involves `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion`.
    - **No impact on `_chat_kb_preflight_fallback`.** The
      fallback is kept. Only the promotion is removed.

    **Risk mitigation.** Before removing, inspect:

    1. All call sites of `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion`
       in `kiso/worker/loop.py` and adjacent modules.
    2. All tests in `tests/` that reference the function,
       the `plan→chat_kb promotion` log string, or
       `_PLAN_TO_CHAT_KB_PROMOTE_MSGS`.
    3. Any functional test that expects a plan→chat_kb
       transition to appear as a user-visible msg task.

    If the investigation surfaces a legitimate user-visible
    feature that depends on the promotion (unlikely — the
    user-visible artifact is a transition msg like "I already
    know this, replying directly", and the same feel is
    achievable via the classifier's direct chat_kb path), the
    fallback plan is:

    - **Plan B:** keep `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion`
      but add a workspace-state gate at the top —
      `if _session_workspace_has_files(session): return
      False`. This narrows the failure surface to sessions
      without files, which still leaves some false positives
      open but fixes F24 immediately. Strictly less
      generalist than Plan A.

    The investigation is part of the milestone; the decision
    between Plan A (remove) and Plan B (gate) is recorded in
    the devplan at completion, with the evidence that drove
    it.

    **Investigation outcome: Plan A taken.** Grep confirmed
    the promotion function had a single call site in the
    worker loop dispatcher and all its supporting helpers
    (`_looks_like_question`, `_has_imperative_prefix`,
    `_PLAN_PROMOTE_QUESTION_PREFIXES`,
    `_PLAN_PROMOTE_IMPERATIVE_PREFIXES`,
    `_PLAN_TO_CHAT_KB_PROMOTE_MSGS`) were used exclusively
    by the promotion itself. Tests were consolidated in a
    single class `TestPlanChatKbPromotion` in
    `tests/test_chat_kb.py`. No production code outside the
    promotion path depended on these symbols. Plan B (gate
    with workspace-state check) was not needed — clean Plan A
    removal was feasible without risk of orphaned references.

    **Tasks.**

    - [x] Grep call sites of
          `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion` in
          `kiso/worker/loop.py` and the rest of `kiso/`
          → exactly one call site, in the worker loop
          dispatcher around line 2854
    - [x] Grep tests referencing the function or its
          related strings → all in
          `tests/test_chat_kb.py::TestPlanChatKbPromotion`
    - [x] Decided Plan A (full removal) based on the grep
          evidence: no other consumers
    - [x] Deleted `_plan_chat_kb_preflight_promotion`,
          `_PLAN_TO_CHAT_KB_PROMOTE_MSGS`,
          `_has_imperative_prefix`, `_looks_like_question`,
          `_PLAN_PROMOTE_QUESTION_PREFIXES`,
          `_PLAN_PROMOTE_IMPERATIVE_PREFIXES` from
          `kiso/worker/loop.py`
    - [x] Deleted the call site in the worker loop
          dispatcher
    - [x] Removed `TestPlanChatKbPromotion` entirely from
          `tests/test_chat_kb.py` and replaced with
          `TestClassifierIsAuthoritative`, a guard test
          that asserts the removed symbols do NOT exist in
          `kiso.worker.loop` — this locks in the contract
          so a future refactor cannot silently re-introduce
          the evidence-hierarchy inversion bug. A second
          test confirms the symmetric
          `_chat_kb_preflight_fallback` and
          `_CHAT_KB_FALLBACK_MSGS` are still present (they
          are directionally safe and kept)
    - [x] Scrubbed the orphaned milestone-reference comment
          `M1291: chat_kb pre-flight...` in the dispatcher
          and replaced with a timeless description of what
          the safety net does and why
    - [x] Full unit regression: 4204 passed, 9 skipped
    - [x] Integration suite: 34 passed, 58 skipped
    - [x] `tests/test_chat_kb.py`: 34 passed
    - [x] Commit & push; functional F24 re-run deferred to
          next LLM-credit suite run

    **Done when.** F24 no longer false-positives on the
    session-with-file / compute-question / KB-lexical-match
    combination. F23 and other chat_kb tests pass unchanged.
    The promotion is fully removed. ✅

59. [x] **M1331** — Retry aider on OpenRouter per-request cap with provider-reported affordable max_tokens ✅

    **Note.** This milestone describes the fix to be
    implemented in the `kiso-run/plugins/wrapper-aider` repo.
    It is tracked here because it was discovered and
    diagnosed from kiso-run/core functional test failures
    (`TestF17FullPipeline::test_screenshot_ocr_aider_exec_msg`,
    `TestF29AiderWriteCode::test_aider_write_script`) and
    must land before those tests can be validated green.
    The actual implementation happens in a separate repo
    with its own DEVPLAN.md entry.

    **Problem.** Two functional failures on the 2026-04-12
    post-M1329 run share a single root cause:

    - `TestF17FullPipeline.test_screenshot_ocr_aider_exec_msg`
      failed with
      `AssertionError: Plan 3 should stay codegen-only, got:
      ['exec', 'msg']`. Log trace shows aider failing with
      `OpenrouterException - This request requires more
      credits, or fewer max_tokens. You requested up to
      64000 tokens, but can only afford 49423`, followed by
      kiso replan falling back to an exec task that writes
      the file via `cat > heredoc`. The replan fallback is
      structurally correct (the final artifact is produced),
      but the test's codegen-only assertion does not
      tolerate it.

    - `TestF29AiderWriteCode.test_aider_write_script` timed
      out with `asyncio.timeouts.py:115: TimeoutError`. Log
      trace shows the same OpenRouter error, but this time
      the replan keeps retrying aider (since the goal
      explicitly requires aider) and each retry hits the
      same 402 until the test timeout fires.

    **Not credits exhaustion.** The user's OpenRouter
    balance is positive. The error is a per-request
    affordability cap: OpenRouter enforces
    `max_tokens_per_request ≤ balance / per_token_cost`. For
    high-max-output models (Claude Sonnet 4.x, etc., with
    `max_output_tokens = 64000`) on moderate balances, a
    single request that asks for the model's full max output
    exceeds what the current balance funds in one call, so
    OpenRouter rejects with 402 and a very specific message
    including the affordable ceiling: `can only afford
    49423`.

    **Why aider requests 64000.** Aider reads
    `max_output_tokens` from the model's litellm settings
    (at `aider/resources/model-settings.yml` or the
    model's provider config) and passes it as `max_tokens`
    on every completion call. It does not know about the
    balance-dependent per-request cap, and its built-in
    retry loop retries with the same `max_tokens`, so 402
    errors loop forever until the outer timeout fires.

    **Fix (wrapper-aider, not core).** Detect the specific
    OpenRouter 402 "can only afford N" error in aider's
    stderr. Parse N with a deterministic regex
    (`can only afford (\d+)`). Retry aider **exactly once**
    with `max_tokens` capped to N, using aider's native
    mechanism for overriding per-model settings (likely a
    temporary `--model-settings-file` with a YAML override,
    to be confirmed during implementation).

    **Properties of the fix.**

    - **Structural.** The cap value comes from the provider's
      own error message, not from a hard-coded constant or a
      guess. It is the exact ceiling OpenRouter reports as
      affordable at this balance + model combination.
    - **Respects `feedback_max_tokens_truncation.md`.** That
      policy forbids setting *artificial* max_tokens caps.
      Here the cap is not artificial — it is the provider's
      explicitly stated affordable ceiling. Accepting a
      provider-declared limit is not the same as inventing
      one.
    - **Deterministic, no heuristics.** Regex parse on a
      stable OpenRouter error string. If the format changes
      and the regex fails to match, the code falls through
      to the existing error path with no regression.
    - **One retry only.** No retry storm, no loop.
    - **Zero impact on the successful path.** The parser
      and retry branch only fire when the aider exit is
      non-zero AND stderr matches the OpenRouter 402 format.
    - **Scope confined to `wrapper-aider`.** No changes in
      kiso-run/core. F17 and F29 are fixed transitively
      because aider no longer fails, so there is no replan
      fallback to exec (F17 Plan 3 stays codegen-only) and
      no timeout loop (F29 completes).
    - **Generalist.** Any OpenRouter call from aider that
      hits the per-request cap now adapts automatically,
      regardless of which model, which balance, or which
      request. Not overfitted to F17 or F29.

    **Risk and fallback.** The fix assumes aider has a CLI
    / config mechanism to override `max_tokens` per-run.
    Verification is part of the implementation. If aider
    does not expose such a mechanism in the installed
    version, the fallback options, in order of preference,
    are:

    1. Write a temporary `model-settings.yml` with the
       current model + `max_tokens: N` and pass it via
       `--model-settings-file` — this is the most likely
       supported path.
    2. Set an environment variable that litellm picks up
       (e.g. some `LITELLM_*` or `AIDER_*` knob) before the
       retry subprocess.
    3. Catch the error upstream in the wrapper and exit
       with a specific non-zero code + a clear stderr
       message so that kiso's reviewer sees
       "`aider cannot afford max_tokens N on this balance`"
       — this does NOT fix F17/F29 but it at least surfaces
       the real cause instead of a generic replan loop.

    If none of the retry paths are feasible, the milestone
    will be split: the wrapper change lands as a
    diagnostic-only error surface (option 3), and a
    separate milestone is opened in kiso-run/core to make
    F29 skip gracefully on that specific error and to make
    F17 tolerate a single exec fallback in Plan 3 when
    aider has surfaced the cap error.

    **Cross-repo tracking.** When this milestone is started,
    a corresponding milestone is opened in
    `kiso-run/plugins/wrapper-aider/DEVPLAN.md`. The core
    milestone here is marked ✅ only after the wrapper
    milestone is implemented, committed, pushed, and the
    next kiso-run/core functional suite run shows F17 +
    F29 passing (or, if option 3 fallback lands, F17/F29
    are updated to match).

    **Wrapper fix landed.** Implemented as M10 in
    `kiso-run/plugins/wrapper-aider` (commit `9228a55` on
    main, 2026-04-13). See that milestone entry for the
    detailed root-cause confirmation, the Option-1
    mechanism choice (`--model-settings-file`), the aider
    source verification at `aider/models.py:1080-1089`
    (full-replace semantics), the parser regex, the
    override YAML shape, and the 15 unit tests covering
    parser / override-builder / end-to-end gate.

    **Tasks.**

    - [x] Open a corresponding milestone in
          `kiso-run/plugins/wrapper-aider/DEVPLAN.md` —
          M10, same problem/fix shape
    - [x] In wrapper-aider, verify the exact aider CLI /
          config mechanism for overriding `max_tokens` —
          Option 1 (`--model-settings-file` + yaml loader
          with full-replace semantics) confirmed
    - [x] Implement the parser + retry branch in

### Phase 21: MCP client integration (placeholders — superseded)

**Status.** The original high-level placeholders M1313-M1318 in this
phase are **superseded by M1332-M1343** in Phase 21 (revised) below.
They remain here as a historical pointer so the design evolution is
auditable, but they are NOT to be executed. All actionable work for
MCP integration + wrapper retirement + tool/skill rename cleanup is
tracked in the revised phase. Start reading from M1332.

54. [ ] ~~**M1313** — MCP client core (`kiso/mcp.py`)~~ — superseded by M1332-M1335

    **Why:** Kiso needs to connect to external MCP servers to access
    the MCP ecosystem (GitHub, Google Drive, Postgres, Slack, etc.)
    without writing dedicated wrappers.

    **Approach:** Create `kiso/mcp.py` with an `MCPClient` class that
    manages MCP server subprocess lifecycle and JSON-RPC communication.
    MCP servers are configured at instance level in `config.toml`.
    All users of the instance see the same MCP servers.

    **Design:**
    - Config: `[mcp.<name>]` sections in `config.toml` with `command`,
      `args`, `env` fields
    - `MCPClient`: spawns subprocess, sends JSON-RPC 2.0 via stdin,
      reads responses from stdout
    - Lifecycle: lazy start (on first use), auto-restart on crash,
      graceful shutdown on kiso exit
    - Methods: `initialize()`, `list_tools()`, `call_tool(name, params)`,
      `shutdown()`
    - `MCPManager`: manages pool of `MCPClient` instances, one per
      configured server

    **Tasks:**
    - [ ] Add `[mcp]` config schema to `kiso/config.py`
    - [ ] Create `kiso/mcp.py` with `MCPClient` and `MCPManager`
    - [ ] Implement JSON-RPC 2.0 framing (request/response)
    - [ ] Implement `initialize` handshake
    - [ ] Implement `tools/list` discovery
    - [ ] Implement `tools/call` execution
    - [ ] Implement lifecycle (lazy start, restart, shutdown)
    - [ ] Unit tests with mock subprocess
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when:** `MCPManager` can start a mock MCP server, discover
    its tools, call a tool, and handle crash/restart.

48. [ ] ~~**M1314** — MCP in the planner~~ — superseded by M1336

    **Why:** The planner needs to see MCP functions as available
    capabilities, alongside wrappers, so it can plan tasks that use

    **Approach:** Add `build_planner_mcp_list()` that queries
    `MCPManager.list_tools()` for all configured servers and formats
    them for the planner prompt.  Add `type="mcp"` as a new task type
    with `server`, `method`, `params` fields.  Update plan validation
    to accept MCP tasks.

    **Changes:**
    - `kiso/wrappers.py` or new `kiso/mcp.py`: `build_planner_mcp_list()`
    - `kiso/brain/common.py`: `TASK_TYPE_MCP = "mcp"`, add to valid types
    - `kiso/brain/planner.py`: inject MCP list into planner prompt,
      validate MCP tasks (server exists, method exists in schema)
    - `kiso/roles/planner.md`: add MCP section explaining the new task
      type, when to use MCP vs wrapper

49. [ ] ~~**M1315** — MCP in the worker~~ — superseded by M1337

    to the reviewer.

### Phase 21 (revised): MCP client, consumer-only posture, wrapper retirement

**Design context and scope decisions.** This phase replaces the
placeholder milestones M1313-M1318 with the detailed architecture
agreed on during the 2026-04-13 design round. Core posture
decisions that apply to all milestones in this phase:

1. **Kiso is a consumer-only MCP client.** Kiso does NOT publish
   MCP servers, does NOT maintain a curated registry of servers,
   and does NOT bless specific servers as "official". Users bring
   their own servers from the wider ecosystem (pulsemcp.com,
   mcp.so, `modelcontextprotocol/servers`, npm, PyPI, GitHub).
   When a user asks to install an MCP server with a vague name
   ("installami il GitHub MCP"), Kiso MUST emit a msg-only plan
   asking for a concrete URL or package identifier. Never guess,
   never pick a default, never invent a server name.

2. **Two transports, no legacy fallback.** Kiso supports stdio
   (primary, used by most servers) and the current Streamable
   HTTP transport (for remote hosted servers like Google Maps
   Grounding Lite). The deprecated HTTP+SSE transport (MCP spec
   2024-11-05) is NOT supported. If a server only offers legacy
   HTTP+SSE, use its stdio mode if available; otherwise the
   server is not compatible with Kiso v0.9. Document the
   limitation in `docs/mcp.md`. Add legacy fallback later only
   if a concrete user need arises.

3. **Tools-only primitive in v0.9.** Of the three MCP primitives
   (tools, resources, prompts), Kiso implements only **tools** in
   v0.9. Resources (passive content) and prompts (prompt
   templates) are deferred. This covers the majority of ecosystem
   value — all practical MCP servers (GitHub, GitLab, Postgres,
   filesystem, Google Maps, moltbook, etc.) are tools-first.

4. **Minimal client capabilities.** Kiso advertises no optional
   client capabilities on `initialize`:
   - NO `roots` (server cannot query kiso's filesystem roots)
   - NO `sampling` (server cannot call kiso's LLM)
   - NO `elicitation` (server cannot prompt the user via kiso UI)
   - NO `experimental`
   This is the minimum-surface posture. Servers that require any
   of these capabilities degrade gracefully per spec. Expand the
   capability set in a future version only when a concrete need
   arises.

5. **Vocabulary: "method" in Kiso, "tool" only in MCP protocol
   internals.** Kiso eliminated "tool" and "skill" as synonyms for
   "wrapper" in M1306-M1320. MCP uses "tool" as its protocol
   terminology (`tools/list`, `tools/call`, `inputSchema`), which
   is an implementation-internal detail that never leaks to users.
   In all Kiso-facing code, config, docs, and logs, refer to what
   an MCP server exposes as a **method**. The setting is
   `briefer_mcp_method_filter_threshold`, the briefer schema field
   is `mcp_methods`, the task field is `task.method`, the Python
   type is `MCPMethod`, the CLI says "available methods", the
   docs have one disclaimer mapping to MCP spec terminology.
   `tools/list` and `tools/call` appear ONLY inside
   `kiso/mcp/stdio.py` and `kiso/mcp/http.py` as JSON-RPC method
   names per the MCP spec — they never appear in user-facing text.

6. **Install policy: `uvx` and `npx`, never global pip/npm.** Kiso
   prefers ephemeral/isolated runners over persistent global
   installs. npm-distributed servers are configured with
   `command = "npx"`, `args = ["-y", "<pkg>"]`. PyPI-distributed
   servers are configured with `command = "uvx"`,
   `args = ["<pkg>"]`. Git-clone-only servers (fallback for
   servers not published to a registry) are cloned into
   `~/.kiso/mcp/servers/<name>/` and installed via `uv venv` +
   `uv pip install -e .` — isolated venv, no system pollution.
   **Never** `pip install` with system Python, **never**
   `npm install -g`. The `kiso mcp install` command pre-flight
   checks for `uv` and `npx` on PATH and emits clear install
   instructions if missing.

7. **Config is instance-wide.** `[mcp.*]` sections live in the
   single daemon-wide `config.toml`. All sessions see the same
   MCP servers. Per-user MCP scoping is deferred until Kiso grows
   real multi-tenancy; the existing `users.<name>` model can be
   extended with `mcp_servers = [...]` as an opt-in filter when
   needed. No breaking change to the current model.

8. **Credentials via CLI, not chat.** Secrets are managed by
   `kiso mcp env <name> set/list/unset/show` which writes to
   `~/.kiso/mcp/<name>.env` with `0600` permissions. The file is
   merged into the subprocess environment at spawn time. Kiso's
   planner and messenger have hard refusal patterns for secrets
   pasted in chat: if a user pastes a token in conversation,
   Kiso emits a msg-only plan refusing to store it and instructs
   the user to use `kiso mcp env`. No `kiso mcp login` OAuth
   helper — OAuth setup is per-server, documented in each
   server's own README, and out of Kiso's scope. Kiso relays
   server setup instructions but never drives the OAuth dance.

9. **Hard retirement, no grace period.** Kiso is in active
   development with no released users. The `gworkspace`,
   `websearch`, and `moltbook` wrappers are retired in one
   release (M1340-M1342). The GitHub repos
   `kiso-run/wrapper-gworkspace`, `wrapper-websearch`,
   `wrapper-moltbook` have already been deleted manually by the
   admin. The retirement milestones only remove registry entries
   and scrub code/doc references.

10. **Dependencies added.** `jsonschema >= 4.0` declared
    explicitly in `pyproject.toml` for validating MCP tool input
    arguments against their `inputSchema`. Likely already present
    as a transitive dep (openai/litellm) but declaring explicit
    makes the contract visible. Runtime requirements: `uv` and
    `npx` on PATH (checked at install time, documented).

---

53. [x] **M1332** — MCP scaffolding: package, config schema, dataclasses, client ABC ✅

    **Why.** Foundation for all other MCP milestones in this
    phase. Creates the `kiso/mcp/` package, the typed
    dataclasses for tool specs / server info / tool results, the
    abstract `MCPClient` interface that stdio and HTTP
    implementations will implement, and extends `kiso/config.py`

    `${env:VAR}` expansion at load time.

      `MCPClient`, `MCPMethod`, `MCPServer`, `MCPError`

      - `MCPMethod`: `{server, name, title, description, input_schema, output_schema, annotations}`
      - `MCPServerInfo`: `{name, title, version, protocol_version, capabilities, instructions}`
      - `MCPCallResult`: `{stdout_text, published_files, structured_content, is_error}`
      - `MCPError(Exception)` hierarchy: `MCPProtocolError`, `MCPTransportError`, `MCPInvocationError`, `MCPCapError`

54. [x] **M1333** — stdio transport: `MCPStdioClient` ✅

    **Why.** The primary MCP transport. All local MCP servers
    (npm packages via `npx`, PyPI packages via `uvx`, git-clone
    source checkouts) use stdio.

    **Scope.** Implement `MCPStdioClient(MCPClient)` in
    `kiso/mcp/stdio.py`:
    - Subprocess spawn via `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec` with
      `stdin=PIPE`, `stdout=PIPE`, `stderr=PIPE`, configurable
      `cwd`, environment from `os.environ` minus `KISO_*`
      deny-list plus the server's `env` + per-server env file
      `~/.kiso/mcp/<name>.env` (if present)
    - `start_new_session=True` so SIGTERM on shutdown terminates
      the whole process group
    - JSON-RPC framing: newline-delimited JSON objects on
      stdin/stdout (per MCP spec: `tools/list` / `tools/call`
      etc. named ONLY here, never in user-facing text)
    - Message loop reader: an asyncio task continuously reads
      stdout line-by-line, routes responses to pending request
      futures by `id`, dispatches notifications
    - stderr reader: separate asyncio task that drains the
      stderr pipe into a ring buffer (max 1MB in memory) + log
      file `~/.kiso/mcp/<name>.err.log` (append mode, rotated
      per session start). Critical for preventing pipe
      backpressure deadlock.
    - Graceful shutdown per spec: close stdin → wait 5s for
      exit → SIGTERM → wait 5s → SIGKILL
    - Request ID generation, pending request tracking,
      per-request timeout with `notifications/cancelled` on
      timeout

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Implement `MCPStdioClient` with full lifecycle
    - [ ] Implement stderr non-blocking reader
    - [ ] Implement JSON-RPC request/response correlation by id
    - [ ] Implement cancellation (`notifications/cancelled`)
    - [ ] Implement graceful shutdown sequence
    - [ ] Unit tests with a mock subprocess (a small Python
          script that echoes canned `initialize` +
          `tools/list` + `tools/call` responses):
          - Happy path: spawn, initialize, list, call, shutdown
          - stderr stream capture without blocking stdin/stdout
          - Ping-pong correlation (out-of-order responses
            matched to pending requests by id)
          - Timeout on `call_method` → cancellation notification
            sent, pending future rejected
          - Subprocess crash mid-call → appropriate
            `MCPTransportError`
          - Shutdown sequence: close stdin → SIGTERM → SIGKILL
    - [ ] Integration test: spawn
          `@modelcontextprotocol/server-everything` (reference
          sample server) via `npx -y` and run real initialize +
          tools/list (optional, only if `npx` is available)
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** A `MCPStdioClient` can connect to any stdio
    MCP server, handle the full lifecycle, and cleanly handle
    subprocess crashes, timeouts, and shutdown without leaking
    processes or leaving zombie pipes.

55. [x] **M1334** — Streamable HTTP transport: `MCPStreamableHTTPClient` ✅

    **Why.** Required for hosted MCP servers like Google Maps
    Grounding Lite at `https://mapstools.googleapis.com/mcp`.
    Without HTTP transport support, Kiso is cut off from a
    significant and growing slice of the ecosystem (cloud-hosted
    MCP services).

    **Scope.** Implement `MCPStreamableHTTPClient(MCPClient)` in
    `kiso/mcp/http.py`:
    - HTTP POST to the configured MCP endpoint URL with:
      - `Content-Type: application/json`
      - `Accept: application/json, text/event-stream`
      - `MCP-Protocol-Version: 2025-06-18` (the current spec
        version Kiso targets)
      - `Mcp-Session-Id: <captured-from-initialize>` on all
        requests after `initialize`
      - Custom `headers` from server config (for API keys like
        `X-Goog-Api-Key`)
      - `Authorization` header if `auth` is configured
    - Handle two response content-types per spec: `application/json`
      (single response) and `text/event-stream` (SSE stream with
      possibly many messages before the final response)
    - Capture `Mcp-Session-Id` from `InitializeResult` response
      headers, include on all subsequent requests
    - HTTP 404 on a session-id → server expired the session,
      start a new session by re-initializing
    - HTTP DELETE to the endpoint with session-id on shutdown
    - Reconnect on SSE stream interruption using `Last-Event-ID`
      header per spec
    - Deliberate NON-support of the deprecated HTTP+SSE transport
      (2024-11-05): on HTTP 405 from the new transport's POST,
      emit a clear error explaining Kiso does not support legacy
      HTTP+SSE, point to workarounds (use stdio mode if the
      server offers one). **Do NOT attempt the legacy GET-then-
      endpoint-event fallback.**

    **Dependency.** Use `httpx` or `aiohttp` for the HTTP client.
    Kiso already depends on `httpx` (for LLM calls), so reuse it.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Implement `MCPStreamableHTTPClient` using `httpx`
    - [ ] Implement `Accept` header handling and dual
          content-type response parsing (single JSON vs SSE
          stream)
    - [ ] Implement session-id capture + inclusion
    - [ ] Implement protocol-version header
    - [ ] Implement SSE stream reconnect with `Last-Event-ID`
    - [ ] Implement HTTP DELETE on shutdown
    - [ ] Implement clear error on legacy 405 (no fallback)
    - [ ] Implement cancellation via
          `notifications/cancelled` POST
    - [ ] Unit tests with an `aiohttp` test server simulating
          the full Streamable HTTP protocol:
          - Happy path: initialize → tools/list → tools/call →
            shutdown
          - Session-id lifecycle (capture, include, 404 →
            reinit)
          - SSE response stream with interspersed server
            notifications
          - Dual content-type: single JSON vs SSE stream
          - Cancellation
          - Reconnect on stream interruption
          - Legacy 405 → clear error without falling back
    - [ ] Integration test against a known hosted MCP server
          (Google Maps Grounding Lite, optional, requires API
          key in env — skipped if not present)
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** A `MCPStreamableHTTPClient` can connect to any
    Streamable HTTP MCP endpoint, complete the full lifecycle,
    handle SSE streams, reconnect, and shut down cleanly. Legacy
    HTTP+SSE servers produce a clear error with workaround
    instructions, not a silent hang.

56. [x] **M1335** — `MCPManager`: lifecycle pool, lazy start, cancellation, pagination ✅

    **Why.** Single entry point for everything that consumes MCP
    server functionality inside Kiso (planner integration,
    worker dispatch, CLI). Manages the per-daemon lifecycle of
    all configured MCP clients.

    **Scope.** Implement `MCPManager` in `kiso/mcp/manager.py`:
    - Singleton-ish: a module-level `get_manager(config)` that
      returns a cached instance per daemon process
    - Pool of `MCPClient` instances keyed by server name, one
      per `[mcp.<name>]` config entry
    - **Lazy start**: an `MCPClient` is created AND initialized
      on the first `list_methods(name)` or `call_method(name, ...)`
      call. Clients that are never used don't cost any startup
      time or subprocess resources.
    - **Crash detection and restart**: on `MCPTransportError`,
      mark the client as needing restart. Next call re-spawns
      it. Circuit breaker: 3 consecutive restarts within 60s →
      mark as `unhealthy`, exclude from `available_servers()`
      listing, require manual `kiso mcp test <name>` to
      re-enable.
    - **`list_methods(server_name)` with pagination**: calls
      `tools/list` in a loop, following `nextCursor` until null,
      returns the full list of `MCPMethod`. Cache per server
      with 60s TTL (invalidated on `notifications/tools/list_changed`
      from the server, when the server declared the `listChanged`
      capability).
    - **`call_method(server_name, method_name, args)` with
      timeout**: delegates to the client, enforces per-server
      `timeout_s` (configurable, default 60s), sends
      `notifications/cancelled` on timeout.
    - **Shutdown**: `shutdown_all()` called from kiso daemon
      teardown. Walks the pool, calls `client.shutdown()` on
      each. Per-client failures don't block others.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Implement `MCPManager` with lazy start, pool, cache
    - [ ] Implement crash detection and restart logic with
          circuit breaker (max 3 restarts / 60s)
    - [ ] Implement `list_methods` pagination loop
    - [ ] Implement `call_method` timeout and cancellation
    - [ ] Implement `shutdown_all`
    - [ ] Wire `get_manager(config)` into the worker daemon
          startup + teardown
    - [ ] Unit tests with mock clients:
          - Pool lifecycle: lazy start, reuse, shutdown
          - Crash + restart within limit
          - Crash storm exceeds limit → unhealthy
          - Pagination loop follows cursor
          - `list_methods` cache hit + miss
          - `call_method` timeout → cancellation + error
          - `shutdown_all` continues through per-client failures
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** Kiso's worker daemon has a single
    `MCPManager` instance managing all configured MCP servers.
    Servers spawn lazily on first use, survive transient
    failures with restart, enforce per-call timeouts, and shut
    down cleanly on daemon teardown.

57. [x] **M1336** — Planner integration: task type `mcp`, briefer extension, validation ✅

    **Why.** The planner LLM must be able to produce `mcp` task
    entries, the briefer must be able to select relevant MCP
    methods for each user message (to stay within the planner
    prompt budget), and the validator must enforce correctness
    of the produced plans.

    **Scope.**

    - **Task type constant**: add `TASK_TYPE_MCP = "mcp"` to
      `kiso/brain/common.py`. Extend `_TASK_TYPES`.
    - **Plan schema extension**: extend `PLAN_SCHEMA` task entry
      with two new **optional** fields:
      - `server`: `{"anyOf": [{"type": "string"}, {"type": "null"}]}`
      - `method`: `{"anyOf": [{"type": "string"}, {"type": "null"}]}`
      Both remain OUT of the `required` list (same pattern as
      `group`), so existing non-MCP task fixtures do not need
      updating. Extend the `type` enum to include `"mcp"`.
    - **Briefer schema extension**: add `mcp_methods` to
      `BRIEFER_SCHEMA` as a **required** field:
      `{"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}`. Format:
      qualified strings like `"github:create_issue"`. All
      existing briefer mocks must be updated to include
      `"mcp_methods": []` — one-time migration cost paid to
      maintain the explicit-contract pattern (see memory note on
      `relevant_entities` for precedent).
    - **Planner validation** (`_validate_plan` in
      `kiso/brain/planner.py`):
      - If `type == "mcp"`: `server` must be non-null and
        present in `MCPManager.available_servers()`, `method`
        must be non-null and present in the cached
        `list_methods(server)`, `wrapper` must be null.
      - If `type != "mcp"`: `server` and `method` must be null.
      - `args` for MCP task: validate against the method's
        `input_schema` using `jsonschema.validate`. On schema
        error, return a detailed error message quoting the
        failing property path and expected type.
    - **Briefer prompt extension**: extend `build_briefer_messages`
      to include an `## Available MCP methods` section listing
      all methods as `server:name — short description` (compact
      form, no full schema). Briefer LLM selects the relevant
      subset per message.
    - **Planner prompt section**: in `kiso/brain/planner.py`
      `_build_planner_messages`, after the `## Wrappers`
      section, add a `## MCP Methods` section. Use tiered
      display symmetric to wrappers:
      - If total MCP method count ≤ `briefer_mcp_method_filter_threshold`
        (new setting, default 10): show all methods with full
        `input_schema` inline.
      - Otherwise: show the briefer-selected subset with full
        `input_schema`, others as one-line summary.
    - **New setting** in `SETTINGS_DEFAULTS`:
      `briefer_mcp_method_filter_threshold = 10` (matching the
      wrapper threshold for consistency).
    - **Planner role prompt** (`kiso/roles/planner.md`): add an
      MCP section explaining the `mcp` task type, the
      `server`/`method`/`args` fields, how to choose MCP vs
      wrapper, and the **hard rule** against guessing server
      names when the user asks to install/configure an MCP
      server vaguely:
      > **MCP server installation.** Kiso does NOT maintain a
      > registry of MCP servers. When the user asks to install,
      > add, or configure an MCP server without providing a
      > concrete URL or package identifier, produce a msg-only
      > plan that asks for the URL. Never guess server names,
      > never invent URLs, never pick a default server. Valid
      > inputs you can act on: a pulsemcp.com URL, a github.com
      > repo URL, an npm/pypi package URL or pseudo-URL (npm:X,
      > pypi:X), or a direct server.json URL. Anything vague
      > → produce a msg asking for clarification.
    - **Secret refusal pattern** in planner.md and messenger.md:
      if a user pastes a secret (token, api key, password) in
      chat for MCP config purposes, produce a msg-only refusal
      with instructions to use `kiso mcp env <name> set`. This
      pattern already exists conceptually for other contexts
      and extends to MCP.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Add `TASK_TYPE_MCP` constant and extend `_TASK_TYPES`
    - [ ] Extend `PLAN_SCHEMA` with `server`, `method` as
          optional fields; add `"mcp"` to the type enum
    - [ ] Extend `BRIEFER_SCHEMA` with `mcp_methods` as
          required field
    - [ ] Update all existing briefer mocks in tests to include
          `mcp_methods: []` (grep for BRIEFER_SCHEMA and mock
          patterns)
    - [ ] Implement `_validate_plan` semantic checks for MCP
          task: server/method cross-reference against
          `MCPManager`, `jsonschema.validate` for args
    - [ ] Implement `_validate_plan` cross-check that non-MCP
          tasks have `server`/`method` as null or absent
    - [ ] Extend briefer prompt with `## Available MCP methods`
          section
    - [ ] Extend planner prompt builder with `## MCP Methods`
          section using tiered display
    - [ ] Add `briefer_mcp_method_filter_threshold` setting to
          `SETTINGS_DEFAULTS` with documentation comment
    - [ ] Update `kiso/roles/planner.md` with MCP section and
          no-registry hard rule
    - [ ] Update `kiso/roles/messenger.md` / planner.md with
          secret refusal pattern for MCP credentials
    - [ ] Unit tests:
          - Schema migration: old plan dicts without
            `server`/`method` still parse; new mcp task dicts
            parse and validate
          - Semantic validation: unknown server rejected,
            unknown method rejected, non-conforming args
            rejected with detailed error
          - Non-MCP tasks with stray `server` field rejected
          - Briefer schema migration: all existing briefer
            tests pass after adding `mcp_methods: []`
          - Planner prompt builder produces the MCP section
            correctly in both tiered-display modes
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** The planner can produce valid `mcp` task
    entries, validation catches unknown servers/methods and
    bad args, the briefer selects MCP methods per message,
    the planner prompt stays within budget via briefer
    filtering. The planner never guesses at MCP server URLs
    when the user asks to install one vaguely.

58. [x] **M1337** — Worker dispatch + MCP result rendering into session workspace ✅

    **Why.** The worker loop must dispatch `mcp` tasks to a
    handler that calls `MCPManager.call_method`, renders the
    `content[]` response into a stdout string the reviewer can
    consume, and writes any binary content (images, audio,
    blobs) into the session workspace using the existing
    `Published files:` marker pattern.

    **Scope.**

    - `kiso/worker/mcp.py` — `_handle_mcp_task(ctx, task_row, i,
      is_final, usage_idx_before)` following the signature of
      `_handle_wrapper_task`. Steps:
      1. Parse `server`, `method`, `args` from task_row
      2. Pre-flight: `MCPManager.available_servers()` contains
         `server`, cached `list_methods(server)` contains
         `method`, args validate against `input_schema`
      3. Call `MCPManager.call_method(server, method, args)`
         with the per-server timeout
      4. Render the result via `kiso/mcp/result.py`
         `render_mcp_result(server, method, task_id, session,
         result)` into `(stdout_text, published_files, is_error)`
      5. Save published files to `sessions/<id>/` and emit
         `Published files:` marker lines in stdout_text
         (reusing `_extract_published_urls` parser from
         `worker/replan.py`)
      6. On `is_error`: mark task failed, reason from content
      7. On success: mark task done, pass to reviewer
    - `kiso/mcp/result.py` — `render_mcp_result` implementation
      per the content-type mapping decided in the architecture:
      - `text` → append to stdout
      - `structuredContent` → JSON-stringify, append; drop
        duplicate text content if it matches the JSON
      - `image` (base64) → save to
        `sessions/<id>/mcp-{server}-{method}-{task_id}-{idx}.{ext}`
        with extension derived from `mimeType`; append
        `Published files:` line
      - `audio` (base64) → same pattern with `.wav`/`.mp3`/`.flac`
        extension
      - `resource_link` with `file://` URI → expose path in
        stdout, record `FileRef`
      - `resource_link` with `http(s)://` URI → expose URL in
        stdout, no auto-fetch
      - `embedded_resource` with text → inline in stdout with
        header
      - `embedded_resource` with blob → save as image/audio
      - `isError: true` → return `is_error=True`, stdout
        starts with error text extracted from content
    - Registration: add `TASK_TYPE_MCP: _handle_mcp_task` to
      `_TASK_HANDLERS` dict in `kiso/worker/loop.py`

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Implement `render_mcp_result` in `kiso/mcp/result.py`
          with full content-type handling + `Published files:`
          marker emission + structuredContent dedup
    - [ ] Implement `_handle_mcp_task` in `kiso/worker/mcp.py`
    - [ ] Register handler in `_TASK_HANDLERS` in
          `kiso/worker/loop.py`
    - [ ] Unit tests for `render_mcp_result`:
          - Text only → stdout contains text
          - Multiple text content → concatenated
          - Structured content + duplicate text → dedup
          - Image content → workspace file created, `Published
            files:` line emitted, correct filename pattern
          - Audio content → same pattern
          - Mixed text + image → both handled
          - Resource link file:// → path in stdout
          - Resource link http:// → URL in stdout, no fetch
          - Embedded resource text → inlined
          - Embedded resource blob → workspace file
          - `isError: true` → returned as error
    - [ ] Unit tests for `_handle_mcp_task` with mock
          `MCPManager`:
          - Happy path: call, render, task done, reviewer sees
            stdout
          - Unknown server → task failed with clear reason
          - Unknown method → task failed with clear reason
          - Invalid args → task failed (validation)
          - Transport error → task failed, replan
          - Tool error (`isError: true`) → task failed, replan
            reason from content
    - [ ] Integration test: spawn a reference MCP server like
          `@modelcontextprotocol/server-everything` via
          `npx -y`, run a real `call_method` end-to-end,
          verify the workspace file is created and the marker
          is emitted correctly (optional, gated on `npx`
          available)
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** The worker dispatches `mcp` tasks, renders
    results including binary content into the session workspace,
    and the downstream reviewer/messenger/cross-plan-file-
    awareness infrastructure sees MCP outputs identically to
    wrapper outputs. No new primitives; everything reuses the
    `Published files:` pattern.

59. [x] **M1338** — CLI: `kiso mcp install/list/test/remove/env` with uv/npx policy ✅

    **Why.** Human-facing entry point for managing MCP server
    configuration. Powers the workflow where the planner
    produces an exec task calling `kiso mcp install --from-url
    <url>` in response to a user install request (that
    includes a concrete URL — the planner never guesses).

    **Scope.** Add `cli/mcp.py` with subcommands:

    - **`kiso mcp list`** — table of configured servers: name,
      transport, status (up / lazy / unhealthy), cached method
      count. No secrets shown.
    - **`kiso mcp add <name> stdio --command ... [--args ...]
      [--cwd ...] [--env KEY=VAL ...] [--transport stdio]`** —
      direct interactive-lite form for advanced users who know
      exactly what they want.
    - **`kiso mcp add <name> http <url> [--header KEY=VAL ...]
      [--transport http]`** — same, for HTTP servers.
    - **`kiso mcp install --from-url <url>`** — the main path.
      Resolver in `kiso/mcp/install.py` handles:
      - `https://www.pulsemcp.com/servers/<name>` → fetch
        `/serverjson` endpoint, parse Pulsemcp standardized
        format, normalize to Kiso config
      - `https://github.com/<org>/<repo>` → clone into
        `~/.kiso/mcp/servers/<repo>/`, inspect for
        `pyproject.toml[project.scripts]` entry point or
        `package.json.bin`, create venv via `uv venv` + install
        via `uv pip install -e .`, config points at the venv
        binary
      - `https://www.npmjs.com/package/<name>` OR pseudo-URL
        `npm:@scope/name` → resolve to
        `command = "npx"`, `args = ["-y", name]`. No install
        step (npx caches on first use).
      - `https://pypi.org/project/<name>` OR pseudo-URL
        `pypi:name` → resolve to `command = "uvx"`,
        `args = [name]`. No install step (uvx caches).
      - Direct URL to a `server.json` or `mcp.json` → fetch,
        parse, normalize
      - Unknown URL form → error with supported form list
      - **Pre-flight**: `shutil.which("uv")` and
        `shutil.which("npx")` checked; if either is missing
        AND the resolver needs it, error with install
        instructions ("install uv from https://docs.astral.sh/uv/",
        "install node+npm from https://nodejs.org/")
      - After config is written, run `kiso mcp test <name>`
        automatically and report success/failure
      - On handshake failure, emit diagnostic about likely
        missing credentials or manual setup, with a message
        guiding the user to the server's README for auth
        instructions (this is where the acamolese-edge-case
        guidance lands — see example walkthrough in
        `docs/mcp.md`)
    - **`kiso mcp test <name>`** — spawn the client via the
      manager, run `initialize` + `list_methods` + `shutdown`,
      report each step and the discovered methods.
    - **`kiso mcp remove <name>`** — remove the `[mcp.<name>]`
      section from config.toml. Prompt for confirmation unless
      `--yes`. For git-cloned servers, optionally
      `--delete-source` removes `~/.kiso/mcp/servers/<name>/`
      too (default: keep).
    - **`kiso mcp env <name> set KEY VALUE`** — write to
      `~/.kiso/mcp/<name>.env`, perms `0600`, merge-on-write
      (don't clobber other vars).
    - **`kiso mcp env <name> unset KEY`** — remove one var.
    - **`kiso mcp env <name> list`** — show keys only, NOT
      values. Safe to use in shared terminal.
    - **`kiso mcp env <name> show`** — show keys AND values.
      Warn: "secrets visible — only run in trusted terminal".
    - **`kiso mcp logs <name> [--tail N]`** — tail
      `~/.kiso/mcp/<name>.err.log`.
    - **NO `kiso mcp login`** — OAuth setup is per-server,
      out-of-Kiso-scope, documented per-server in
      `docs/mcp.md`.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Create `cli/mcp.py` with argparse subcommand
          structure
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp list`
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp add stdio/http` (direct form)
    - [ ] Implement `kiso/mcp/install.py` resolver for all URL
          forms (pulsemcp, github, npm, pypi, server.json,
          pseudo-URLs)
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp install --from-url` with
          pre-flight `uv`/`npx` checks
    - [ ] Implement git-clone path: clone into
          `~/.kiso/mcp/servers/<name>/`, `uv venv` +
          `uv pip install -e .`, entry-point detection from
          `pyproject.toml` or `package.json`
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp test` with full diagnostic
          output
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp remove` with confirmation
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp env set/unset/list/show` with
          0600 perms and secret-safety defaults
    - [ ] Implement `kiso mcp logs`
    - [ ] Register `kiso mcp` in `cli/__init__.py`
    - [ ] Unit tests:
          - Resolver: each URL form → expected config
          - Resolver: unknown URL → error
          - Pre-flight missing `uv` → clear error with install
            link
          - Config write round-trip: add, read back,
            equivalence
          - `env` file ops: 0600 perms, merge-on-write, show
            warning
          - `install --from-url` with mock resolver and mock
            manager
          - `test` with mock manager returning success and
            various failures
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** A user can do the full MCP server setup
    workflow entirely from the CLI: install from a URL, set
    credentials, test the handshake, list configured servers,
    tail logs, and remove. `uv` and `npx` are the only
    runtime dependencies for install. No global `pip install`
    or `npm install -g` ever happens.

60. [x] **M1339** — Documentation: `docs/extensibility.md`, `docs/mcp.md`, architecture update ✅

    **Why.** The wrapper-vs-MCP-vs-recipe boundary rule needs
    a canonical user-facing home. Without clear docs, users
    don't know where to bring their extension work, and the
    rule we just established will drift. This milestone
    delivers the documentation backbone.

    **Scope.**

    - **New file: `docs/extensibility.md`** — the front door
      for "I want to extend Kiso, where do I start?". Contains:
      - The three extension surfaces (wrapper, MCP, recipe)
      - The decision tree: "install + manage local software?
        → wrapper; remote API / SaaS proxy? → MCP; just
        planner instructions? → recipe"
      - The boundary rule: "if it needs both local install AND
        remote API, it's a wrapper; if it's just remote API,
        it's an MCP server"
      - One paragraph about the v0.9 retirements (gworkspace,
        websearch, moltbook) as case studies of the rule
      - Links forward to `docs/mcp.md`, `docs/recipes.md`,
        wrapper docs
    - **New file: `docs/mcp.md`** — the deep-dive user guide.
      Structure:
      1. **What MCP is and Kiso's posture** — "Kiso is a
         consumer, not a registry. We don't publish or curate
         MCP servers."
      2. **Where to find servers** — pulsemcp.com, mcp.so,
         `modelcontextprotocol/servers`, GitHub search, npm
         search, PyPI search. No Kiso endorsement.
      3. **How to install one** — the `kiso mcp install
         --from-url` workflow, with the explicit no-registry
         rule: "Kiso needs a concrete URL or package
         identifier. It will not guess."
      4. **Three concrete example configs** (with working
         real-world URLs):
         - **npm stdio via npx**:
           `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` as the primary
           example (the canonical pattern in the MCP
           ecosystem). Full walkthrough: install → env setup
           → test → first method call.
         - **PyPI stdio via uvx**: a well-packaged Python
           server as example.
         - **Remote HTTP**: `mapstools.googleapis.com/mcp`
           (Google Maps Grounding Lite). API key setup,
           config TOML, test.
      5. **Authentication** — covers env-var-based static
         credentials (the common case, via `kiso mcp env`),
         mentions OAuth device flow as a future-friendly
         pattern, and has an `Advanced: single-host OAuth
         servers` subsection that documents acamolese-style
         servers (local OAuth dance, requires shell+browser
         on the host machine) as the edge case it is, with
         explicit language flagging why it doesn't work for
         headless deployments.
      6. **Credential management** — `kiso mcp env` usage,
         file perms, chat refusal pattern, the
         "don't paste secrets in chat" rule.
      7. **Security notes** — what an MCP server can do,
         why to review tool calls, the human-in-the-loop
         SHOULD per spec.
      8. **Troubleshooting** — `kiso mcp test`, `kiso mcp
         logs`, common errors and their meanings,
         `jsonschema` validation errors.
      9. **Capabilities NOT currently supported** — explicit
         list: resources, prompts, roots, sampling,
         elicitation, logging, experimental. With a
         one-line explanation for each and a pointer to file
         an issue if a specific capability is needed.
      10. **Disclaimer** — "Examples are community servers
          maintained by third parties. Kiso has no
          responsibility or SLA for them."
      11. **Terminology note** — "Kiso uses 'method' for what
          the MCP protocol calls 'tool' (see `tools/list`,
          `tools/call`). Same concept, different name: we
          use 'method' to avoid confusion with our
          pre-rename terminology. When reading the MCP spec,
          mentally substitute 'tool' → 'method'."
    - **Update `docs/architecture.md`** — add a short
      "Extension surfaces" section (≤10 lines) that
      enumerates wrapper/MCP/recipe and points at
      `docs/extensibility.md` as the decision tree. No
      duplication.
    - **Update `README.md`** — top-level "Extending Kiso"
      section linking to `docs/extensibility.md`.
    - **Update `docs/cli.md`** — add the new `kiso mcp`
      subcommand documentation.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Write `docs/extensibility.md` from scratch
    - [ ] Write `docs/mcp.md` from scratch
    - [ ] Add "Extension surfaces" section to
          `docs/architecture.md`
    - [ ] Add "Extending Kiso" section to `README.md`
    - [ ] Update `docs/cli.md` with `kiso mcp` subcommands
    - [ ] Doc lint: markdown syntax check, dead link check,
          embedded TOML config examples round-trip through
          our parser (they must be valid config.toml
          fragments)
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** A new user opening `docs/extensibility.md`
    can understand the wrapper/MCP/recipe distinction in
    under 2 minutes and know where to go next. A user
    opening `docs/mcp.md` can configure a first MCP server
    end-to-end by following one of the three walkthroughs.

61. [x] **M1340** — Retire `gworkspace` wrapper ✅

    **Why.** `gworkspace` is a pure proxy to Google APIs, no
    local install beyond the httpx client, no session
    workspace integration. Violates the wrapper-boundary rule
    (see `docs/extensibility.md`). The GitHub repo
    `kiso-run/wrapper-gworkspace` has already been deleted
    manually by the admin.

    **Scope.**

    - Remove `gworkspace` entry from `registry.json`
    - Grep for `gworkspace` references in:
      - `kiso/roles/*.md` (planner, briefer, classifier
        prompts might mention it by name in examples)
      - `kiso/brain/common.py` (regex lists, type enums,
        M1320-allow markers)
      - `kiso/sysenv.py` (if any)
      - `tests/` (functional tests may reference it)
      - `docs/` (architecture, cli, old mcp guide, readme)
    - Remove every found reference, or if it's illustrative
      (e.g. "example wrapper") swap to a remaining wrapper
    - Add a CHANGELOG entry explaining the retirement and
      pointing at `docs/mcp.md` for equivalent MCP servers
      (Google Workspace MCPs exist in the ecosystem, no
      Kiso endorsement of any specific one)

    **Tasks.**
