    - [ ] Full grep for `gworkspace` across
          `kiso/`, `cli/`, `tests/`, `docs/`, `README.md`
    - [ ] Scrub each reference appropriately
    - [ ] Update CHANGELOG
    - [ ] Run full unit + integration + live suite to catch
          any missed references
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** `kiso wrapper list` does not show
    `gworkspace`. `kiso wrapper install gworkspace` returns
    a clear error with link to `docs/mcp.md`. No stray
    references in code or docs.

62. [x] **M1341** — Retire `websearch` wrapper ✅

    **Why.** `websearch` is a pure proxy to Brave/Serper
    APIs, no local install, no workspace integration. Same
    violation pattern as `gworkspace`. The GitHub repo has
    been deleted manually.

    **Important distinction.** The built-in `search` task
    type (handled by `kiso/brain/search.py` or similar,
    part of the planner task vocabulary) is a SEPARATE
    concept and stays intact. M1341 only removes the
    `websearch` *wrapper*, not the `search` task type. The
    planner prompt has references to both — the wrapper
    ones go, the task-type ones stay.

    **Scope.** Same pattern as M1340, applied to `websearch`.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Remove `websearch` from `registry.json`
    - [ ] Grep for `websearch` (the wrapper name) across
          `kiso/`, `cli/`, `tests/`, `docs/`
    - [ ] Scrub wrapper references while preserving any
          `search` (task type) references
    - [ ] Verify the built-in `search` task type still
          works via unit + integration tests
    - [ ] Update CHANGELOG
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** `websearch` wrapper is gone from the
    registry and code. Built-in `search` task type
    continues to work. No stray wrapper references.

63. [x] **M1342** — Retire `moltbook` wrapper ✅

    **Why.** `moltbook` wrapper is a pure proxy to the
    Moltbook social network API, no local install, no
    workspace integration. The community MCP server
    `thebenlamm/moltbook-mcp` exists as an ecosystem
    alternative (documented as an example in `docs/mcp.md`
    under M1339 — not endorsed, just listed). The GitHub
    repo has been deleted manually.

    **Scope.** Same pattern as M1340.

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Remove `moltbook` from `registry.json`
    - [ ] Grep for `moltbook` across `kiso/`, `cli/`,
          `tests/`, `docs/`
    - [ ] Scrub references; update any functional tests
          that exercised `moltbook` (either remove them
          entirely or adapt to use a remaining wrapper as a
          stand-in)
    - [ ] Update CHANGELOG
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** `moltbook` wrapper is gone. Users who
    still want Moltbook integration can follow the
    `docs/mcp.md` example pointing at the community MCP
    server, without Kiso taking responsibility for it.

64. [x] **M1343** — Complete tool/skill rename cleanup (finish what M1306-M1320 started) ✅

    **Why.** The rename pass M1306-M1320 left residuals in
    several code paths. Audit on 2026-04-13 found:

    - **Shell completion scripts** (user-facing): `kiso/completions/kiso.bash`
      and `kiso.zsh` still expose `skill` as a top-level
      command in the completion table. `kiso <TAB>` shows
      `skill` as a suggested subcommand, which is wrong.
    - **Role prompts** (LLM-facing, highest impact):
      `kiso/roles/planner.md` lines 29, 69, 70, 81, 105, 112
      use "tool" meaning "wrapper". `kiso/roles/classifier.md`
      lines 4 and 6 use "tools/connectors/plugins". 
      `kiso/roles/worker.md` line 6 uses "specific tool".
      These inconsistencies cause the planner LLM to
      occasionally emit `type: tool` (validator rejects, retry
      burn).
    - **Internal code** (comments, log messages, docstrings):
      `kiso/brain/planner.py` lines 746, 956, 959, 1016,
      1018, 1066, 1069, 1232, 1239, 1240, 1270, 1271, 1306,
      1420. `kiso/brain/common.py` lines 1353 (docstring),
      1385 (docstring), 1416 (log format string).
      `kiso/brain/roles_registry.py` line 51 (briefer
      description). `kiso/registry.py` line 1 (module
      docstring). `kiso/worker/utils.py` line 416 (comment).
      `kiso/config.py` line 233 (comment on
      `briefer_wrapper_filter_threshold`).
      `kiso/wrappers.py` local variable `tools: list[dict]`
      at lines 133, 182, 184, 186, 191.
    - **Test coverage gap**: `tests/test_rename_completeness.py`
      is the guardian test that scans `kiso/` and `cli/` for
      stray `\b(tool|skill|...)\b` references. It currently
      passes despite all the above hits, meaning the scanner
      has allowlist holes or doesn't cover `.md` role prompt
      files. The guardian has bugs.

    **What is explicitly NOT in scope (intentional
    survivors).**

    - Input regex in `kiso/brain/common.py` marked
      `# noqa: M1320-allow` — these accept natural language
      user input ("install tool X", "wrapper Y"). Layer
      intentionally bilingual. Stay.
    - `tools/list` and `tools/call` strings inside
      `kiso/mcp/stdio.py` and `kiso/mcp/http.py` (to be
      added in M1333-M1334). These are JSON-RPC method
      names per the MCP spec. They are protocol-internal,
      never user-facing. Stay.
    - `test_rename_completeness.py`'s regex alphabet
      (`\b(tool|skill|...)\b`) — that's the guardian test,
      allow.

    **Scope.**

    - **Shell completion scripts**: `skill` is removed from
      top-level completion, replaced with `wrapper` if not
      already present, or dropped if the `wrapper` command
      subsumed `skill`.
    - **Role prompts**: `kiso/roles/planner.md`,
      `classifier.md`, `worker.md` — replace every "tool"
      that means "wrapper" with "wrapper". Examples and
      code snippets in the prompts are updated to use
      wrapper field names. This is LLM-input-sensitive
      content; treat carefully and validate end-to-end.
    - **Internal code**: every comment/log/docstring listed
      above gets rewritten to use "wrapper" consistently.
      The `tools: list[dict]` variable in
      `kiso/wrappers.py` is renamed to `wrappers` or
      `wrapper_infos`.
    - **Test coverage**: `test_rename_completeness.py` is
      extended to also scan `kiso/roles/*.md`. Any remaining
      allowlist holes are closed. After M1343, running the
      guardian with `-v` must show zero surviving `tool` /
      `skill` references as kiso concepts.

    **Ordering.** This milestone runs AFTER M1340-M1342
    because the retirements may touch some of the same
    files (planner.md may mention gworkspace/websearch/
    moltbook by name as "tools", and cleaning them up
    alongside the rename is more efficient than two
    passes).

    **Tasks.**

    - [ ] Run the grep audit fresh (some lines may have
          shifted since 2026-04-13)
    - [ ] Clean `kiso/completions/kiso.bash` and `kiso.zsh`
    - [ ] Clean `kiso/roles/planner.md` (test the cleaned
          prompt against a small canned plan set to verify
          behavior unchanged)
    - [ ] Clean `kiso/roles/classifier.md`
    - [ ] Clean `kiso/roles/worker.md`
    - [ ] Clean internal code references in `kiso/brain/`,
          `kiso/worker/`, `kiso/registry.py`, `kiso/config.py`,
          `kiso/wrappers.py`
    - [ ] Extend `test_rename_completeness.py` to scan
          `.md` files in `kiso/roles/`, close any
          allowlist holes uncovered
    - [ ] Run the full unit + integration suite
    - [x] Re-run a subset of the live functional suite on
          the cleaned role prompts (classifier + planner +
          worker) to catch any LLM regression from the
          prompt changes
    - [ ] Commit & push

    **Done when.** `grep -rn '\btool\b\|\bskill\b' kiso/
    cli/` returns only intentional survivors (regex
    `noqa: M1320-allow` entries, `test_rename_completeness.py`
    guardian, `tools/list`/`tools/call` in MCP protocol
    modules). `test_rename_completeness.py` with its
    extended scope passes. End-to-end functional run
    (classifier → planner → worker) shows no rename-related
    regression.

65. [x] **M1344** — MCP test infrastructure: mock fixtures + live reference-server tests ✅

    **Why.** The client milestones M1332-M1337 each carry
    their own unit tests, but we need two additional test
    tiers to have real confidence:

    1. **Deterministic integration tests** — fast,
       offline, controllable fault injection, no external
       dependencies. Run on every CI. Use self-hosted mock
       servers we write in `tests/fixtures/`.
    2. **Live tests against real reference MCP servers** —
       proves end-to-end interoperability with the actual
       ecosystem. Gated on network + `npx` availability.
       Uses servers from `@modelcontextprotocol/servers`
       that do NOT require authentication, so the tests are
       reproducible by any contributor without credentials.

    This milestone delivers both tiers in one place so the
    test harness is coherent and reusable across M1333,
    M1334, M1335, M1337, M1338.

    ---

    ### Tier 1 — Deterministic mock fixtures

    **Fixture 1: `tests/fixtures/mock_stdio_mcp_server.py`** —
    a standalone Python script that implements a minimal
    stdio MCP server with controllable behavior via env
    vars. It speaks the real JSON-RPC framing over stdin/
    stdout and exits cleanly on stdin EOF or SIGTERM.

    Supported test scenarios (via `MOCK_MCP_SCENARIO` env):
    - `happy` (default) — returns a fixed method list, echoes
      tool call args as text content
    - `slow_init` — delays `initialize` response by N seconds
      (configurable via `MOCK_MCP_INIT_DELAY`) to test
      initialization timeout handling
    - `crash_on_call` — exits with code 1 on first
      `tools/call` to test crash recovery + restart
    - `large_tools_list` — returns 50+ methods across 2
      pages (cursor pagination) to test the pagination loop
    - `mixed_content` — returns text + image (base64) +
      structured content to test result rendering
    - `is_error` — returns `{isError: true}` with error text
    - `notification_storm` — emits
      `notifications/tools/list_changed` periodically to
      test notification handling
    - `stderr_flood` — writes 2MB+ to stderr to test the
      non-blocking stderr drain and ring buffer

    Spawned via `asyncio.create_subprocess_exec(sys.executable,
    path_to_fixture, env={"MOCK_MCP_SCENARIO": ...})`.
    Fast (Python startup ~100ms), deterministic, no network.

    **Fixture 2: `tests/fixtures/mock_http_mcp_server.py`** —
    an `aiohttp` app that simulates Streamable HTTP MCP
    transport. Runs in-process on a random port, started
    and torn down per test via a pytest fixture.

    Supported endpoints:
    - `POST /mcp` with full content-type negotiation
      (returns `application/json` or `text/event-stream`
      based on test scenario config)
    - `Mcp-Session-Id` generation on `initialize`, 404 on
      expired session
    - `MCP-Protocol-Version` header validation
    - SSE stream with interspersed server notifications
      before the final response
    - `DELETE /mcp` with session-id cleanup

    Supported test scenarios (via fixture parameters):
    - Baseline happy path
    - Single-JSON response mode (no SSE)
    - SSE stream with N server notifications before
      response
    - Session expiry (returns 404 on second request)
    - Legacy `HTTP 405 Method Not Allowed` on POST (to
      verify Kiso's clear-error-no-fallback behavior for
      deprecated HTTP+SSE servers)
    - Protocol version mismatch

    ---

    ### Tier 2 — Live tests with reference MCP servers (no auth)

    **File: `tests/live/test_mcp_reference_servers.py`**

    Gated via the existing `live_network` pytest marker so
    these only run when the live suite is enabled AND `npx`
    is on PATH (skipped gracefully otherwise).

    **Reference servers used (all auth-free, all from
    `@modelcontextprotocol/servers`)**:

    | Package | Spawn | What we test |
    |---|---|---|
    | `@modelcontextprotocol/server-everything` | `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-everything` | Reference impl of all primitives. Full handshake, paginated tools/list, a concrete tool call, structured content rendering, shutdown. The canonical smoke test. |
    | `@modelcontextprotocol/server-memory` | `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-memory` | In-memory knowledge graph. Test `create_entities` + `read_graph` round-trip. Exercises real state-changing tools. |
    | `@modelcontextprotocol/server-fetch` | `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-fetch` | Fetches a URL (we fetch `https://example.com`, which is a stable public baseline). Tests that result rendering handles longer text content. |
    | `@modelcontextprotocol/server-sequentialthinking` | `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-sequentialthinking` | Reasoning helper. Tests lifecycle on a tool that emits multiple content blocks. |

    Tests:
    - `test_everything_server_handshake` — spawn via
      `MCPStdioClient`, `initialize`, read `serverInfo`, call
      `shutdown`. Assert protocolVersion negotiated is
      `2025-06-18` (or the server's latest, with fallback
      logic validated).
    - `test_everything_server_tools_list_paginated` — call
      `list_methods`, assert at least one method returned,
      verify the loop handles `nextCursor` correctly if the
      server paginates.
    - `test_everything_server_call_method` — call a real
      method (the everything server has `echo` or similar),
      verify the result rendering produces expected stdout
      text.
    - `test_memory_server_graph_roundtrip` — create entities,
      read them back, verify structured content is parsed
      and rendered.
    - `test_fetch_server_example_com` — fetch
      `https://example.com`, verify result contains
      "Example Domain" text, verify the `text` content
      block is concatenated into the task stdout.
    - `test_sequentialthinking_lifecycle` — full lifecycle
      on a tool that emits multi-block content.
    - `test_nonexistent_package_clear_error` — attempt to
      spawn a non-existent npm package, verify the error
      surfaces cleanly with actionable diagnostic.

    All tests run without credentials, on any machine with
    network + `npx` available.

    ---

    ### Tier 3 — Optional auth-required live tests (opt-in)

    **File: `tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py`**

    Gated on specific env vars; each test skips if its
    corresponding env var is unset. For contributors who
    have credentials, these provide extra real-world
    validation; for those who don't, they're no-ops.

    Tests:
    - `test_brave_search_stdio` — requires
      `TEST_BRAVE_API_KEY` in env. Spawns
      `@modelcontextprotocol/server-brave-search` via npx,
      issues a simple query, verifies results come back. Brave
      Search has a free tier API key easy to obtain, no
      billing required.
    - `test_github_stdio_anonymous` — uses
      `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` without a PAT.
      Tests that the server handles missing auth gracefully
      (the public read-only methods should work without a
      token — list_public_repo_issues on an open-source repo
      like `kiso-run/core`). Skipped if the server refuses
      anonymous access; documents the behavior as a test
      artifact.
    - `test_google_maps_grounding_http` — requires
      `TEST_GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY`. Connects to
      `https://mapstools.googleapis.com/mcp` via
      `MCPStreamableHTTPClient`, runs `search_places` with a
      known-good query ("Eiffel Tower"), verifies results.
      Exercises the HTTP transport against a real hosted
      server. Google Maps has a free quota tier.

    These are "bonus" coverage — the project doesn't
    require them to pass for CI green. They're here so
    contributors who do have the credentials get extra
    confidence.

    ---

    ### Tier 4 — Functional end-to-end via planner

    **File: `tests/functional/test_mcp_install_flow.py`**

    Gated on `--functional` marker (requires LLM credits).
    Full pipeline test: natural-language request → planner
    → worker → real MCP server → result rendered.

    Test: `test_install_and_use_memory_server_end_to_end`:
    1. Send message: "Install the MCP server from
       `npm:@modelcontextprotocol/server-memory`"
    2. Planner produces a plan with an exec task calling
       `kiso mcp install --from-url npm:@modelcontextprotocol/server-memory`
    3. Worker executes, config written, handshake passes
    4. Send message: "Create an entity 'test' with
       observation 'it works' in memory"
    5. Planner produces a plan with an `mcp` task calling
       `memory:create_entities`
    6. Worker dispatches, server responds, reviewer
       accepts
    7. Send message: "What's in memory?"
    8. Planner produces a plan with `memory:read_graph`
    9. Worker dispatches, result contains "test" entity
    10. Messenger reports the result back to the user
    11. Assert the final user-visible message mentions
        "test" and "it works"

    This is the single comprehensive test that proves the
    whole MCP integration works end-to-end through every
    layer (config parse, planner prompt, briefer schema,
    task validation, worker dispatch, result rendering,
    reviewer, messenger). Expensive (requires credits) but
    invaluable as an acceptance gate.

    Test: `test_vague_install_request_asks_for_url`:
    1. Send message: "installami il github mcp"
    2. Planner produces a msg-only plan asking for the
       concrete URL (per the no-registry hard rule in
       planner.md)
    3. Assert the messenger's reply contains guidance about
       where to find server URLs (pulsemcp.com, mcp.so,
       github.com/modelcontextprotocol/servers) and does
       NOT contain an invented URL or an invented server
       name
    4. Assert no exec task was created, no install was
       attempted

    This directly validates the hard rule against guessing
    MCP server identities.

    Test: `test_secret_in_chat_refused`:
    1. After a successful install of any auth-requiring
       server, send message: "Save this token for
       <server>: <fake-token>"
    2. Planner produces a msg-only plan refusing to store
       the secret in chat and instructing the user to use
       `kiso mcp env <name> set`
    3. Assert no config.toml changes, no env file changes,
       no state mutation from the chat content

    ---

66. [x] **M1345** — Phase 21 post-landing test fixes + safety rule messenger leak + GitHub live coverage ✅

    **Context.** First full test matrix run after Phase 21
    landed surfaced a cluster of independent failures. Root
    causes were investigated on 2026-04-14 and split into
    the actionable fixes below. M1344 (live reference
    server tests) itself was green, but four adjacent
    issues came out:

    1. **Safety rule messenger leak** (`TestFRulesPathDisclosure.test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`).
       The reviewer correctly marks path-disclosure tasks
       `stuck` for safety violation, but the messenger
       that composes the user-facing refusal echoes the
       verbatim paths from the safety rule text it sees in
       its own context. Same architectural bug class as
       M1328 (reviewer.reason leaked into user-visible
       replan template): **internal enforcement metadata
       should not leak into the presentation layer**. Path
       disclosure is the visible case; the general class
       covers any future safety rule (secrets, PII,
       blocklisted content).
       Bonus: the test assertion at
       `tests/functional/test_safety_rules.py:48` uses
       `or` where `and` is meant, so the assertion is
       weaker than intended — passes whenever at least one
       of `/home/` or `/root/` is absent. Both bugs fix
       together.

    2. **Multilingual text-stats regex gap**
       (`TestF30FullPipeline.test_browse_ocr_aider_exec`).
       `CHARS_COUNT_RE` and `LINES_COUNT_RE` in
       `tests/functional/conftest.py` match
       `caratteri: 1978` but not `caratteri è: 1978`
       (Italian copula between the noun and the number).
       The messenger legitimately produces the second
       form in Italian responses; the regex is
       under-tolerant.

    3. **Live wrapper install test still references a
       retired wrapper**
       (`TestWrapperInstallRemove.test_install_and_remove_official_wrapper`).
       The test hard-codes `websearch` as the canonical
       test wrapper; that repo was deleted in M1341.
       `git clone` 404s → `RuntimeError: git clone failed`.

    4. **Live reference server test targets a non-existent
       npm package** (`TestSequentialThinkingServer.test_initialize_and_shutdown`).
       `@modelcontextprotocol/server-sequentialthinking`
       returns npm 404 — that exact package name does not
       exist on the npm registry. This is a bug I
       introduced in M1344: the name was invented, not
       verified against the actual registry.

    5. **`TestFRulesLifecycle.test_rule_removal_restores_behavior`** —
       extended-suite timeout on the first run. A manual
       rerun on 2026-04-14 passed cleanly. Flake,
       environmental (slow LLM path), no code issue. No
       code fix; documented here as the reason the test
       is not part of the in-scope fix list.

    Two additional improvements land in the same milestone
    while we are touching the live-auth test area:

    6. **New GitHub MCP live test.**
       `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` is the most
       widely used MCP server in the ecosystem. Adding a
       smoke test (initialize + list_methods) that skips
       cleanly when `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN` is
       missing gives contributors with a PAT free bonus
       coverage of the stdio transport against a real
       authenticated server.

    7. **Env var naming: drop the `TEST_` prefix.** The
       live auth tests read from `TEST_BRAVE_API_KEY` and
       `TEST_GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY` today. Those names
       imply "test-fixture keys" but we are testing real
       services with real credentials — there is nothing
       test-specific about the keys themselves. Switching
       to the canonical names every MCP server expects
       natively (`BRAVE_API_KEY`, `GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY`,
       `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN`) means: (a) when a
       user already has one of those keys set for real
       usage on a dev box, the live test automatically
       runs with zero extra configuration; (b) the same
       key powers both production usage of that MCP
       server and its live test, no duplication.

    ---

    ### Fix 1 — Safety rule messenger refusal (architectural)

    Root cause: safety rules are injected into the
    messenger's context pool alongside the planner's and
    reviewer's, so the messenger sees them verbatim. When
    asked to compose a refusal for a stuck-on-safety task,
    the LLM paraphrases the rule text and ends up naming
    the very content the rule exists to hide. This is the
    **enforcement metadata leaking into presentation**
    pattern, directly analogous to M1328's reviewer.reason
    leak into user-visible replan messages.

    Three coordinated structural changes:

    - **(a) Drop safety rules from messenger context.**
      The safety_rules section is useful to the planner
      (so it does not plan violations) and to the
      reviewer (so it blocks outputs in violation). It is
      NOT needed by the messenger, whose job is
      composition of the user-facing reply, not
      enforcement. Locate the exact injection point
      (likely in `kiso/brain/planner.py`'s prompt
      builder or in `kiso/worker/message_flow.py`'s
      `_msg_task_impl`) and skip the safety_rules
      injection for the messenger role while preserving
      it for planner and reviewer.

    - **(b) Messenger role prompt clause.** Add an
      explicit directive to `kiso/roles/messenger.md`:

      > When a task fails, is stuck, or cannot be
      > completed, compose a refusal that acknowledges
      > the failure without repeating or paraphrasing the
      > specific content the task was attempting to
      > access, list, or reveal. If the user asked "where
      > are config files" and the task was blocked for a
      > safety reason, reply "I can't provide that
      > information right now — could you rephrase or try
      > something different?" — never enumerate the
      > forbidden items in your refusal. Describe the
      > constraint generically; the user already knows
      > what they asked for, echoing the forbidden
      > content gives them no value and leaks the very
      > thing the constraint exists to protect.

      This is LLM-level prompt guidance. Layer (a) is
      the structural fix; (b) is the reinforcement.

    - **(c) Stuck category coarse-grained.** When the
      worker hands a stuck task off to the messenger, it
      currently passes the full reviewer.reason text.
      Replace that with a coarse `stuck_category` enum
      derived from the reason via deterministic pattern
      match in the worker (before calling the messenger):
      - `reviewer.reason` contains "safety rule" →
        `stuck_category = "safety_violation"`
      - contains "credits" / "quota" / "rate limit" →
        `"resource_exhausted"`
      - contains "unreachable" / "timeout" / "connection"
        → `"unreachable_service"`
      - contains "wrapper" / "not installed" / "cannot
        find" → `"wrapper_unavailable"`
      - default → `"unknown"`

      The messenger prompt has templates per category,
      and never sees the detailed reason text. Same
      discipline as M1328 applied to a new leak channel.

    Scope clarifications and risk notes:

    - `BRIEFER_SCHEMA` is NOT touched. Safety rules are
      injected into planner/messenger contexts AFTER the
      briefer decision, directly in the prompt builder.
      No sweep of briefing mock fixtures is required.
    - Behavior rules (f-rules-2 citation marker test)
      are a separate channel with a different injection
      point. Behavior rules continue to reach the
      messenger (they are content guidelines, not
      enforcement directives). Not affected.
    - Reviewer unchanged: keeps seeing safety rules for
      enforcement, keeps emitting detailed reason text
      for logs. Only the messenger path is narrowed.

    Fix 1 also includes the `tests/functional/test_safety_rules.py:48`
    assertion bug fix: `or` → `and`. The author's
    intended semantics (from the error string they wrote)
    is "neither path leaked"; the `or` version only
    fails when both are present, weakening the test.
    Both the structural fix and the assertion fix are
    required for the test to be meaningful.

    ### Fix 2 — Text-stats regex multilingual tolerance

    `CHARS_COUNT_RE` and `LINES_COUNT_RE` in
    `tests/functional/conftest.py:104-108` currently
    tolerate only whitespace, `count`, `:`, `*` between
    the noun and the number. Italian responses from the
    messenger say things like `caratteri è: 1978` or
    `righe sono: 69` — with an Italian copula (`è`,
    `sono`) between the noun and the number. The regex
    misses these.

    Fix: loosen the between-noun-and-digit tolerance to
    `[^0-9\n]{0,15}` — up to 15 non-digit characters on
    the same line. Covers any copula, punctuation, or
    short connector in any language without being
    overfitted.

    New regex shape:

    ```python
    CHARS_COUNT_RE = re.compile(
        r"(?:char(?:acter)?s?|caratteri)[^0-9\n]{0,15}\d+",
        re.IGNORECASE,
    )
    LINES_COUNT_RE = re.compile(
        r"(?:lines?|righe?)[^0-9\n]{0,15}\d+",
        re.IGNORECASE,
    )
    ```

    The 15-char window prevents the regex from slurping
    across unrelated parts of the text; newlines are
    explicitly excluded. Round-trip on both the old
    passing cases (`chars: 1432`, `caratteri: 92`,
    `**Character Count:** 1432`) and the new Italian
    form (`caratteri è: 1978`).

    ### Fix 3 — Wrapper install test replacement

    `tests/live/test_cli_live.py:126` hard-codes
    `skill_name = "websearch"` with a comment calling it
    "the canonical example wrapper". Websearch was
    retired in M1341 and the GitHub repo has been
    deleted. Replace with `browser`, which is
    (a) still in the live registry, (b) still has a
    published kiso-run repo, and (c) is a reasonable
    canonical example after the retirements.

    The test still exercises the full install → remove
    lifecycle via real git clone; only the target name
    changes.

    ### Fix 4 — Replace sequentialthinking with filesystem

    `@modelcontextprotocol/server-sequentialthinking`
    returns npm 404. I invented the name during M1344
    without verifying against the registry.
    `@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem` exists, is
    officially maintained, accepts a path argument
    (which exercises the args-passing code path in our
    stdio transport), and exposes concrete methods
    (`read_file`, `list_directory`, etc.) that allow a
    real `tools/call` smoke beyond just `list_methods`.

    `TestSequentialThinkingServer` in
    `tests/live/test_mcp_reference_servers.py` gets
    replaced by `TestFilesystemServer` with the same
    lifecycle shape but targeting the filesystem server
    with `tmp_path` as its sandbox root.

    ### Fix 5 — GitHub live test

    New `TestGitHubServer` class in
    `tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py`:

    - Gated on `live_network` pytest marker
    - Skips if `shutil.which("npx") is None`
    - Skips if `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN` env var
      is not set
    - Spawns `@modelcontextprotocol/server-github` via
      `npx -y`, passes the PAT through the server env
    - Runs `initialize` + `list_methods` + `shutdown`
    - Asserts the server exposes more than 5 methods
      (the real server-github exposes ~26)
    - No `tools/call` assertion — smoke only, to avoid
      coupling the test to specific repo content or
      GitHub API changes

    ### Fix 6 — Env var rename

    Rename in `tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py`:
    - `_BRAVE_KEY = os.environ.get("TEST_BRAVE_API_KEY")`
      → `os.environ.get("BRAVE_API_KEY")`
    - `_GMAPS_KEY = os.environ.get("TEST_GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY")`
      → `os.environ.get("GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY")`
    - The corresponding `@pytest.mark.skipif` strings
      updated to reference the new env var names

    Plus a sweep of `docs/mcp.md` and anywhere else the
    `TEST_*` prefix appears to match the new convention.
    These are the canonical names every MCP server
    expects natively, so a contributor who has the key
    already set for real usage gets automatic live test
    coverage without any duplication.

67. [x] **M1346** — `run_tests.sh` loads `.env` from the repo root ✅

    **Problem.** Live tests that need credentials
    (`BRAVE_API_KEY`, `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN`,
    `GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY`, plus `KISO_LLM_API_KEY` /
    `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`) currently require the
    contributor to either (a) `set -a; source .env; set +a`
    manually before every `run_tests.sh` invocation, or
    (b) put keys into `~/.kiso/instances/kiso/.env`, which
    is the runtime `.env` of an installed Kiso instance —
    **not** the right place for developer/test credentials.
    Those two files have distinct scopes and should not
    be conflated.

    **Decision.** `utils/run_tests.sh` should also load
    `<repo-root>/.env` if present, using the same
    idempotent pattern (`[[ -z "${!key:-}" ]]` → do not
    overwrite variables already exported in the parent
    shell). The repo `.env` is loaded **before** the
    instance `.env`, so repo keys win for the contributor
    scenario but the instance `.env` still works as a
    fallback for environments that only have the runtime
    file configured.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Add a shell-level test (bats) in
          `tests/bash/` covering:
          (1) repo `.env` loaded when present,
          (2) pre-exported vars not overwritten,
          (3) comments + blank lines ignored,
          (4) graceful no-op when repo `.env` missing.
    - [x] Extend `utils/run_tests.sh`: resolve
          `REPO_ROOT` (parent dir of the script's
          location), then apply the same loader block
          used for the instance `.env` to
          `"$REPO_ROOT/.env"` **first**.
    - [x] Confirm `.gitignore` already excludes `.env`
          at repo root (it does — verify only).
    - [x] Add the three MCP live-test keys to
          `.env.example` with brief comments pointing
          at where to obtain each one
          (GitHub Settings → Tokens, Brave API
          dashboard, Google Cloud Console Grounding
          Lite).
    - [x] Update `docs/testing-live.md`: document the
          new loader path and precedence order.
    - [x] Full bats run + live-network spot run to
          confirm the loader works end-to-end
          (`./utils/run_tests.sh l tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py`
          should now pick up the repo `.env` without
          a manual `source`).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - A contributor with keys in `<repo>/.env` can run
      any `./utils/run_tests.sh <tier>` invocation and
      the keys are visible to pytest without a manual
      `source` step.
    - Variables already present in the parent shell
      environment are never overwritten by either
      `.env` file (documented precedence: parent shell
      > repo `.env` > instance `.env`).
    - `.env.example` lists all live-test credentials
      a contributor might want to set.

68. [x] **M1347** — MCP HTTP client: `Mcp-Session-Id` must be optional ✅

    **Problem.** `MCPStreamableHTTPClient.initialize()` in
    `kiso/mcp/http.py` raises `MCPProtocolError("server did
    not return an Mcp-Session-Id header")` when the server
    omits that header on the initialize response. This
    breaks stateless real servers: the live test
    `TestGoogleMapsGroundingLite` against
    `https://mapstools.googleapis.com/mcp` fails with
    exactly this error because Google's hosted MCP endpoint
    is stateless and does not issue session IDs.

    **Spec reality.** MCP 2025-06-18 says session IDs are
    optional: the server *MAY* return an `Mcp-Session-Id`
    on initialize; if present the client *MUST* include it
    on subsequent requests; if absent the client operates
    without one. Our current code enforces presence, which
    is stricter than the spec and incompatible with hosted
    stateless servers.

    **Fix**:
    - [x] In `initialize()`, treat `Mcp-Session-Id` as
          optional. If the header is absent, set
          `self._session_id = None` and proceed.
    - [x] In `_base_headers(with_session=True)`, only emit
          the header when `self._session_id is not None`.
    - [x] In `_post_rpc`, the 404 → re-initialize retry
          branch must still work even when no session id
          was issued (re-init reuses the same code path).
    - [x] In `shutdown()`, only DELETE when a session id
          exists (already guarded — verify).
    - [x] Unit test: stateless server (mock returns 200
          without `Mcp-Session-Id`) → `initialize()`
          succeeds, `list_methods()` works, `shutdown()`
          runs clean.
    - [x] Unit test: stateful server (mock returns
          `Mcp-Session-Id: abc`) → header is echoed on
          every subsequent request (regression guard).
    - [x] Re-run
          `tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py::TestGoogleMapsGroundingLite`
          and confirm it passes when
          `GOOGLE_MAPS_API_KEY` is set.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - `MCPStreamableHTTPClient` initializes successfully
      against stateless MCP servers.
    - Existing stateful-server tests still pass without
      modification.
    - The Google Maps live test passes end-to-end with a
      real API key (or skips cleanly when the key is
      absent).

69. [x] **M1348** — `run_tests.sh` menu: auto-count tests + parameterized time estimates ✅

    **Problem.** The main `run_tests.sh` menu hard-codes
    test counts and expected durations per tier ("~4045
    tests, ~45s (xdist)", "89 tests, <5s", etc.). Both
    numbers drift silently: the current unit suite is
    ~4385 tests, bash is 95, and the LLM suites change
    duration cycle to cycle as we add/remove milestones.
    Contributors see stale estimates, which erodes trust
    in the runner output.

    **Decision.** Compute both at runtime:
    - **Counts**: run `pytest --collect-only -q <paths>`
      once at menu-render time per tier and parse the
      trailing `N tests collected` line. Bash counts via
      `grep -c '^@test'` over `tests/bash/*.bats`.
      Cache per-tier counts in-process so the menu
      renders in <300 ms.
    - **Times**: store `avg_seconds_per_test` per tier
      in `utils/test_times.json` (checked in). Menu
      displays `N × avg → total` rounded to the nearest
      useful unit (`~Xs`, `~Xm`, `~Xm Ys`).
      A helper `utils/update_test_times.py` parses the
      `━━━ RECAP ━━━` output from a run log and writes
      back the updated averages, so refreshing the
      numbers is a one-command operation after any
      fresh full-matrix run.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Add `utils/test_times.json` seeded with
          values from the 2026-04-14 recap (unit,
          bash, integration, live, docker, plugin,
          functional, extended).
    - [x] Add `utils/update_test_times.py`: accepts a
          path to a run log (or `-` for stdin),
          parses `━━━ RECAP ━━━` blocks, computes
          `executed_count` (excluding deselected) and
          `elapsed_seconds` per tier, writes back the
          JSON preserving unrelated tiers. Unit tests
          cover pytest-style, bats-style, mixed
          pass/fail lines, deselected exclusion, and
          non-recap content filtering.
    - [x] Refactor `run_tests.sh` menu to read
          `{count, avg_seconds}` from `test_times.json`
          via a `_tier_line` helper and format
          `N tests, ~Xs/~Xm/~Xh`. Falls back to
          "— no data —" if the JSON is missing.
          Source-of-truth is the checked-in JSON,
          not runtime collection (faster menu, no
          flaky `--collect-only` calls).
    - [x] Update `docs/testing.md` with the
          "refresh the numbers after a full run"
          one-liner and updated `.env` precedence.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - The menu shows real counts + estimates computed
      from `test_times.json`, no hard-coded digits left
      in the `show_menu` function.
    - After a full matrix run, running
      `python utils/update_test_times.py <path-to-log>`
      updates the JSON and the next menu invocation
      shows the refreshed estimates.

70. [x] **M1349** — Fix `TestFRulesLifecycle.test_rule_removal_restores_behavior` — use two sessions ✅

    **Problem.** The test adds a safety rule, sends r1
    on session S (messenger refuses), deletes the rule
    from DB, then sends r2 **on the same session S** and
    expects the refusal to vanish. It doesn't: r2's
    messenger still refuses because Kiso's multi-turn
    memory legitimately includes r1 + r1's assistant
    message in r2's context window. The model continues
    in-character from its own prior refusal even though
    the briefer for r2 correctly shows `0 tags`,
    `0 relevant_entities` — the rule is gone from facts,
    but the conversation history still exists. This is
    **correct** multi-turn behavior, not a bug.

    **Fix (test only).** r1 runs on session A to prove
    the rule was active. The rule is deleted. r2 runs on
    a **new, independent session B** so that the
    messenger has no history carrying the refusal
    pattern. Under a clean session, removing the fact
    row is sufficient to restore normal behavior, which
    is what the test set out to measure.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Extend `run_message` fixture with optional
          `session_id` kwarg (conftest.py) — minimal
          surface, default behaviour unchanged for
          other tests.
    - [x] Update
          `TestFRulesLifecycle.test_rule_removal_restores_behavior`
          to build a fresh UUID session for r2 and pass
          it via the new kwarg.
    - [x] Add an inline comment explaining the
          two-session split and the eventually-consistent
          semantics.
    - [x] Run adjacent unit regressions (worker + cli)
          to confirm no regressions; functional run
          deferred to next LLM-credit batch.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - `test_rule_removal_restores_behavior` passes
      consistently on live + extended runs.
    - The test comment explicitly documents why the
      two-session split is required.

71. [x] **M1350** — Document eventually-consistent semantics of safety-rule removal ✅

    **Problem.** Safety rules stored as facts
    (`category=safety`) are loaded by the briefer at
    plan time. Deleting a rule from the DB stops the
    briefer from surfacing it on subsequent plans —
    but any **existing session's chat history** still
    carries the assistant messages that were produced
    **under** that rule, and multi-turn LLM calls
    continue those patterns in-character. Net result:
    rule removal is *eventually consistent* within a
    session; within the same session, prior refusals
    can influence follow-up turns until the session
    ends or is reset. This was investigated during
    M1349 and verified against the failing
    `TestFRulesLifecycle` run on 2026-04-14.

    **Decision: document, do not auto-invalidate.**
    Auto-invalidating chat history on rule delete was
    evaluated and rejected:
    (1) it is overfitted to `category=safety` and
    creates a micro-policy engine,
    (2) it breaks benign flows (experimenting with
    rules, single-turn rules, unrelated session
    context wiped as collateral damage),
    (3) it is a partial fix anyway — curator-derived
    facts and cross-session state are not touched.
    Kiso already exposes `kiso reset session <id>`
    (`cli/reset.py:_reset_session`) which gives the
    operator explicit, auditable control over
    wiping a session's state.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Extend `docs/security.md` with section 11
          "Safety Rules" covering add/remove
          semantics, the eventually-consistent
          session-carryover behaviour, and
          `kiso reset session` as the immediate
          clean-slate lever.
    - [x] Threat-model note included: rule injection
          via compromised admin credentials is a
          credentials compromise, not a safety-rule
          bug.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - The eventually-consistent semantics are written
      down in `docs/` where an operator can find them.
    - `kiso reset session` is referenced as the
      explicit-clean-slate lever.

72. [x] **M1351** — Rewrite `TestF41AiderEditFile` fixture with an unambiguous bug ✅

    **Problem.** The test fixture writes a file with
    `def add(a, b): return a - b` and asks the LLM
    planner to *"use aider to fix the `add` function
    that subtracts instead of summing"*. On the
    2026-04-14 extended run, aider — driven by the
    planner's natural-language instructions — renamed
    the function to `subtract` instead of flipping
    the operator, then the replan loop ran out of
    attempts (5/5) asking for clarification. Log
    shows repeated `Exec task ... stdout=def subtract(a, b):`.

    **Root cause.** The fixture and goal together
    encode an ambiguity a human would also hit:
    "the function that subtracts" can mean either
    *"the function whose body does subtraction"*
    (rename it) or *"the function named add that has
    a bug"* (flip the operator). The current fixture
    makes both readings plausible, so the test becomes
    a coin flip on the planner's natural-language
    generation. The test should measure the aider
    wrapper lifecycle, not LLM disambiguation skill.

    **Decision.** Rewrite the fixture with a
    mechanical, non-ambiguous bug where the function
    name cannot be confused with its behavior:

    ```python
    def compute(a, b):
        return a * b   # bug: should be a + b
    print(compute(3, 4))
    ```

    Goal text: *"il file X contiene la funzione
    `compute` che fa una moltiplicazione invece di
    un'addizione; usa aider per correggerla, poi
    esegui lo script e dimmi il risultato"*. There
    is no rename temptation because `compute` is
    operation-agnostic, and the fix ("change `*` to
    `+`") is a single-character edit aider handles
    surgically.

    **Rejected alternative (option B from analysis).**
    Teaching the planner to send diff-style instructions
    to aider for mechanical bugs was rejected: it
    requires the planner to already know the fix
    before calling aider (negating aider's value),
    introduces a new "surgical vs natural-language"
    heuristic, and for non-mechanical bugs natural
    language remains correct. Option A (fixture
    rewrite) wins without compromise.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Rewrite the fixture file contents in
          `tests/functional/test_advanced_flows.py::TestF41AiderEditFile::test_aider_fixes_bug`
          to the `compute` + `*` form.
    - [x] Update the user-message goal text to match.
    - [x] Update the post-fix exec assertion: `3 * 4
          = 12` pre-fix, `3 + 4 = 7` post-fix. The
          regex already checks for `\b7\b`; 12 does
          not contain `\b7\b`, safe.
    - [ ] Re-run the extended suite focused on F41
          + adjacent aider tests — deferred to next
          LLM-credit extended run.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - `TestF41AiderEditFile.test_aider_fixes_bug`
      passes consistently with the new fixture.
    - The fixture + goal text contain no naming
      ambiguity that could plausibly invite a rename.

73. [x] **M1352** — Probe-gated `deps.sh` re-run on `kiso wrapper install` ✅

    **Problem.** `kiso wrapper install X` runs `deps.sh`
    **unconditionally**, even when X is already installed
    and the system state is healthy. `deps.sh` typically
    wraps `apt-get install`, `pip install`,
    `playwright install`, or similar provisioning
    commands. This conflates two distinct operations:
    provisioning (rare, expensive) and readiness check
    (frequent, cheap). Observed consequences on
    2026-04-14 full matrix run:

    - `TestF2WikipediaPython` timed out after the
      reviewer correctly diagnosed *"another process
      was using the dpkg frontend lock, preventing the
      browser wrapper dependencies from being
      refreshed"*. The lock holder was almost
      certainly `unattended-upgrades`, which is
      statistically guaranteed to fire inside a ~2h
      matrix run.
    - Every real user pays redundant apt calls on
      every wrapper invocation flow, not just in tests.

    **Root cause.** Kiso has no concept of *"this
    wrapper is already provisioned and healthy, skip
    re-provisioning"*. It always re-runs `deps.sh`,
    which is the moral equivalent of running
    `apt install vim` every time you open vim.

    **Decision: probe-gated skip.** Wrappers may
    declare an optional `health_check` command in
    their `kiso.toml`. On `kiso wrapper install X`
    when X is already installed:

    1. Read the wrapper's manifest version from the
       local clone and compare it to the version in
       the fetched registry entry.
    2. If versions match AND `health_check` is
       declared AND the command exits 0, skip
       `deps.sh` entirely and report
       `"already installed (version N.N, health: ok)"`.
    3. Otherwise (no probe declared, probe fails, or
       version drift), run `deps.sh` exactly as today.

    `--force` flag on `kiso wrapper install`
    bypasses the gate entirely for manual recovery.

    **Why this is generalist, not overfitted.**
    - The policy never mentions `browser`, `apt`,
      `chromium`, or `dpkg`. It is a cache-invalidation
      policy keyed on (version, probe).
    - Applies uniformly to every wrapper.
    - Resolves the class of problems: apt contention
      on `browser`, redundant `pip install` on
      `aider`, redundant `playwright install` on
      `ocr`, and any future wrapper with expensive
      provisioning.

    **Why it does not break legitimate use cases.**
    - Wrappers without `health_check` keep current
      behaviour byte-for-byte — zero regression.
      Opt-in per wrapper.
    - Manifest version bump → check fails → full
      `deps.sh` runs. Upstream changes with new deps
      are still caught.
    - Corrupted system state (someone
      `apt remove`d a required package) → probe
      fails → `deps.sh` runs. Self-healing.
    - `--force` always available as explicit
      escape hatch.

    **Residual risk.** A probe too shallow to catch a
    real failure (e.g. `chromium --version` passes
    but the binary crashes in headless mode) skips a
    `deps.sh` that would have helped. Mitigation:
    probe quality is the wrapper author's
    responsibility; no probe declared → safe default
    (always run); `--force` always available.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Define the `health_check` field as an
          optional string under `[kiso]` in the
          plugin's `kiso.toml`. Manifest parsing is
          already generic (`tomllib.load`), no
          schema update needed.
    - [x] Unit tests for the gate decision function
          (`tests/test_plugin_install_gate.py`, 11
          cases): --no-deps, missing deps.sh,
          --force, pull changed, no probe, healthy
          probe, failing probe; plus
          `_run_health_check` helper (exit 0, non-0,
          missing binary, empty string).
    - [x] Implement the gate in
          `cli/plugin_ops._plugin_install` — the
          "already installed" branch now reads
          `health_check`, runs the probe, and calls
          `_gate_deps_decision`. Used by both
          wrapper and connector install flows.
    - [x] Add `--force` flag to both `kiso wrapper
          install` and `kiso connector install`.
    - [ ] Update `kiso.toml` of the official
          `browser`/`aider`/`ocr` wrappers — lives
          in external repos, deferred: this core
          change is backward-compatible so wrapper
          repos can adopt `health_check` at their
          own pace.
    - [x] Update `docs/wrappers.md` with the
          `health_check` field, gate truth table,

    - [ ] Functional regression on a host with

          passed).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**

      `deps.sh` execution.

74. [x] **M1353** — `preset_tools_installed` fixture: generous cold-install budget ✅

    **Problem.** The `preset_tools_installed` fixture
    in `tests/functional/conftest.py` shells out to
    `uv run kiso wrapper install browser` (and sibling
    tools) with a 300s subprocess timeout. On the
    2026-04-14 matrix run this timed out during the
    cold install of `browser` because chromium
    provisioning on a loaded host can exceed 5
    minutes. This is a genuinely expensive operation
    the first time the fixture runs — M1352 cannot
    help here because there is nothing to skip.

    **Decision: raise the fixture-level subprocess
    timeout to 1800s (30 min).** The fixture is
    session-scoped (one install per functional run),
    so the budget is paid at most once per suite
    invocation. Per-test timeouts are unaffected.

    **Why this is safe.**
    - The timeout raise is strictly local to the
      fixture subprocess call. No production code
      path touches this value.
    - 1800s is a generous cap that accommodates
      cold apt + chromium downloads on loaded CI
      hosts. On a fast machine the real install
      finishes in ~1–2 minutes; the headroom costs
      nothing when the install succeeds quickly.
    - If the install genuinely hangs forever, the
      fixture still fails — just after 30 min
      instead of 5.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Raised the `subprocess.run` timeout in
          `preset_tools_installed` from 300 to
          1800 seconds with an inline comment
          citing the cold chromium install cost.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when:**
    - A cold `preset_tools_installed` run on a
      loaded host no longer races against a 300s
      timeout for a legitimate slow install.
    - No change to per-test timeouts or to any
      non-fixture code.

75. [x] **M1354** — Validator: neutral feedback on `install_proposal + search` conflict ✅

    **Why.** In the 2026-04-15 full matrix,
    `TestSearchTaskFlow.test_planner_emits_search_for_web_query`
    failed because the planner drafted `[search, replan]`
    with `install_proposal=True`. The validator correctly
    detected the contradiction but returned a prescriptive
    feedback message — *"End the plan with a msg asking
    for approval"* — which biased the planner's retry
    toward dropping the `search` task instead of dropping
    `install_proposal`. On retry the planner reduced to
    `[msg]` and the test failed with
    `Expected at least one data-gathering task
    (search/exec/wrapper), got: ['msg']`.

    This is a real product bug, not a test flake: `search`
    is a built-in Kiso task type that never needs a wrapper
    installed. Whenever a plan has both a `search` task and
    `install_proposal=True`, the proposal is spurious by
    construction (the planner can already fulfil the task
    via the built-in).

    **Approach.** Two coordinated changes, both minimal:

    1. In `kiso/brain/planner.py`, detect the specific
       combo `install_proposal=True` **and** any
       `type == "search"` in `tasks`, and emit a
       dedicated feedback message that explicitly
       instructs the planner to drop `install_proposal`
       and keep the search task(s). Phrasing biases
       toward the semantically correct resolution
       ("search is built-in, no install needed") instead
       of the current prescriptive "end with msg".
    2. In `kiso/roles/planner.md`, add one line under
       the existing install guidance clarifying that
       `install_proposal` / `needs_install` must never
       be set on a plan that already contains a
       `search` task, because built-in search needs no
       wrapper.

    **No in-place mutation of the plan object**: the
    validator still returns errors, the planner still
    retries. Only the feedback string changes. This keeps
    the validator a pure function with no hidden side
    effects.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Unit test
          `test_needs_install_with_search_bias_drop_proposal`
          in `tests/test_brain.py::TestM984NeedsInstallMsgOnly`:
          plan with needs_install + one search task
          → feedback contains "built-in" and "drop
          needs_install", NOT "end the plan with a msg".
    - [x] Guard unit test
          `test_needs_install_with_exec_keeps_legacy_reduce_to_msg`:
          exec+needs_install still gets legacy
          reduce-to-msg feedback (rule did not widen).
    - [x] Implement the dedicated branch in
          `validate_plan` (kiso/brain/planner.py:803),
          firing only when non-msg tasks are
          exclusively `TASK_TYPE_SEARCH`.
    - [x] Add one-line guidance in
          `kiso/roles/planner.md` Install section.
          Planner prompt size stays under 15600 char
          budget.
    - [ ] Re-run
          `tests/live/test_flows.py::TestSearchTaskFlow`
          — deferred to next LLM-credit run.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - Unit test for the new feedback passes.
    - No regression in the existing validator unit
      tests (plans with exec/wrapper + install_proposal
      still receive the reduce-to-msg feedback).
    - The dedicated feedback string cannot be confused
      with the legacy one (different wording).

76. [x] **M1355** — Fix `test_system_package_uses_apt` assertion field ✅

    **Why.** The test checks `"apt" in details` where
    `details` is built as `" ".join(t.get("detail", "")
    for t in plan["tasks"])`. The `detail` field is a
    human-readable description, not the shell command.
    On the 2026-04-15 run the model correctly produced
    an exec task but described it as *"update package
    list and install timg package"* — semantically
    perfect, syntactically missing the literal "apt"
    substring. Test failed on a brittle assertion over
    the wrong field.

    **Approach.** In
    `tests/live/test_roles.py::TestPlannerSystemPackageLive::test_system_package_uses_apt`,
    widen the haystack to include all plausible string
    fields on exec tasks (`command`, `detail`, `expect`)
    and use a word-boundary regex for `apt|apt-get`
    instead of a raw substring. The sibling test
    `test_python_lib_uses_uv_pip` likely has the same
    shape — audit and apply the same widening there if
    present.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Widened haystack in both
          `test_system_package_uses_apt` and
          `test_python_lib_uses_uv_pip` to include
          `detail`, `expect`, `command`, `args`
          across every exec task.
    - [x] Used `re.search(r"\b(apt|apt-get|dpkg|package)\b", haystack)`
          for the apt positive assertion — accepts
          natural-language paraphrases like *"update
          package list and install timg"* that would
          have failed a literal `"apt" in details`
          check on 2026-04-15.
    - [x] Used `re.search(r"\b(apt|apt-get|dpkg)\b", haystack)`
          for the Python lib negative assertion with
          word boundary (no false positive on
          "adapt").
    - [x] Added `pip` / `uv pip` negative guard on
          the apt test to symmetrically block the
          wrong package manager.
    - [ ] Re-run the `TestPlannerSystemPackageLive`
          class against a live LLM — deferred to
          next LLM-credit run.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - The test passes on any plan that contains an exec
      task whose command uses `apt` or `apt-get`,
      regardless of where in the task fields the word
      appears.
    - The test still fails cleanly when the planner
      emits a `search` or `pip install` for a system
      package query (the anti-regression assertion is
      preserved).

77. [x] **M1356** — LLM transport retry: catch `ssl.SSLError` as transient ✅

    **Why.** The 2026-04-15 run of
    `TestFProjBoundFact.test_project_fact_visible_to_bound_session`
    crashed with
    `ssl.SSLError: [SSL: SSLV3_ALERT_BAD_RECORD_MAC]`
    during an httpx call to OpenRouter. `kiso/llm.py`
    already has a bounded transport retry for
    `httpx.RequestError` (2 attempts, exponential
    backoff) at lines 509-525, but `ssl.SSLError` can
    escape mid-stream reads without being wrapped by
    httpx, so the retry branch was never taken. In
    production this means a real network/TLS hiccup
    kills a running plan instead of self-healing.

    **Approach.** In `kiso/llm.py` `call_llm`, add
    `ssl.SSLError` to the except chain **as a transport
    error**, reusing the exact same retry-budget
    machinery (`_transport_retries`,
    `_MAX_TRANSPORT_RETRIES`, exponential backoff).
    Exclude `ssl.SSLCertVerificationError` from the
    retryable set — certificate verification failures
    are permanent configuration issues, not transients,
    and retrying them wastes budget and masks the real
    cause.

    - Retryable: `ssl.SSLError` (base) except
      `SSLCertVerificationError` — covers
      `BAD_RECORD_MAC`, `SSLEOFError`,
      `SSLZeroReturnError`, `SSLSyscallError`.
    - Non-retryable: `SSLCertVerificationError` —
      propagates immediately as `LLMError` with the
      original cert message.
    - Budget unchanged: still 2 retries total,
      shared with `httpx.RequestError`.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Unit test `test_ssl_error_retried_and_recovers`:
          first call raises `ssl.SSLError(BAD_RECORD_MAC)`,
          second succeeds, `call_llm` returns with one
          transport retry.
    - [x] Unit test
          `test_ssl_cert_verification_error_not_retried`:
          `SSLCertVerificationError` → fail fast, no
          retry consumed.
    - [x] Unit test `test_ssl_error_exhausted_raises_llm_error`:
          persistent SSL errors drain budget and surface
          as `LLMError` citing `SSLError` class name.
    - [x] Implement: `except ssl.SSLError` after
          `httpx.RequestError`, early short-circuit on
          `SSLCertVerificationError`, shared retry
          budget.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - The three new unit tests pass.
    - A transient SSL bad-record-mac no longer crashes
      a running plan — the retry path recovers.
    - Cert verification errors still fail fast with a
      clear message.

79. [x] **M1358** — Validator error messages: neutrality audit ✅

    **Why.** M1354 uncovered one instance of a
    prescriptive validator feedback message that
    biased the planner toward the wrong correction
    when multiple resolutions were legitimate. The
    class of bug is "validator error message dictates
    a single fix path when more than one exists" —
    there are very likely other instances in
    `kiso/brain/planner.py`'s `validate_plan` helpers,
    since many error strings were added organically as
    specific failure modes were discovered. An audit
    pass catches them before they surface as flaky
    tests or surprising planner behaviour in
    production.

    **Approach.** Read every error string returned by
    `validate_plan` and its helpers. For each:

    1. Identify whether the validation rule has **one**
       or **multiple** legitimate resolutions.
    2. If **one** (e.g. *"Task details must be
       non-empty"*), the prescriptive message is fine
       and stays.
    3. If **multiple**, rewrite the message to list
       the options without biasing the retry (pattern:
       *"X conflicts with Y. Either drop X and keep Y,
       or drop Y and keep X"*).

    The audit is read-only against prod logic — only
    error string literals change. Existing validator
    behaviour is untouched.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Enumerated all 62 `errors.append(...)` calls
          in `kiso/brain/planner.py` under
          `validate_plan` and helpers via AST pass.
    - [x] Classified each as single-resolution or
          multi-resolution. Most are genuinely SR
          (strict schema rules), and the MR ones
          already present alternatives neutrally
          (L256 install-name routing, L326 wrapper
          not installed, L508 msg-only rejection,
          L838 kb_answer coherence, L559 last-task
          type). The main systemic bias was the
          needs_install+search combo fixed in M1354.
    - [x] **One borderline case refined**: the
          artifact-goal-mismatch message (planner.py
          L786) prescribed "Add an exec task" even
          though the validator check at L782 accepts
          both `exec` and `wrapper` as resolutions.
          Rewritten to present both options
          explicitly (*"Add an action task — either
          an exec task ... or a wrapper task ..."*).
    - [x] Unit test
          `test_artifact_message_does_not_prescribe_only_exec`
          in `TestArtifactGoalMismatch` guards the
          new wording against drift.
    - [x] Full `tests/test_brain.py` regression
          passes (964/964).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Audit outcome**: the validator was not
    systemically biased. The `needs_install + search`
    case fixed in M1354 was the one genuine offender
    in multi-resolution territory; one more borderline
    case (L786 artifact creation) refined here. All
    other error strings are either single-resolution
    (and correctly imperative) or already list
    alternatives neutrally.

    **Done when**:
    - Every multi-resolution validator error message
      has been rewritten to present options rather
      than prescribe a specific fix direction.
    - Single-resolution messages are preserved as-is.
    - Unit tests guard the new wording against future
      drift.

80. [x] **M1359** — `run_tests.sh`: auto-offer refresh of `test_times.json` after full matrix ✅

    **Why.** M1348 added `utils/update_test_times.py`
    as a manual post-run step — contributors who run
    the full matrix have to remember to feed the log
    back through it. In practice they won't, and
    `utils/test_times.json` will drift again. A one
    line prompt at the end of a full-matrix run,
    offering the refresh, eliminates the drift without
    forcing the update.

    **Approach.** After a full matrix run completes
    (`./utils/run_tests.sh a` or equivalent — the
    "All automatic" path), if the run output contains
    a complete `━━━ RECAP ━━━` block AND stdin is a
    TTY, prompt *"Update utils/test_times.json from
    this run? [y/N] "*. On `y`, pipe the captured log
    through `uv run python utils/update_test_times.py -`
    and print the summary. On anything else, print
    *"skipped — run `uv run python utils/update_test_times.py <log>`
    manually if you change your mind"* and exit
    normally. Non-interactive CI runs (no TTY) skip
    the prompt entirely.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Added `_offer_test_times_refresh` helper
          in `utils/run_tests.sh` after `_print_recap`.
          Guards: TTY, ≥3 suites, updater exists,
          log exists.
    - [x] On `y` pipes `_CAPTURE_LOG` through
          `uv run python utils/update_test_times.py`;
          on anything else prints the manual-run
          reminder.
    - [x] Bats test
          `tests/bash/test_run_tests_refresh_offer.bats`
          verifies all four silent-skip paths
          (non-TTY, few suites, missing updater,
          missing log).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - A contributor running `./utils/run_tests.sh a`
      interactively sees the refresh prompt after the
      RECAP.
    - CI / non-interactive runs see no prompt and no
      behavioural change.
    - Declining the prompt leaves `test_times.json`
      untouched and exits cleanly.

81. [x] **M1360** — Strip milestone ID references from production code ✅

    **Why.** The feedback rule
    `feedback_no_milestone_refs_in_code.md` says milestone
    identifiers (M###, M####) belong in commit messages
    and the devplan, not in source code. An audit on
    2026-04-15 found 29 such references across 16 files
    under `kiso/` and `cli/`. This is the smallest
    surface — ideal warm-up for the tool we use in
    M1361/M1362 and zero risk of breaking imports
    (comments/docstrings only, no symbol renames).

    **Approach.** A scrubbing pass via Python AST walks
    each file, identifies comment tokens and docstring
    `ast.Constant(str)` at module/class/function level,
    strips leading `M###:` / `(M###)` / `# --- M###: `
    patterns while preserving the descriptive content.
    Empty or trivial lines remaining after stripping
    are removed entirely. String literals inside
    expressions (test data, config values) are never
    touched.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Built an AST-based scrubber (`/tmp/scrubber.py`,
          throwaway) that identifies comment tokens and
          module/class/function docstring ranges, then
          strips `M###` / `M###-N:` / `(M###)` / `— M###`
          patterns while preserving visual dividers and
          unchanged lines.
    - [x] Scrubber bug fix round-trip: early pass
          dropped legitimate `# -----` visual dividers
          when no scrub had actually touched them;
          fixed by making drop conditional on actual
          substitution before reverting and re-running.
    - [x] Applied to `kiso/**/*.py` and `cli/**/*.py`
          → 35 hits across 20 files.
    - [x] 5 residuals in `kiso/brain/common.py` are
          `# noqa: M1320-allow` linter directives used
          by `test_rename_completeness.py` — functional
          markers, not cruft, deliberately preserved.
    - [x] Full host unit suite stays green
          (4406 passed).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - `uv run pytest tests/` excluding live/functional
      stays green.
    - Grep for `\bM\d{2,4}\b` in `kiso/` + `cli/`
      comments returns zero hits.

    safely. If referenced elsewhere (unlikely but

84. [x] **M1363** — Fix M1359 auto-refresh: write recap block to `_CAPTURE_LOG` ✅

    **Why.** On the 2026-04-15 full matrix run the
    M1359 auto-refresh prompt fired and the user said
    yes, but the updater reported *"no recap block
    found in input"* and bailed out. Root cause:
    `_print_recap` in `utils/run_tests.sh` writes the
    `━━━ RECAP ━━━` block to stdout only; it never
    appends to `_CAPTURE_LOG`. `_offer_test_times_refresh`
    passes `_CAPTURE_LOG` to `update_test_times.py`,
    which correctly reports no recap because that file
    never contained one. This is a bug I introduced in
    M1359 — the integration path wasn't tested.

    **Approach.** The minimal fix is to capture
    `_print_recap`'s output via `tee -a "$_CAPTURE_LOG"`
    so the recap block lands in the same file the
    updater reads. The bats tests from M1359 already
    cover the silent-skip paths; add one test that
    feeds a known-good recap snippet to the updater
    and asserts the JSON is refreshed.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Wrapped `_print_recap` with
          `| tee -a "$_CAPTURE_LOG"` so the block
          lands in the file the updater reads.
    - [x] Added end-to-end updater tests in
          `tests/test_update_test_times.py::TestMainEndToEnd`:
          `test_main_writes_json_from_captured_log`
          feeds a realistic recap log (with pytest
          noise, blank lines, failure summary
          marker) through `main()` and asserts the
          JSON is written correctly;
          `test_main_reports_error_when_recap_missing`
          guards the error path.
    - [ ] Manual smoke: re-run
          `./utils/run_tests.sh a` interactively —
          deferred to next matrix run.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - `_CAPTURE_LOG` contains the RECAP block after a
      full run.
    - `_offer_test_times_refresh` accepted with `y`
      completes the JSON refresh without error.
