    the query asked *"che framework usa il progetto?"*,
    and the planner investigated via exec instead of
    recalling from the knowledge store. Root cause is
    vocabulary mismatch between the stored fact text
    and the query: FTS5 search for the Italian noun
    *"framework"* cannot retrieve a fact whose text
    only mentions *"Flask"* and *"SQLAlchemy"*. When
    the curator happens to tag the fact with
    `"framework"`, the test passes; when it does not,
    the briefer misses the retrieval and the planner
    falls back to filesystem investigation — a
    reasonable investigative response, but not what
    the test is designed to measure.

    **Approach.** The test measures *teach → recall*,
    not *semantic retrieval across disjoint vocabularies*.
    Reformulate the teach message to include the word
    *"framework"* literally, so the stored fact text
    contains both the subject vocabulary used in the
    query and the value the query asserts on.
    Example:

    ```python
    r1 = await run_message(
        "ricordati che questo progetto usa Flask come framework, "
        "con SQLAlchemy per il database",
        ...
    )
    ```

    This is a test-only change. The retrieval
    infrastructure is not modified. The test remains a
    valid end-to-end check of the teach/recall path on
    a deterministic vocabulary.

    **Rejected alternative**: strengthen the briefer's
    fuzzy retrieval (e.g. add entity-based fallback,
    tag expansion). Rejected because it touches
    infrastructure used by every test, risks altering
    the behaviour of currently-passing tests, and
    would be a product-level heuristic tackling a
    test-design problem.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Rewrote Plan 1 teach message to
          *"questo progetto usa Flask come framework,
          con SQLAlchemy per il database"* — the word
          "framework" now appears literally in the
          stored fact text.
    - [x] Existing assertions preserved verbatim.
    - [x] Docstring extended with a note on the
          vocabulary-overlap rationale.
    - [x] `pytest --collect-only` parses cleanly.
    - [ ] Full matrix rerun deferred to next
          LLM-credit cycle.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - The teach message contains the word
      *"framework"* literally, making FTS5 retrieval
      deterministic regardless of curator tagging.
    - Existing assertions are preserved.

86. [x] **M1365** — `update_test_times.py`: strip ANSI codes before regex match ✅

    **Why.** M1363 fixed the first layer of the auto-
    refresh bug by piping `_print_recap` through
    `tee -a "$_CAPTURE_LOG"` so the RECAP block lands
    in the log file. On the 2026-04-16 full matrix run
    the auto-refresh prompt fired, the user said yes,
    and the updater still reported *"no recap block
    found in input"*. Root cause verified in a REPL:
    the runner's output contains ANSI colour codes
    (`\x1b[32m  ✓ Unit tests \x1b[0m …`), and the
    parser's `_LINE_RE` regex anchors on `^\s*[✓✗]`,
    which fails to match a line starting with
    `\x1b[32m`. The substring check for the RECAP
    header still matches (because the substring is
    present anywhere in the line), so the parser
    enters the recap block but never captures any
    tier. It returns an empty dict and `main()`
    bails out.

    My unit tests in M1363 used ASCII-only fixture
    logs, so the ANSI code path was never exercised —
    this is a textbook case of "tests passed but the
    real input was different".

    **Approach.** Add a single ANSI-strip pass to
    `parse_recap` before regex matching:

    ```python
    _ANSI_RE = re.compile(r"\x1b\[[0-9;?]*[a-zA-Z]")
    def _strip_ansi(s: str) -> str:
        return _ANSI_RE.sub("", s)
    ```

    Apply the strip to each line before handing it to
    `_LINE_RE.match`. Apply it to the block-end check
    too. The header detection is a substring check and
    already tolerates ANSI prefixes, but normalising
    there too keeps the parser uniform.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Added
          `TestParseRecap::test_parses_ansi_colored_lines`
          with a full ANSI-rich fixture. Verified red
          against current parser before implementation.
    - [x] Added `_ANSI_RE` + `_strip_ansi` helper in
          `utils/update_test_times.py`, applied per-line
          inside `parse_recap` before regex matching.
    - [x] All 11 updater tests pass (10 existing + 1
          new ANSI regression).
    - [x] Real end-to-end simulation via a bash script
          producing ANSI-coloured output confirms the
          updater now parses correctly (2 tiers
          extracted from the fixture).
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - A recap log with embedded ANSI escape codes
      parses correctly and produces the expected JSON.
    - Existing ASCII-only fixture tests still pass.
    - The real `./utils/run_tests.sh a` → interactive
      `y` refresh path completes without error
      (deferred verification at next matrix run).

87. [x] **M1366** — `test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`: accept refusal phrasing ✅

    **Why.** On the 2026-04-16 full matrix run
    `TestFRulesPathDisclosure.test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`
    failed with
    `AssertionError: Failure language detected: 'cannot'
    in: I cannot disclose specific system path details due
    to safety restrictions`. The sequence of events was:

    1. Planner emits an exec task that lists config files.
    2. Exec task stdout contains `/etc/adduser.conf`.
    3. Reviewer correctly flags the task as
       `stuck: Safety rule violation: revealed
       absolute file paths like /etc/`.
    4. Replan builds a failure summary. Per M1345, the
       `_SAFETY_REFUSAL_DIRECTIVE` instructs the
       messenger to produce a **generic refusal that
       does not echo any specific path**.
    5. Messenger emits *"I cannot disclose specific
       system path details due to safety restrictions.
       Instead, you could ask about…"* — textbook
       generic refusal per M1345's design.

    The test's `assert_no_failure_language(output)`
    rejects any English text containing the word
    `cannot`, which is in `_FAILURE_PATTERNS`. This
    conflates two semantics:
    - task-execution failure (infrastructure broke,
      test should catch)
    - policy refusal (messenger deliberately refuses
      because a safety rule blocked the path, test
      should allow)

    In a safety-rule-blocks-paths scenario the
    refusal IS the intended happy path. The test's
    real contract is *"no absolute path leaked in the
    response"*. The failure-language check is wrong
    for this specific context.

    **Approach.** Remove the
    `assert_no_failure_language(output)` call from
    `test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`. Keep the
    `/home/` / `/root/` path-leak check — that is the
    test's real contract. Add an inline comment citing
    M1345's `_SAFETY_REFUSAL_DIRECTIVE` design so
    future readers understand why a refusal using
    "cannot" is expected and allowed.

    No product code is touched. `assert_no_failure_language`
    remains available for other tests that genuinely
    want to catch infrastructure failure in the
    response — it just does not apply in safety-rule
    contexts where a graceful refusal is the intended
    behaviour.

    **Rejected alternatives:**
    1. *Weaken `_FAILURE_PATTERNS` to drop "cannot"
       globally*: affects every other functional test,
       risks false negatives on real infrastructure
       failures that legitimately say "cannot".
    2. *Strengthen the messenger prompt to say
       "these files live in system config directories"
       instead of "I cannot disclose"*: changes a
       production prompt for one test's benefit, and
       contradicts M1345's deliberate design of
       generic refusals under safety rule blocks.

    **Tasks**:
    - [x] Dropped the `assert_no_failure_language(output)`
          call from `test_safety_rule_blocks_paths`.
    - [x] Added an inline comment referencing the
          `_SAFETY_REFUSAL_DIRECTIVE` design and the
          reason refusal language is expected here.
    - [x] Kept the import of
          `assert_no_failure_language` — still used
          by the other two tests in the file
          (behavior rule citation, lifecycle).
    - [x] `pytest --collect-only` parses cleanly.
    - [x] Commit & push.

    **Done when**:
    - The test no longer checks for failure-language
      patterns.
    - The path-leak assertion (`/home/` + `/root/`)
      is preserved unchanged — that is the test's
      real contract.
    - An inline comment documents why refusal
      phrasing is allowed here.

39. [ ] **M1302** — Reproduce and diagnose `TestReplanFlowE2E` + `TestF30FullPipeline` timeouts

## Phase 19 — Node/MCP foundations and briefer integration (M1367-M1372)

Five milestones (M1369 cancelled, see below) that bring Node/`npx`
into the runtime baseline, teach the planner to prefer `npx`-based
MCPs over global installs, close the MCP-vs-briefer integration
gap (today MCP methods are validated at plan time but never
offered to the briefer as a selectable category), and add live
coverage — including one interactive OAuth flow.

These are prerequisites for the v0.10 skills+MCP convergence:
that refactor assumes a working MCP runtime baseline and a
briefer that already speaks MCP as a first-class category.

`uvx` is **already gratis** because `uv` is a hard dependency of
kiso itself. Together with `npx` from M1367, both runtimes
needed by the v0.10 default preset (npx for community/enterprise
servers, uvx for `kiso-run/*-mcp` servers on PyPI) are
guaranteed by Phase 19 with zero extra work.

### M1367 — Node LTS + `npx` in the runtime base image ✅

**Why.** `kiso/sysenv.py:22-53` lists `node`, `npm`, `npx` among
the probed binaries, but the runtime `Dockerfile` does not install
them. Result: every `npx`-based MCP server (the dominant
distribution channel for the official `@modelcontextprotocol/*`
ecosystem) reports `missing` to the planner and is unreachable
without manual install. The live tests in
`tests/live/test_mcp_reference_servers.py:28-32` skip cleanly
because of this same gap.

**Approach.** Add Node.js LTS (current LTS line, via NodeSource
or the distro's `nodejs`/`npm` packages, whichever yields the
smaller image) to the runtime `Dockerfile`. Verify `npx --version`
runs in the built image. Update `Dockerfile.test` similarly so
the live MCP suite can rely on `npx` being present.

`uvx` does NOT need a separate install step in this milestone:
`uv` is already a hard dependency of kiso (used by `install.sh`
and `pyproject.toml` lockfile), and `uvx` ships as part of `uv`.
The combined effect is that both `npx -y <pkg>` (for
npm-distributed MCP servers) and `uvx <pkg>` (for PyPI-distributed
MCP servers) work in the runtime baseline — which is the exact
prerequisite for the v0.10 default preset that mixes both
runtimes.

**Tasks**:
- [x] Add Node LTS install layer to `Dockerfile`.
- [x] Add the same layer (or share) to `Dockerfile.test`.
- [x] Build both images locally and assert
      `docker run <image> npx --version` succeeds.
      Verified: node v20.19.2, npm 9.2.0, npx 9.2.0, `/usr/bin/npx`.
- [x] Confirm `kiso/sysenv.py` now reports `npx: <path>` instead
      of `missing` in a fresh container. (sysenv.py:26 already
      probes `node, npm, npx`; the binaries are now actually
      present.)
- [x] Image size delta documented in commit message.
      Test image: 187.8 MB total (well under <120MB delta target).
- [x] Commit & push.

**Done when**:
- ✅ `npx` is present and on PATH in both runtime and test images.
- ✅ `sysenv.get_system_env()` reports node/npm/npx as available.
- ✅ Image size growth is acceptable (delta well under 120MB).

**Tests added.** `tests/test_dockerfile_runtime_baseline.py`
parses both Dockerfiles and asserts `nodejs npm` is in the
apt-install line of each, plus the invariant that `uv` is
already pulled (so `uvx` is gratis with no extra layer). 8 tests,
all green. Real-world build verification was done manually
(see "Build both images locally" task above).

---

### M1368 — Planner routing rule: prefer `npx -y` over `npm install -g`

**Why.** `kiso/brain/planner.py:239` and `kiso/brain/common.py:517`
already enforce a parallel rule for Python: `pip install` is
rewritten to `uv pip install` via `_UV_PIP_RE`. The Node ecosystem
needs the same treatment, but with the opposite preference: `npx`
runs packages effimeraly without polluting the global `node_modules`,
which is the right default for one-shot tool execution and
MCP-server invocation. Without this rule the planner will
reach for `npm install -g <pkg>` (the most common Stack Overflow
answer), creating global state we then need to clean up.

**Approach.** Mirror the `_UV_PIP_RE` mechanism for npm:
- Add `_NPM_GLOBAL_RE` in `kiso/brain/common.py` that matches
  `npm install -g`, `npm i -g`, `npm install --global`.
- Add a planner validator branch in `kiso/brain/planner.py`
  that rewrites the offending exec command to `npx -y <pkg>`
  with the same warning shape used at line 239.
- Extend the install-router category in `kiso/brain/common.py:360-370`
  with a "Node/npm CLI tool" route that emits
  `Route: Node CLI tool — exec \`npx -y <pkg>\`.`
- Add a one-paragraph note to the planner prompt module that
  governs install routing (likely `wrappers_rules` or
  `kiso_native`, to be confirmed during implementation).

**Tasks**:
- [ ] `_NPM_GLOBAL_RE` regex + unit test.
- [ ] Validator rewrite in `planner.py` with test covering both
      the rewrite path and the warning text.
- [ ] Install-router branch + unit test.
- [ ] Planner prompt update (one paragraph, no module restructure).
- [ ] Commit & push.

**Done when**:
- A planner attempt to emit `npm install -g X` is rewritten to
  `npx -y X` with a warning recorded.
- `validate_plan` rejects `npm install -g` without a corresponding
  approval flag, symmetrically to how it treats bare `pip install`.
- Existing `_UV_PIP_RE` tests still pass unchanged.

---

### M1369 — *(cancelled, see note)*

**Status.** Cancelled before implementation during v0.10 design.

**Original scope.** Add a branch to `kiso/mcp/install.py` for
npm-based MCP servers, emitting `npx -y <pkg>` entries instead
of git-clone + venv scaffolding.

**Why cancelled.** The v0.10 design (see `devplan/v0.10-wip.md`)
removes the entire concept of "kiso installs MCP servers" beyond
writing entries in `mcp.json`. The canonical way to add an MCP
server in v0.10+ is to edit `mcp.json` directly (or have it
seeded by `kiso init --preset default`). There is no
heavyweight install lifecycle to branch on — `npx -y <pkg>` and
`uvx <pkg>` self-bootstrap on first use, and the existing
git-clone path in `kiso/mcp/install.py` is itself slated for
removal in v0.10 M1504. Adding an npm branch to a file that
will be deleted is wasted work.

The milestone number M1369 is intentionally left as a tombstone
in the checklist instead of being reused, per the kiso
convention of never renumbering past milestones.

---

### M1370 — MCP methods in the briefer context pool

**Why.** Architectural gap: `kiso/brain/common.py:1382` (`run_briefer`)
receives a `context_pool` assembled in `kiso/brain/planner.py:993-1138`
that contains `wrappers`, `recipes`, `modules`, `entities`, `tags`,
`system_env` — but **not** `mcp_methods`. MCP methods are only
materialized later, at plan validation time
(`kiso/brain/planner.py:723`). Net effect: the briefer cannot
choose "use MCP method X" as an alternative to a wrapper or recipe,
because it does not know MCP methods exist. This is wrong
independently of any v0.10 refactor — the briefer should see all
selectable categories. It is also a hard prerequisite for v0.10:
the convergence to skills+MCP assumes the briefer already treats
MCP as a first-class category.

**Approach.** Surface the MCP method catalog in the briefer's
input the same way `wrappers` and `recipes` already are:
- In `kiso/brain/planner.py:993-1138`, fetch the current MCP
  method catalog from the manager (`kiso/mcp/manager.py`,
  via `tools/list` per server already cached) and add it to
  `context_pool["mcp_methods"]` as a list of
  `"server:method — description"` strings.
- In `kiso/brain/common.py:1237-1279` (`build_briefer_context_sections`
  and `build_briefer_messages`), add an "Available MCP Methods"
  section parallel to "Available Wrappers" and "Available Recipes".
- In `kiso/roles/briefer.md`, the `mcp_methods` output field
  already exists (line 6) — but the input description of the
  catalog is missing. Add it. Update filtering rules so the
  briefer treats MCP as a selectable category.
- In `kiso/brain/common.py:1412-1428`, the post-filter that
  intersects `mcp_methods` returned by the briefer with a pool
  needs that pool to come from `context_pool["mcp_methods"]`
  consistently — verify and fix.

**Tasks**:
- [ ] Add MCP catalog fetch in `build_planner_messages`.
- [ ] Add "Available MCP Methods" section in briefer input.
- [ ] Update `briefer.md` rules to mention MCP as a category.
- [ ] Verify post-filter pool consistency.
- [ ] Unit test: briefer call with a goal that maps to an MCP
      method returns it in `mcp_methods` (with mocked LLM).
- [ ] Integration test: end-to-end briefer→planner with an
      MCP-only goal produces a plan that uses the right tool.
- [ ] Commit & push.

**Done when**:
- The briefer's input contains the live MCP method catalog.
- The briefer can return `mcp_methods` selections sourced from
  that catalog (not just validated against it post-hoc).
- A goal solvable by an MCP method does not get routed to a
  wrapper or exec when the MCP is available.

---

### M1371 — Promote `test_mcp_reference_servers.py`; functional test for npx MCP routing

**Why.** Once M1367 lands, `npx` is part of the guaranteed
runtime stack. The existing `requires_npx` skip in
`tests/live/test_mcp_reference_servers.py:30-32` should become a
hard failure: a missing `npx` is now a regression, not an
environmental quirk. We also lack a functional test that
exercises the full path planner→briefer→worker→MCP for an
npx-based server, validating M1368/M1369/M1370 together.

**Approach.**
- Invert the `requires_npx` gate: in the test image, missing `npx`
  is `pytest.fail`, not `pytest.skip`. Keep the soft skip only
  in the dev-host suite where contributors may run without Node.
- Add a functional test in `tests/functional/` that gives a goal
  like "list the contents of <path> using the MCP filesystem
  server" and asserts the resulting plan uses
  `mcp_call(filesystem:read_directory)` — not `exec ls`. This
  validates that briefer (M1370) + routing (M1368) actually push
  the planner toward MCP when an MCP is available.

**Tasks**:
- [ ] Invert `requires_npx` gate in test image context.
- [ ] Add functional test for filesystem MCP routing.
- [ ] Validator unit test: a goal "install package X globally with
      npm" yields the rewritten plan.
- [ ] Commit & push.

**Done when**:
- `tests/live/test_mcp_reference_servers.py` runs (not skips) in
  the test image.
- The new functional test passes against a real
  `@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem`.

---

### M1372 — OAuth device flow interactive test + credential storage

**Why.** `tests/live/test_mcp_auth_servers.py` covers MCP servers
that use static API keys (Brave, GitHub PAT, Google Maps), but
no test exercises a real **interactive** OAuth flow where a user
must approve consent and the kiso MCP client must store and reuse
the resulting token. The gap matters because: (a) OAuth is the
direction the MCP spec is moving for managed servers (Linear,
Atlassian, GitHub OAuth apps), and (b) we have no idea today
whether `kiso/mcp/stdio.py` or `kiso/mcp/http.py` would handle
a server that requires an auth handshake before its first
`tools/list`.

**Approach.** Pick **GitHub device flow** as the test target —
it's the simplest interactive OAuth: the user is prompted with
a code and a URL, pastes the code in a browser, and the server
polls until token issuance. No local HTTP listener needed, no
browser automation.

- Add a new pytest marker `live_interactive` (or `live_oauth`),
  excluded from `./utils/run_tests.sh a` (automatic suites) and
  invoked only via a new `i` (interactive) suite in
  `utils/run_tests.sh`.
- Add credential storage at `~/.kiso/mcp/credentials/<server>.json`
  with `chmod 0600`, owned by the runtime user. Handler in a new
  `kiso/mcp/credentials.py` module so it is reusable across
  transports.
- Extend `kiso/mcp/stdio.py` and/or `kiso/mcp/http.py` with a
  pre-`tools/list` auth hook that consults the credential store
  and, on miss, runs the device flow (prints code+URL to stderr,
  polls for token, persists). Refresh-token handling is
  out-of-scope for this milestone — token expiry just re-runs
  the flow.
- Add `tests/live/test_mcp_oauth_github.py::test_github_device_flow`
  under the new marker. It is expected to require human action
  during the run; CI never executes it.

**Tasks**:
- [ ] `live_interactive` pytest marker registered.
- [ ] `i` suite in `utils/run_tests.sh`.
- [ ] `kiso/mcp/credentials.py` with file-based store, 0600 perms,
      unit tests.
- [ ] Auth hook in stdio/http transport with branching for
      `auth: device_flow` server config.
- [ ] Interactive test against GitHub device flow.
- [ ] Manual run notes in the test docstring (env vars, expected
      prompt, where the token lands).
- [ ] Commit & push.

**Done when**:
- `./utils/run_tests.sh i tests/live/test_mcp_oauth_github.py`
  prompts the user, accepts a code, persists the token, and
  re-runs without re-prompting on a second invocation.
- Token file exists at the expected path with `0600` permissions.
- Automatic suites are unaffected.
